from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_betweenness
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to a sparse adjacency matrix
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adj_matrix = csgraph_betweenness(distance_matrix, directed=False, return_paths=False)
    heuristics_matrix = adj_matrix.toarray()

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_betweenness
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the matrix into a sparse, undirected graph
    row, col, _ = np.where(np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1) == 1)
    graph = np.zeros((row.size, row.size))
    graph[np.tril_indices(row.size, k=-1)] = graph.T[np.tril_indices(row.size, k=-1)]
    graph[np.tril_indices(row.size, k=-1)] = distance_matrix[np.tril_indices(row.size, k=-1)]

    # Compute betweenness centrality
    betweenness, _ = csgraph_betweenness(csgraph=graph, directed=False)

    # Normalize betweenness scores
    betweenness = np.maximum(betweenness, 0)  # Ensure non-negative scores
    max_betweenness = np.max(betweenness)
    return betweenness / max_betweenness

import numpy as np
from scipy.cluster.hierarchy import linkage, dendrogram
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Perform hierarchical clustering on the distance matrix
    z = linkage(distance_matrix, method='ward')
    
    # Step 2: Create a dendrogram to visualize the clusters
    fig = plt.figure(figsize=(10, 7))
    dn = dendrogram(z, labels=range(distance_matrix.shape[0]), truncate_mode='level', p=3)
    
    # Step 3: Assign cluster labels to each point (vertices)
    cluster_labels = np.array(dn['leaves'])
    
    # Step 4: Calculate the average distance for each cluster
    cluster_centroids = np.array([distance_matrix[cluster_labels == i].mean(axis=0) for i in range(len(np.unique(cluster_labels)))])
    
    # Step 5: Create a new distance matrix where each distance is increased by an edge weight to a cluster centroid
    new_distances = distance_matrix + np.expand_dims(cluster_centroids, axis=0) - np.expand_dims(cluster_centroids, axis=1)
    
    # Step 6: Normalize the new distances (if needed, based on your problem-specific constraints)
    normalized_distances = new_distances / new_distances.max()
    
    # Step 7: Return the normalized distances as the heuristics matrix
    return normalized_distances



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def page_rank(distance_matrix, alpha=0.85, damping_factor=0.85, max_iter=100, tolerance=1e-8):
    """
    Calculate Google PageRank for a given distance matrix.
    Alpha and damping factor are parameters for the PageRank algorithm.
    max_iter is the maximum number of iterations, and tolerance is the convergence criteria.
    """
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    rank = np.ones(n) / n  # Initialize ranks as 1/n for each node
    
    for _ in range(max_iter):
        new_rank = np.zeros(n)
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if distance_matrix[i, j] > 0:  # Only consider edges with non-zero distance
                    new_rank[i] += (1 - damping_factor) * (distance_matrix[i, j] / np.sum(distance_matrix)) * rank[j]
        # Normalize ranks
        new_rank /= np.sum(new_rank)
        
        # Convergence check
        if np.linalg.norm(new_rank - rank) < tolerance:
            break
        
        rank = new_rank
    
    return rank



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def potential_function(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    potential_scores = np.ones(distance_matrix.shape)  # Initialize all scores to 1

    # Calculate the potential function based on the distance matrix
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            potential_scores[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]
            potential_scores[j, i] = distance_matrix[i, j]  # Since distance_matrix is symmetric

    # Normalize potential scores to be between 0 and 1
    potential_scores /= np.sum(distance_matrix)

    # Consider diagonal elements as 0 since they don't represent actual distances
    potential_scores[np.diag_indices(n)] = 0

    return potential_scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, future_cost_matrix, alpha=0.5, beta=0.5):
    """
    This function calculates edge heuristics based on the weighted sum of the physical distance
    and an estimate of future costs.

    :param distance_matrix: numpy array of shape (n, n), where n is the number of nodes.
    :param future_cost_matrix: numpy array of shape (n, n), where n is the number of nodes.
    :param alpha: A hyperparameter (0 <= alpha <= 1) to balance the influence of distance vs. future cost.
    :param beta: A hyperparameter (0 <= beta <= 1) to balance the influence of future cost.

    :return: numpy array of shape (n, n), where each element represents the heuristic score of including an edge.
    """
    n = len(distance_matrix)

    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with zeros
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)

    # Iterate over each node (except the last one)
    for i in range(n - 1):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            # Calculate the weighted sum
            heuristics_matrix[i, j] = (alpha * distance_matrix[i, j] + beta * future_cost_matrix[i, j])
            # Symmetrically, add the transpose case
            heuristics_matrix[j, i] = heuristics_matrix[i, j]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_weights, edge_types, network_connectivity):
    """
    heuristics function.

    Args:
    distance_matrix (numpy.ndarray): The adjacency matrix of the graph, where each element represents the distance between nodes.
    edge_weights (numpy.ndarray): The weight of each edge. Weights can represent capacity, cost, etc.
    edge_types (numpy.ndarray): The type of each edge. This could be road, railway, air, etc.
    network_connectivity (numpy.ndarray): A matrix representing network connectivity, indicating how interconnected nodes are.

    Returns:
    numpy.ndarray: A matrix of the same shape as the input, with each element representing the undesirability score of including the corresponding edge in a solution.
    """

    # Define weights for each factor
    distance_weight = 0.4  # Higher value for shorter distances, higher edge weights, and higher network connectivity
    edge_weight_weight = 0.3  # Higher value for heavier edges, higher edge types cost
    edge_type_weight = 0.2  # Higher value for less beneficial edge types
    connectivity_weight = 0.1  # Higher value for less connected networks

    # Calculate the score for each edge
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    scores = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Distance-based score
            distance_score = distance_weight * distance_matrix[i, j]
            
            # Edge weight-based score
            if edge_weights is not None:
                edge_weight_score = edge_weight_weight * edge_weights[i, j]
            else:
                edge_weight_score = 0
                
            # Edge type-based score
            if edge_types is not None:
                edge_type_score = edge_type_weight * edge_types[i, j]
            else:
                edge_type_score = 0
                
            # Network connectivity-based score
            connectivity_score = connectivity_weight * network_connectivity[i, j]
            
            # Total score
            total_score = distance_score + edge_weight_score + edge_type_score + connectivity_score
            scores[i, j] = total_score

    return scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    row_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)  # Row-wise sum of distances
    col_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)  # Column-wise sum of distances
    
    # Replace zero distances with a large value to differentiate them
    distance_matrix[distance_matrix == 0] = np.inf
    
    # Create a frequency matrix where each element represents the count of a specific distance
    frequency_matrix = np.zeros((num_nodes, num_nodes))
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if distance_matrix[i][j]!= np.inf:
                frequency_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
                frequency_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[j][i]
    
    # Calculate the heuristic score for each edge
    heuristic_scores = np.where(distance_matrix!= np.inf,
                                 row_sums + col_sums + frequency_matrix[distance_matrix!= np.inf],
                                 np.inf)  # Use infinite for non-existent distances
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # We're not considering Steiner points yet, as they weren't explicitly provided
    # Calculate the simple TSP heuristic (Sum of closest pairwise distances)
    heuristics_matrix = np.sum(np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis] + np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)[np.newaxis, :])
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_ shortest_paths
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adj_matrix = np.ones((n, n), dtype=bool)  # Initialize adjacency matrix
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j]!= 0:  # Edge exists
                adj_matrix[i, j] = True
                adj_matrix[j, i] = True

    # Compute betweenness centrality
    betweenness_centrality = csgraph_shortest_paths.betweenness_centrality(
        csgraph=adj_matrix,
        return_distances=False,
        return_predecessors=False
    )

    # Normalize betweenness centrality between 0 and 1
    max_betweenness = max(betweenness_centrality.values())
    normalized_betweenness = {node: bc / max_betweenness for node, bc in betweenness_centrality.items()}

    # Create the heuristic matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j]!= 0:  # Edge exists
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = normalized_betweenness[i] * normalized_betweenness[j]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Weights for edges. Shorter distances get higher weight.
    edge_weights = np.exp(-distance_matrix / 100)  # Decay factor to give less weight for longer distances

    # Assuming the matrix is symmetric (i.e., the same distance from A to B as from B to A)
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Self-loops are not typically desirable, so their weights are set to 0
    diagonal = np.full((n, n), 0)
    edge_weights = np.where(np.triu(np.ones((n, n))), edge_weights, diagonal)

    return edge_weights



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_weights):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # D^2 heuristic
    squared_distances = np.square(distance_matrix)
    d_squared = squared_distances.sum(axis=1)
    
    # Weighted D^2 for each edge
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i + 1, num_nodes):
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = heuristic_matrix[j, i] = d_squared[i] + d_squared[j] * edge_weights[i][j]
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the average distance to neighboring vertices for each vertex
    neighbor_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix[np.nonzero(distance_matrix)], axis=1)
    
    # Create a new matrix with the same shape as the input
    result_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Assign a higher value for more densely connected vertices
    result_matrix += distance_matrix  # Raw distance as initial contribution
    result_matrix += 100 * (neighbor_distances - np.min(neighbor_distances))  # Higher value for more connected vertices
    result_matrix -= np.max(result_matrix)  # Normalize values to between 0 and 1

    return result_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    neighborhood_scores = []

    # Calculate neighborhood score for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:  # Ignore the diagonal (self-distance)
                score = 0
                for k in range(n):
                    if k!= i and k!= j:  # Ignore self and duplicate edges
                        score += distance_matrix[i][k]
                neighborhood_scores.append(score)

    # Create a matrix of the same shape with the neighborhood scores
    heuristic_matrix = np.array(neighborhood_scores).reshape(n, n)
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def prim_mst_cost(distance_matrix, start_node):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    visited = set()
    heap = [(0, start_node)]  # (cost, node)
    total_cost = 0
    while heap:
        cost, current = heapq.heappop(heap)
        if current not in visited:
            visited.add(current)
            total_cost += cost
            for neighbor, edge_cost in enumerate(distance_matrix[current]):
                if neighbor not in visited and edge_cost!= float('inf'):  # assuming graph is undirected and no infinite cost edges
                    heapq.heappush(heap, (edge_cost, neighbor))
    return total_cost



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def floyd_warshall(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    for k in range(num_nodes):
        for i in range(num_nodes):
            for j in range(num_nodes):
                distance_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    return distance_matrix



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Ensure the matrix is square
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    if n!= distance_matrix.shape[1]:
        raise ValueError("Input matrix should be square.")

    # Calculate the heuristic score
    heuristic_scores = np.zeros((n, n))

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                # Neighbors count
                neighbor_count = np.sum(distance_matrix[i] < distance_matrix[j])
                
                # Weight based on inverse distance to neighbors
                weight = 1 / (distance_matrix[j] + 1)

                # Combine with absolute distance
                heuristic_scores[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] + neighbor_count * weight

    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Diagonal Dominance
    dominance = np.diag(distance_matrix) - np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0) - np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix + dominance
    
    # Average Distance
    avg_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    avg_distances = avg_distances.reshape(-1, 1)
    heuristics_matrix = heuristics_matrix + avg_distances.T
    
    # Entropy (assuming distances are uniformly distributed between 0 and 1)
    # Note: This step is highly theoretical and might need to be adjusted based on the actual range of distances
    entropy = -np.sum(np.bincount(distance_matrix.ravel(), minlength=100) * np.log2(np.bincount(distance_matrix.ravel(), minlength=100))) / np.log2(100)
    heuristics_matrix = heuristics_matrix + entropy
    
    # Density
    density = distance_matrix.sum() / (distance_matrix.size * (distance_matrix.size - 1))
    heuristics_matrix = heuristics_matrix + density * 100  # Adjust the weight based on your specific needs
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, obstruction_matrix):
    """
    Computes a heuristic score for each edge in the distance_matrix.
    This function incorporates both the immediate distance and an
    additional obstruction_factor for each edge.

    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (numpy.ndarray): A square matrix where distance_matrix[i, j]
                                     is the distance between nodes i and j.
    obstruction_matrix (numpy.ndarray): A square matrix where obstruction_matrix[i, j]
                                       represents the estimated cost of traversing
                                       the edge from node i to j.

    Returns:
    numpy.ndarray: A matrix of the same shape as distance_matrix, containing
                    the heuristic score for each edge.
    """
    # Ensure matrices are of the same shape
    if distance_matrix.shape!= obstruction_matrix.shape:
        raise ValueError("distance_matrix and obstruction_matrix must be of the same shape")

    # Initialize heuristic matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)

    # Apply obstruction factor
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] += obstruction_matrix[i, j]

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize the priority queue and MST edge set
    queue = [(0, 0)]  # (cost, node)
    parent = [None] * n
    mst_edges = []

    while queue:
        cost, u = heapq.heappop(queue)

        # Skip if this vertex has already been included in MST
        if parent[u] is not None:
            continue

        # Add to MST
        mst_edges.append((u, min(queue, key=lambda x: x[0])[1]))

        # Process neighbors
        for v, edge_cost in enumerate(distance_matrix[u]):
            if edge_cost > cost and v not in parent:
                heapq.heappush(queue, (edge_cost, v))
                parent[v] = u

    # Convert MST edges to a matrix for easier handling
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for u, v in mst_edges:
        heuristic_matrix[u][v] = 1
        heuristic_matrix[v][u] = 1  # for undirected graph, symmetry

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize heuristic values
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()

    # Apply the new heuristic formula
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if i!= j and k!= i and k!= j:
                    # The new heuristic considers the impact of future edges
                    # on current edge's undesirability.
                    heuristics_matrix[i][j] = max(
                        distance_matrix[i][j], 
                        heuristics_matrix[i][k] + heuristics_matrix[k][j]
                    )

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def mst_heuristic(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    parent = list(range(n))
    rank = [0] * n
    edges = []

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            edges.append((distance_matrix[i][j], i, j))

    heapq.heapify(edges)

    while edges:
        cost, u, v = heapq.heappop(edges)
        if find(parent, u)!= find(parent, v):
            union(parent, u, v)

    # Assign cost to each edge based on the MST
    mst_cost = 0
    for edge in edges:
        u, v = edge
        if find(parent, u)!= find(parent, v):
            mst_cost += distance_matrix[u][v]

    # Scale cost to original range
    max_cost = max(distance_matrix.diagonal())
    heuristics = [c / max_cost for c in mst_cost]

    return heuristics



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Calculate the adjacency matrix from distance matrix
    adj_matrix = np.abs(distance_matrix - np.diag(np.diag(distance_matrix)))
    
    # Compute the minimum dominating set for each node
    dominating_sets = []
    for i in range(adj_matrix.shape[0]):
        # Compute the neighbors of node i
        neighbors = np.where(adj_matrix[i]!= 0)[0]
        # Compute the dominating set of node i
        dominating_set = set(neighbors)
        # Add the nodes that are not dominated by any other node in the set
        for j in neighbors:
            if not any(adj_matrix[j][k] for k in dominating_set):
                dominating_set.add(j)
        dominating_sets.append(dominating_set)
    
    # Construct the heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros(adj_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(adj_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in dominating_sets[i]:
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = 1 / adj_matrix[i][j]
        for k in dominating_sets[i]:
            heuristics_matrix[j][k] = 1 / adj_matrix[k][j]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Manhattan distance heuristic
    def manhattan_dist(node1, node2):
        return np.abs(node1[0] - node2[0]) + np.abs(node1[1] - node2[1])

    n_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same size as the input
    heuristic_matrix = np.full_like(distance_matrix, np.inf)

    # Calculate and populate the heuristic matrix
    for i in range(n_nodes):
        for j in range(n_nodes):
            if i!= j:
                # Manhattan distance heuristic
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] + manhattan_dist(i, j)

    # Normalize the heuristic matrix by dividing each element by the maximum heuristic value
    max_heuristic = np.max(heuristic_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix /= max_heuristic

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    # Step 1: Select initial node with minimum adjacent edges
    initial_node = min(range(num_nodes), key=lambda i: len(distance_matrix[i]))
    
    # Step 2: Initialize visited nodes set
    visited = [False] * num_nodes
    visited[initial_node] = True
    
    # Step 3: Initialize the cost and path
    cost = 0
    path = [initial_node]
    
    while len(path) < num_nodes:
        # Step 4: Find unvisited neighbor with the smallest new cost
        new_costs = [distance_matrix[path[-1]][i] for i in range(num_nodes) if not visited[i]]
        new_cost_indices = [i for i, cost in enumerate(new_costs) if cost < distance_matrix[path[-1]][initial_node]]
        new_cost = min(new_costs[i] for i in new_cost_indices)
        
        # Step 5: Update potential new path and cost
        potential_new_path = []
        for i in range(num_nodes):
            if not visited[i] and distance_matrix[path[-1]][i] == new_cost:
                potential_new_path.append(i)
        
        if potential_new_path:
            new_node = potential_new_path[0]
            cost += new_cost
            path.append(new_node)
            visited[new_node] = True
        else:
            break
    
    # Step 6: Modify edge weights
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:
                current_cost = cost
                removed_cost = (distance_matrix[i][path[-1]] + distance_matrix[path[-1]][j]) - distance_matrix[i][j]
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] = current_cost + removed_cost
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def betweenness_centrality(graph):
    # Graph representation can be adjacency matrix or adjacency list
    # For simplicity, let's assume we have an adjacency matrix 'graph'
    n = graph.shape[0]
    betweenness = np.zeros((n, n))
    
    for node in range(n):
        # Compute shortest paths between all pairs of nodes
        paths = _dijkstra(graph, node)
        
        # Number of shortest paths that pass through node 'node'
        num_paths = np.sum(paths[:, node] > 0)
        
        # Betweenness for node 'node'
        for i in range(n):
            if i!= node:
                betweenness[i, node] = np.sum(paths[node, i] > 0) / num_paths
                betweenness[node, i] = betweenness[i, node]
    
    return betweenness



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Calculate the degree of each node (vertex) in the graph
    node_degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Return a heuristic matrix where each element is the minimum of the corresponding row
    # This represents the number of edges that need to be added to make that node the most connected
    # higher value implies greater undesirability
    return np.minimum.reduce([distance_matrix + np.eye(distance_matrix.shape[0])])



# Score: -20000

def weighted_distance_heuristics(distance_matrix, weights=1):
    """
    This function calculates a heuristic score for each edge in a distance matrix.
    Edges with smaller distances get higher weights, encouraging their inclusion.
    
    Args:
    distance_matrix (list of list): A 2D list representing the distance between each pair of nodes.
    weights (float): The weight factor to apply to the distance (default is 1).
                      Higher weights give more importance to shorter edges.
    
    Returns:
    list of list: A 2D list with the same shape as the input, where each element is the weighted distance.
    """
    heuristic_matrix = [[distance * weights for distance in distance_row] for distance_row in distance_matrix]
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    betweenness = nx.edge_betweenness_centrality(G, weight='weight') # Assuming 'weight' column in distance_matrix

    # Convert dictionary to numpy array for consistent dimensions
    betweenness_matrix = np.array(list(betweenness.values())).reshape(distance_matrix.shape)

    return betweenness_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def weighted_connectivity_density(distance_matrix):
    m, n = distance_matrix.shape
    # Calculate the number of connections for each node
    num_connections = np.sum(distance_matrix!= 0, axis=1)
    
    # Calculate the density (average distance between connected nodes)
    avg_dist_connected = np.zeros(m)
    for i in range(m):
        # Exclude the node from its own connections for calculating average distance
        mask = (distance_matrix[i]!= 0) & (distance_matrix[:, i]!= 0)
        avg_dist_connected[i] = np.mean(distance_matrix[mask]) if np.sum(mask) > 0 else 0

    # Compute the weighted heuristic for each edge
    heuristic_matrix = num_connections[:, None] - avg_dist_connected[None, :]

    # Take the absolute value and flip the sign for lower is better
    heuristic_matrix = np.abs(heuristic_matrix).T  # Transpose for consistency with distance matrix shape
    heuristic_matrix *= -1  # Flip the sign

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Assuming the input distance matrix is a square matrix where each element represents a Euclidean distance
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the Hamming distance for each pair of vertices
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            diff = np.abs(distance_matrix[i] - distance_matrix[j]) - 1
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = heuristic_matrix[j, i] = diff
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize MST with a single node
    mst = {i: distance_matrix[0][i] for i in range(1, n)}
    mst_edges = [(0, 1)]  # Start with the first edge
    min_heap = [(distance_matrix[0][1], 0, 1)]  # Heap to store (weight, node, neighbor)

    # Prim's Algorithm to construct MST
    while min_heap:
        weight, current, neighbor = heapq.heappop(min_heap)
        
        # Ignore edges if their node has already been included in MST
        if neighbor in mst:
            continue

        mst[neighbor] = weight
        mst_edges.append((min_heap[0][0], current, neighbor))

        # Update potential edges
        for i, j in distance_matrix[current]:
            if i not in mst and j not in mst:
                heapq.heappush(min_heap, (distance_matrix[current][i], current, i))

    # Calculate heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = [[min(mst[j], distance_matrix[i][j]) for j in range(n)] for i in range(n)]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the average distance as a simple local measure
    avg_distance = np.mean(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate the number of edges to consider as a global measure
    num_edges = distance_matrix.size // 2  # Assuming square matrix
    edge_density = num_edges / (distance_matrix.shape[0] * (distance_matrix.shape[0] - 1) // 2)

    # Calculate the shortest path matrix to identify potential reductions
    shortest_path_matrix = _compute_shortest_paths(distance_matrix)
    
    # Assign heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(i+1, distance_matrix.shape[0]):
            # Edge weight
            weight = distance_matrix[i, j]

            # Local: higher average distance and edge density imply greater undesirability
            local_score = avg_distance + edge_density
            
            # Global: short path suggests potential for future reduction
            shortest_path = shortest_path_matrix[i, j]
            if shortest_path > weight:
                global_score = weight - shortest_path
            
            # Combine local and global scores
            heuristics_matrix[i, j] = local_score + global_score

            # Symmetry: no-op for edges where i > j, as it's already accounted for
            heuristics_matrix[j, i] = heuristics_matrix[i, j]
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate global heuristic: sum of diagonal elements (for isolated nodes)
    global_heuristic = np.trace(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate local heuristic: sum of off-diagonal elements (for interconnected nodes)
    local_heuristic = np.sum(distance_matrix) - global_heuristic
    
    # Adjust for matrix size (larger matrices might be more complex to connect)
    size_adjustment = 1 / np.sqrt(distance_matrix.size)
    
    # Combine heuristics with weighting factors
    heuristics_matrix = (1 - size_adjustment) * global_heuristic + size_adjustment * local_heuristic
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, feature_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of distances for each node
    node_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate the feature similarity between each pair of nodes
    similarity = np.dot(feature_matrix, feature_matrix.T)
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate edge importance
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # If the nodes have similar features, the edge's importance is based on distance
            if similarity[i, j] > 0.5:  # Adjust threshold as needed
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]
            else:
                # If the nodes have dissimilar features, the edge's importance is based on the average distance of both nodes to their neighbors
                avg_distance = np.mean(node_sums[np.where(distance_matrix[np.arange(distance_matrix.shape[0]), :] > 0)[0]!= j])
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = avg_distance + distance_matrix[i, j]
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import pairwise_distances
from sklearn.neighbors import NearestNeighbors
def heuristics_innovative(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # 1. Inverse Distance
    inverse_distances = 1 / distance_matrix

    # 2. Density
    # First, we estimate the local density using radius=2
    nn = NearestNeighbors(n_neighbors=2, metric='precomputed').fit(squareform(distance_matrix))
    radii, indices = nn.kneighbors(distance_matrix)
    local_densities = radii / distance_matrix[indices[:, 1]]

    # We assume higher densities are penalized
    density_factor = np.mean(local_densities)
    density_penalty = inverse_distances * (density_factor - 1)

    # 3. Clustering Coefficient
    # Estimate clustering coefficient using Louvain method (requires community detection)
    communities = [community.find(i) for i, community in enumerate(pairwise_distances(distance_matrix).argsort()[:, 1])]
    cc_values = [community.cc() for community in communities]

    # We assume higher clustering coefficents are further penalized
    clustering_penalty = inverse_distances * (np.max(cc_values) - np.mean(cc_values))

    # Combine all penalties
    final_heuristics = inverse_distances + density_penalty + clustering_penalty

    return final_heuristics

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the total number of edges
    num_edges = distance_matrix.shape[0] * distance_matrix.shape[1] // 2
    
    # Sum the distances of all nodes
    total_distances = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Compute the average distance for each node
    avg_distances = total_distances / distance_matrix.shape[1]
    
    # Compute the heuristic score for each edge
    heuristic_scores = np.outer(avg_distances, avg_distances)
    
    # Adjust for overcounting (diagonal elements are double-counted)
    heuristic_scores[np.arange(num_edges), np.arange(num_edges)] *= 0.5
    
    return heuristic_scores

import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Dijkstra's algorithm to calculate tentative distances
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    tentative_distances = [float('inf')] * n
    tentative_distances[0] = 0
    priority_queue = [(0, 0)]  # (distance, node)
    
    while priority_queue:
        current_distance, current_node = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)
        
        # If we have found a shorter path to current node, update
        if current_distance > tentative_distances[current_node]:
            continue
        
        for neighbor, edge_weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_node]):
            if edge_weight > 0 and tentative_distances[neighbor] > current_distance + edge_weight:
                tentative_distances[neighbor] = current_distance + edge_weight
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (tentative_distances[neighbor], neighbor))
    
    # Step 2: Heuristics scoring
    heuristic_matrix = [0] * n
    centrality = [sum(distance_matrix[i]) for i in range(n)]
    max_centrality = max(centrality)
    
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i][j] > 0:
                heuristic_matrix[i] += 1 / (centrality[i] * centrality[j])
                heuristic_matrix[j] += 1 / (centrality[i] * centrality[j])

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, weight_matrix, population_map):
    """
    distance_matrix: A 2D matrix of pairwise distances.
    weight_matrix: A 2D matrix indicating edge weights, typically inverse of distance.
    population_map: A 2D matrix indicating population density at each node.
    """
    
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))

    # Direct Distance Heuristic
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristics_matrix[i, j] += distance_matrix[i, j]
            # Add a small factor to account for inverse distance
            heuristics_matrix[i, j] *= weight_matrix[i, j]

    # Indirect Costs (Nearest Neighbor)
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if i!= j and distance_matrix[i, j] < np.inf:
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] += distance_matrix[k, i] + distance_matrix[k, j]
                    # Apply weights based on the edge's position on the shortest path
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] *= (1 / min(distance_matrix[k, i], distance_matrix[k, j]))

    # Connectivity Score
    connectivity_scores = np.zeros(n)
    for i in range(n):
        connectivity_scores[i] = np.mean(population_map[i])  # Simple average population of all neighboring nodes

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] += connectivity_scores[i] + connectivity_scores[j]
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] *= 0.5  # Adjust factor for weighted connectivity

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    row_sums = sum(distance_matrix, [])
    col_sums = [sum(row) for row in distance_matrix]
    
    # Compute Manhattan Distance
    manhattan_distance = [row_sums[i] + col_sums[i] - 2*distance_matrix[i][i] for i in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    
    return manhattan_distance



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the number of nodes
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize a new distance matrix with the same shape
    heuristics_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

    # Calculate the maximum distance from the current node to any other node
    max_distance = max(distance_matrix[i][j] for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n))

    # Assign the maximum distance to all diagonal elements (self-loops)
    for i in range(n):
        heuristics_matrix[i][i] = max_distance

    # Assign a weight based on how close the node is to reaching the maximum distance
    # A node that is closer to the maximum distance is considered more important
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i == j:
                continue
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
            if distance_matrix[i][j] < max_distance:
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] += max_distance - distance_matrix[i][j]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of each row (a rough measure of centrality)
    row_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Calculate the distance to the furthest neighbor for each node
    max_dist = np.max(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Create a weighted sum of the two components
    heuristics_matrix = row_sums + max_dist / 2.0  # Scale max_dist by 2 to give it equal weight to row_sums
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_betweenness_centrality
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance matrix to a sparse, undirected graph
    graph = csgraph_betweennesscentrality(distance_matrix)
    
    # Create a heuristic matrix where each cell represents the betweenness centrality of the corresponding edge
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Assign betweenness centrality scores to each edge
    for u, v, w in zip(np.argwhere(graph['matrix'] > 0):
        heuristics_matrix[u, v] = graph['betweenness'][u, v]
        heuristics_matrix[v, u] = heuristics_matrix[u, v]  # Since distance matrix is symmetric
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_from_adjmatrix
def betweenness_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to adjacency matrix
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adj_matrix = np.abs(distance_matrix - np.diag(np.diag(distance_matrix)))

    # Compute the betweenness centrality
    betweenness_centrality = np.zeros(adj_matrix.shape)
    betweenness_centrality_csgraph = csgraph_from_adjmatrix(adj_matrix)
    betweenness_centrality, _ = csgraph_betweenness(betweenness_centrality_csgraph)

    # Normalize betweenness centrality values to range between 0 and 1
    betweenness_centrality = (betweenness_centrality - betweenness_centrality.min()) / (betweenness_centrality.max() - betweenness_centrality.min())

    # Ensure the output shape matches the input
    assert betweenness_centrality.shape == distance_matrix.shape, "Input and output matrices should have the same shape."

    return betweenness_centrality

def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree

    # Convert the distance matrix to a sparse, adjacency matrix
    adj_matrix = csgraph.create_adjacency_matrix(distance_matrix)

    # Compute the Minimum Spanning Tree
    mst = minimum_spanning_tree(adj_matrix, connectivity=0)

    # Create a heuristic matrix with higher values for less important edges
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for edge in zip(np.where(mst == 1)[0], np.where(mst == 1)[1]):
        dist = distance_matrix[edge[0]][edge[1]]
        heuristic_matrix[edge[0]][edge[1]] = dist * 2  # Multiplied by 2 for a higher value

    # Set the diagonal elements to a higher value for all nodes
    np.fill_diagonal(heuristic_matrix, np.inf)
    
    return heuristic_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the adjacency matrix from the distance matrix
    adjacency_matrix = np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1)
    adjacency_matrix[adjacency_matrix < 0] = 0

    # Compute the shortest-path matrix using the adjacency matrix
    shortest_paths = csgraph_from_dense(adjacency_matrix, directed=True).minimize(distance_matrix)

    # Compute degree and betweenness centrality
    n = adjacency_matrix.shape[0]
    degrees = np.sum(adjacency_matrix, axis=0)
    betweenness_centrality = np.zeros((n, n))

    for _ in range(2):
        centrality = _betweenness_centrality(adjacency_matrix, n)
        betweenness_centrality += centrality

    # Normalize centrality scores between 0 and 1
    total_centrality = np.sum(betweenness_centrality)
    betweenness_centrality = betweenness_centrality / total_centrality

    # The heuristic value for each edge is the product of its weight and inverse centrality
    heuristic_matrix = np.multiply(distance_matrix, 1 / betweenness_centrality)
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_vertices = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the priority queue (min-heap) and visited list
    priority_queue = [(0, 0)]  # (weight, vertex)
    visited = [False] * num_vertices
    # List to store the heuristic values (undesirability scores)
    heuristics_scores = [[0] * num_vertices for _ in range(num_vertices)]
    
    # Iterate over each vertex
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        # Add the vertex to the priority queue and mark it as visited
        heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (distance_matrix[i][i], i))
        visited[i] = True
        
        # Iterate over the unvisited vertices
        while priority_queue and visited[i]:
            # Pop the vertex with the smallest edge weight
            weight, j = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)
            # If j is already visited, skip it
            if not visited[j]:
                # Update the heuristic score for all unvisited neighbors
                for k in range(num_vertices):
                    if not visited[k]:
                        heuristics_scores[i][k] = max(heuristics_scores[i][k], distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[j][k])
                # Add the unvisited neighbor to the priority queue
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (distance_matrix[i][j], j))
    
    return heuristics_scores

import numpy as np
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the input is a square matrix
    assert np.allclose(distance_matrix, distance_matrix.T), "Input is not a square matrix."
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Create a graph from the distance matrix
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate betweenness centrality
    betweenness = nx.betweenness_centrality(G, normalized=False)
    
    # Convert the centrality values to a matrix
    result = np.array([[betweenness[i][j] for j in range(n)] for i in range(n)])
    
    return result

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure input is a square numpy array
    assert np.allclose(distance_matrix, np.transpose(distance_matrix)), "Input must be a square matrix"

    # Number of nodes
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with zeros
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Apply Floyd-Warshall algorithm to generate heuristic scores
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                # Consider adding edge (i,j) with intermediate node k
                heuristics_matrix[i,j] = max(
                    heuristics_matrix[i,j], 
                    distance_matrix[i,k] + distance_matrix[k,j]
                )
    
    # Handle diagonal elements as they represent direct paths
    np.fill_diagonal(heuristics_matrix, np.inf)
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.linalg import eigs
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Create the adjacency matrix from distance matrix
    adj_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                adj_matrix[i, j] = 1 - distance_matrix[i, j] # Assuming 0 as connection
    # Calculate the eigenvectors of the adjacency matrix
    eigenvalues, eigenvectors = eigs(adj_matrix, k=1)
    # Compute centrality scores
    centrality_scores = np.abs(eigenvectors) / np.sum(eigenvectors)
    # Normalize scores to sum to 1
    centrality_scores /= np.sum(centrality_scores)
    
    # Return a matrix of undesirability scores
    return np.array([1 - centrality_scores[i, j] for i in range(n) for j in range(n)])



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def psp_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Convert distance matrix to graph
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    graph = np.zeros((num_nodes, num_nodes))
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:
                graph[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
    
    # Step 2: Compute PSPs
    def psp(node, graph):
        short_paths = []
        for other_node in range(num_nodes):
            if other_node!= node:
                path_length = float('inf')
                path = []
                while other_node!= node:
                    other_node = min((n for n in range(num_nodes) if n!= node and graph[node][n]!= float('inf')), key=lambda x: graph[node][x])
                    path.append(other_node)
                    path_length = min(path_length, graph[node][other_node])
                    node = other_node
                path.append(node)
                path.reverse()
                short_paths.append((path, path_length))
        return short_paths

    psp_values = psp(0, graph)
    
    # Step 3: Calculate new heuristic score for each edge
    heuristic_scores = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_scores[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] + min([psp_value[1] for psp_value in psp_values[i] if j in psp_value[0]])
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000

def wdh_heuristics(distance_matrix, weights=None):
    """
    Calculate a heuristic score for each entry in the distance_matrix based on weighted distances.
    
    Args:
    - distance_matrix (list of list): A 2D list representing the distance matrix.
    - weights (list, optional): A list of weights corresponding to each row in the distance matrix.
                                If not provided, all weights are assumed to be equal.
    
    Returns:
    - list of list: A 2D list with the same shape as distance_matrix, containing the WDH scores.
    """
    if weights is None:
        # Assuming all weights are equal
        weights = [1 for _ in range(len(distance_matrix))]

    num_rows, num_cols = len(distance_matrix), len(distance_matrix[0])
    wdh_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(num_cols)] for _ in range(num_rows)]

    # Calculate the weighted distance for each entry
    for i in range(num_rows):
        for j in range(num_cols):
            wdh_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] * weights[i]

    return wdh_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, depot_index, demands, service_centers):
    num_nodes, num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape
    heuristics_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)

    # Add distance to each service center
    for service_center in service_centers:
        heuristics_matrix[depot_index, service_center] = 0
        heuristics_matrix[service_center, depot_index] = 0
        heuristics_matrix[service_center, :] += service_center
        heuristics_matrix[:, service_center] += service_center

    # Incorporate traveling salesman effect
    for node in range(num_nodes):
        heuristics_matrix[node, :] += heuristics_matrix[:, node] - distance_matrix[node, :]
        heuristics_matrix[:, node] += heuristics_matrix[node, :] - distance_matrix[node, :]

    # Balance demands
    node_demands = np.array(demands)
    heuristics_matrix[:, -1] = node_demands
    heuristics_matrix[-1, :] = node_demands

    # Add a random penalty to ensure diversity in solutions
    np.random.seed(42)
    heuristics_matrix += np.random.uniform(0, 10, (num_nodes, num_nodes))

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize distances to all vertices as infinite, except the source vertex which is 0
    dist = [float('inf')] * n
    dist[0] = 0
    
    # Dijkstra's algorithm to find shortest paths
    for _ in range(n-1):
        u = min(range(n), key=lambda i: dist[i])
        dist[u] = float('inf')
        for v, w in enumerate(distance_matrix[u]):
            if dist[u] + w < dist[v]:
                dist[v] = dist[u] + w
    
    # The heuristics matrix is the negative of the shortest path from each vertex
    heuristics_matrix = [-d for d in dist]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the adjacency matrix from the distance matrix
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adj_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            adj_matrix[i, j] = adj_matrix[j, i] = distance_matrix[i, j]
            
    # Calculate the degree of each node
    degrees = np.sum(adj_matrix, axis=1)

    # Compute edge density as a heuristic score
    score = 1 - np.minimum(degrees, 1) / n

    return score



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate Manhattan Distance
    manhattan_distances = np.sum(np.abs(distance_matrix), axis=0)
    
    # Max possible distance in a matrix (sum of all distances)
    max_distance = np.sum(distance_matrix)
    
    # Undesirability score for each edge (row)
    undesirability_scores = max_distance - manhattan_distances
    
    # Ensure the score is always non-negative
    undesirability_scores = np.maximum(undesirability_scores, 0)
    
    return undesirability_scores

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    avg_distance = np.mean(np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=0))
    
    # Calculate the impact for each edge
    impact = distance_matrix - avg_distance[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Scale the impact by the average density
    # Here, we calculate the density by dividing the sum of squares of all distances by the number of nodes
    density = (np.sum(distance_matrix**2)) / (num_nodes * (num_nodes - 1))
    impact_scaled = impact * density
    
    return impact_scaled



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Initializing the graph with an infinite cost for all nodes
    graph = {node: {node: float('inf') for node in graph} for node in range(len(distance_matrix))}
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(len(distance_matrix)):
            if i!= j:
                graph[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
    
    # Setting the cost of a node to itself to be zero
    for i in range(len(graph)):
        graph[i][i] = 0
    
    # Dijkstra's algorithm to find the shortest paths
    paths = {node: float('inf') for node in graph}
    paths[0] = 0
    priority_queue = [(0, 0)]  # (current_cost, current_node)
    
    while priority_queue:
        current_cost, current_node = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)
        
        # Skip if we've found a better path to the current node
        if current_cost > paths[current_node]:
            continue
        
        # Update the shortest path costs for neighboring nodes
        for neighbor, weight in graph[current_node].items():
            new_cost = current_cost + weight
            if new_cost < paths[neighbor]:
                paths[neighbor] = new_cost
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (new_cost, neighbor))
    
    # Create a heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [[paths[i] + graph[i][j] for j in range(len(distance_matrix))] for i in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the sum of diagonal elements (self-distances)
    diag_sum = np.diag(distance_matrix)
    
    # Compute the total edge weight
    total_weight = np.sum(distance_matrix)
    
    # Compute the minimum distance (between non-diagonal elements)
    min_distance = np.min(distance_matrix[distance_matrix > 0])
    
    # Compute a connectivity score by subtracting the self-distance from the total edge weight
    connectivity_score = total_weight - diag_sum
    
    # Compute a distance-weight score by dividing the total edge weight by the minimum distance
    distance_weight_score = total_weight / min_distance
    
    # Combine scores using a simple weighted average (adjusting the weights as needed for desired balance)
    heuristic_scores = 0.6 * connectivity_score + 0.4 * distance_weight_score
    
    # Return a matrix with the same shape as the input, filled with the calculated scores
    return heuristic_scores

import numpy as np
from scipy.optimize import linear_sum_assignment
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the matrix into a format suitable for scipy's linear_sum_assignment
    dist_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix)

    # Apply the Hungarian Algorithm
    row_ind, col_ind = linear_sum_assignment(dist_matrix)

    # Create a new matrix to store the heuristic scores
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Fill the heuristic matrix based on the assignments
    heuristic_matrix[row_ind, col_ind] = dist_matrix[row_ind, col_ind]
    heuristic_matrix = np.minimum.accumulate(heuristic_matrix, axis=0)[np.newaxis, :]
    heuristic_matrix = np.minimum.accumulate(heuristic_matrix, axis=1)[np.newaxis, :]

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Reciprocity: For every edge (i, j) in the matrix, add the weight of (j, i)
    reciprocity_score = distance_matrix / distance_matrix
    
    # Minimum Weight Spanning Tree (MWST) heuristic
    def min_weight_spanning_tree(adj_matrix):
        n = len(adj_matrix)
        parent = list(range(n))
        rank = [0] * n
        
        def find(x):
            if parent[x]!= x:
                parent[x] = find(parent[x])
            return parent[x]

        def union(x, y):
            root_x = find(x)
            root_y = find(y)
            if root_x == root_y:
                return
            if rank[root_x] > rank[root_y]:
                parent[root_y] = root_x
            else:
                parent[root_x] = root_y
                if rank[root_x] == rank[root_y]:
                    rank[root_y] += 1
        
        for edge in enumerate(adj_matrix):
            if edge[1] not in parent[edge[0]]:
                union(*edge)
        
        return adj_matrix[edge[0]][edge[1]] for edge in enumerate(adj_matrix) if find(edge[0])!= find(edge[1])
    
    # Bellman-Held-Karp lower bound
    def lower_bound(dist_matrix):
        n = len(dist_matrix)
        L = np.inf
        V = [float('inf')] * n
        V[0] = 0
        for _ in range(n):
            for u in range(n):
                for v in range(u+1, n):
                    L = min(L, dist_matrix[u][v] + V[u] + V[v])
                    if L < dist_matrix[u][v]:
                        break  # No need to check further edges for u and v
                if L < dist_matrix[u][v]:
                    break  # No need to check further vertices for u
            else:
                break  # No need to check further vertices for u
            
        return L
    
    # Combine the three scores
    undesirability_score = reciprocity_score - min_weight_spanning_tree(distance_matrix) + lower_bound(distance_matrix)
    
    return undesirability_score
```

This new heuristics function combines three distinct but related concepts to provide a more comprehensive evaluation of edge undesirability. The reciprocity score normalizes the input distances, the minimum spanning tree heuristic encourages the inclusion of denser edges, and the lower bound heuristic estimates the potential cost of extending the solution.

This combination of heuristics should result in better performance compared to the original functions. However, the exact performance improvement will depend on the specific characteristics of the input distance matrix.

    potential = [1.0 / i for i in range(1, num_nodes + 1)]

        for j in range(num_nodes):
            potential_weight_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] / potential[j]

from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_from_dense
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance matrix to a sparse graph adjacency matrix
    adjacency_matrix = csgraph_from_dense(distance_matrix > 0)
    
    # Calculate the edge betweenness centrality using the Brandes algorithm
    edge_betweenness, _ = csgraph_betweenness(adjacency_matrix)
    
    # Convert the edge betweenness centrality to a matrix of the same shape as the input
    max_betweenness = np.max(edge_betweenness)
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i!= j:  # Ignore diagonal entries
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = edge_betweenness[i, j] / max_betweenness
    
    return heuristics_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Normalize distance matrix to sum up to 1
    total_distance = sum(sum(row) for row in distance_matrix)
    normalized_matrix = [[d / total_distance for d in row] for row in distance_matrix]
    
    # Initialize result matrix with the same shape as the input
    result_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(len(row))] for row in distance_matrix]
    
    # Fill the result matrix with heuristic scores
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(i+1, len(distance_matrix)):
            # Calculate a lower bound on the potential path length between nodes i and j
            # This is a simple heuristic that assumes the shortest path is a straight line
            # In real scenarios, you might use a more sophisticated approach like a graph-based heuristic
            potential_path_length = 0 if i == j else distance_matrix[i][j]
            # Assign a higher score for shorter potential paths
            result_matrix[i][j] = result_matrix[j][i] = 1 / potential_path_length
            # Prevent self-loops by setting this value to 0 for i == j
            result_matrix[i][i] = 0
    
    return result_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a graph from the distance matrix
    graph = np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1)  # Remove the diagonal (self-loops)
    
    # Calculate the MST using the scipy.sparse.csgraph.minimum_spanning_tree function
    mst = minimum_spanning_tree(graph)
    
    # Initialize a new matrix with the same shape as the input distance matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Fill the heuristic matrix
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        tree_nodes = set(np.where(mst[i, :] == 1)[0])
        non_tree_nodes = set(np.where(mst[i, :] == 0)[0])

        for j in tree_nodes:
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = 0  # Direct connections are already covered by the MST
        
        for j in non_tree_nodes:
            tree_node = np.where(mst[i, :] == 1)[0][0]  # Nearest tree node to non-tree node
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = min(distance_matrix[i, j], distance_matrix[tree_node, j])  # Edge cost is min(direct, MST)
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def edge_importance_score(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the degree of each node
    node_degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate the EIS for each edge
    eis = np.empty(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # For each edge (i, j), calculate its EIS
            # The EIS is a combination of the direct distance and a node degree term
            eis[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] + node_degrees[j]
    
    return eis

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the number of vertices (nodes) in the graph
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Sort all edges in non-decreasing order of their weights
    sorted_edges = sorted(enumerate(distance_matrix), key=lambda x: x[1])
    
    # Initialize the MST edges as the first edge
    mst_edges = [sorted_edges[0]]
    
    # Initialize the MST cost
    mst_cost = distance_matrix[sorted_edges[0][0], sorted_edges[0][1]]
    
    # Build the MST using Kruskal's algorithm
    for i in range(1, n):
        # Get the next edge that wouldn't form a cycle with the MST
        u, v = sorted_edges[i]
        if not is_bridge(mst_edges, u, v):
            mst_edges.append((u, v))
            mst_cost += distance_matrix[u, v]
    
    # Create a heuristic score matrix
    heuristic_scores = [[abs(distance_matrix[u, v] - mst_cost) for v in range(n)] for u in range(n)]
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((num_nodes, num_nodes))
    
    # Compute cost factor (average distance to other nodes)
    avg_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    heuristic_matrix += avg_distances[:, np.newaxis] + avg_distances[np.newaxis, :] - 2 * distance_matrix  # Each node's average distance to other nodes
    
    # Compute disparity factor (difference between a node's distance to neighbors and total distance)
    neighbors = np.argwhere(distance_matrix!= 0)
    heuristic_matrix += np.abs(distance_matrix[neighbors[:, 0], neighbors[:, 1]] - np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1))
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the Laplacian matrix from the adjacency matrix (assuming distance matrix is symmetric)
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    L = np.diag(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)) - distance_matrix
    L = L + L.T  # ensure symmetry
    L[np.diag_indices(n)] = 0  # set diagonal elements to 0

    # The eigenvalues of the Laplacian matrix provide a measure of the connectivity of the graph.
    # Smaller eigenvalues correspond to more disconnected components and thus, more undesirable edges.
    eigenvalues, _ = np.linalg.eig(L)
    heuristics_matrix = np.abs(eigenvalues)
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def floyd_warshall(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    for k in range(num_nodes):
        for i in range(num_nodes):
            for j in range(num_nodes):
                distance_matrix[i, j] = min(distance_matrix[i, j], distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j])
    return distance_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix, context_matrix):

    assert distance_matrix.shape == context_matrix.shape

    num_edges = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    importance_scores = (distance_matrix + context_matrix) / 2

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate row sums to represent the degree of each node
    row_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Calculate cumulative distribution of distances for each node
    cumulative_distance = np.cumsum(distance_matrix) / np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Calculate centrality for each edge
    heuristic_matrix = -np.square(cumulative_distance - np.roll(cumulative_distance, 1)) / (row_sums - 1)
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Floyd-Warshall Algorithm to find the shortest path between all pairs
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                distance_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    
    # Calculate the contribution of each edge to the overall shortest path
    contributions = np.where(distance_matrix!= 0, distance_matrix, np.inf)  # Replace inf with max value for non-existing paths
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Sum of shortest paths from the source to all nodes excluding i and j
            total_shortest_paths = np.sum(contributions) - distance_matrix[i][j]
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = total_shortest_paths
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Compute shortest paths using Bellman-Ford algorithm
    def bellman_ford(dist_matrix):
        for _ in range(n - 1):
            for i in range(n):
                for j, weight in enumerate(dist_matrix[i]):
                    if dist_matrix[i][j] > dist_matrix[i][_] + weight:
                        dist_matrix[i][j] = dist_matrix[i][_] + weight
        return dist_matrix

    # Calculate the lower bounds on the shortest paths
    shortest_paths = bellman_ford(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = np.minimum.accumulate(shortest_paths, axis=1)

    # Increase the heuristic value for longer paths
    # to reflect the potential for shortcuts
    heuristic_matrix += (n - 2) * distance_matrix

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def kruskal_heuristic(distance_matrix):
    # Initialize a graph and a priority queue to manage edges
    graph = {i: [] for i in range(len(distance_matrix))}
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(i+1, len(distance_matrix)):
            graph[i].append((distance_matrix[i][j], i, j))
            graph[j].append((distance_matrix[i][j], i, j))
    
    # Initialize a set to keep track of edges in MST
    mst = set()
    
    # Initialize a list to keep track of edges by weight
    edge_weight = []

    # Kruskal's Algorithm with Weighted Edge Addition Factor
    for edge in sorted(graph[0], key=lambda x: x[0]):  # Start with the smallest edge
        if not any(edge[1] in mst or edge[2] in mst, graph[edge[1]], graph[edge[2]]):
            mst.add(edge)
            heapq.heappush(edge_weight, edge[0])
            
            # Add edges with lower weights to MST
            while edge_weight and len(mst) > 1 and edge_weight[0] < min(edge_weight[0], next((w for e in graph[edge[1]] if e[2] not in mst), (float('inf'), 0, 0)))[0]:
                mst.add(next((e for e in graph[edge[1]] if e[2] not in mst), (float('inf'), 0, 0)))
                heapq.heappush(edge_weight, next((w for e in graph[edge[1]] if e[2] not in mst), (float('inf'), 0, 0))[0])
                mst.remove((edge[1], edge[2]))

    return [min(edge[0] for edge in mst) for edge in mst]



# Score: -20000

def kruskal(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    parent = list(range(n))
    rank = [0] * n

    def find(x):
        if parent[x]!= x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]

    def union(x, y):
        rootX = find(x)
        rootY = find(y)
        if rootX == rootY:
            return
        if rank[rootX] > rank[rootY]:
            parent[rootY] = rootX
        elif rank[rootX] < rank[rootY]:
            parent[rootX] = rootY
        else:
            parent[rootY] = rootX
            rank[rootX] += 1

    edges = [(i, j, distance_matrix[i][j]) for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n) if i!= j]
    edges.sort(key=lambda x: x[2])  # Sort edges by distance (weight)

    mst = [0] * n
    for u, v, w in edges:
        if find(u)!= find(v):
            union(u, v)
            mst[u] = w
            mst[v] = w

    return mst

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    mst = kruskal(distance_matrix)
    return [[max(0, distance_matrix[i][j] - mst[i]) for j in range(len(distance_matrix))] for i in range(len(distance_matrix))]
```

The function `heuristics()` now returns a matrix where each entry is the difference between the corresponding edge weight and the weight of the edge in the minimum spanning tree. This score indicates how much each edge in the original matrix should be prioritized or deprioritized in the construction of the MST. Lower values in this matrix indicate that these edges are more favorable, which is what we aim for in the optimization process.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from sklearn.cluster import AgglomerativeClustering
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the adjacency matrix
    adj_matrix = np.abs(distance_matrix - distance_matrix.T)
    
    # Use Agglomerative Clustering to identify densely connected groups
    clustering_model = AgglomerativeClustering(n_clusters=None, affinity='precomputed', linkage='average')
    clustering_labels = clustering_model.fit_predict(adj_matrix)
    
    # Create a heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros(adj_matrix.shape)
    
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i!= j:
                neighbors = adj_matrix[i, j]
                if clustering_labels[i] == clustering_labels[j]:
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 1 / (neighbors * (np.mean(adj_matrix[i, neighbors]) + np.mean(adj_matrix[j, neighbors])))
                else:
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 1 / neighbors
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]

    # Compute initial heuristic values
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] + max(distance_matrix[i]) + max(distance_matrix[:i] + distance_matrix[i+1:])

    # LKH-inspired rebalance step
    for _ in range(100):  # LKH uses a limited number of iterations, but adjust this based on your specific use case
        improved = False
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if i!= j:  # Not including the edge itself
                    prev_cost = heuristic_matrix[i][j]
                    new_cost = distance_matrix[i][j] + min(heuristic_matrix[i][:j] + [heuristic_matrix[j][i]], heuristic_matrix[j][:i] + [heuristic_matrix[i][j]])
                    if new_cost < prev_cost:
                        heuristic_matrix[i][j] = new_cost
                        improved = True

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate deviation from perfect square matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    deviations = distance_matrix - distance_matrix.diagonal()
    deviation_score = deviations.square().sum()

    # Add weighted penalty for deviations near diagonal
    weight_penalty = 0.5  # Adjust this parameter for emphasis on deviation near the diagonal
    deviations_near_diagonal = abs(deviations.abs() - deviations.diagonal().abs())
    weight_penalty_score = (deviations_near_diagonal * (1 - (deviations_near_diagonal / (2 * n))) ** weight_penalty).sum()

    # Combine deviation score and penalty score
    heuristic_score = deviation_score + weight_penalty_score

    # Normalize the score to a range between 0 and 1
    max_score = n * n  # Maximum possible deviation score (n^2)
    normalized_score = heuristic_score / max_score

    return normalized_score



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # We assume the distance matrix is undirected (i.e., distance_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[j][i])
    # and the graph is connected.
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the set of visited nodes and the minimum distance from the source node.
    visited = set()
    min_distance = [float('inf')] * n
    min_distance[0] = 0

    # Priority queue to always expand the lowest-cost edge.
    edge_heap = [(0, 0)]  # (cost, node)

    # Add all nodes to the visited set initially.
    visited.add(0)

    while edge_heap:
        # Extract the edge with the smallest cost.
        cost, node = heapq.heappop(edge_heap)

        # If this node hasn't been visited, add it to the visited set and
        # update its minimum distance.
        if node not in visited:
            visited.add(node)
            for neighbor, edge_cost in enumerate(distance_matrix[node]):
                if neighbor not in visited:
                    # Update the cost to include the new edge.
                    new_cost = cost + edge_cost
                    if new_cost < min_distance[neighbor]:
                        min_distance[neighbor] = new_cost
                        heapq.heappush(edge_heap, (new_cost, neighbor))

    return min_distance



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Initialize the graph with a default distance of infinity for all nodes except those on the diagonal
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    graph = [[float('inf')] * n for _ in range(n)]
    for i in range(n):
        graph[i][i] = 0

    # Fill the graph with the provided distance matrix
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            graph[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]

    # Function to update heuristics based on Dijkstra's algorithm
    def dijkstra(start):
        visited, distances = set(), {start: 0}
        heap = [(0, start)]

        while heap:
            current_distance, current_node = heapq.heappop(heap)

            if current_node in visited:
                continue

            visited.add(current_node)

            for neighbor, edge_cost in enumerate(graph[current_node]):
                if neighbor not in visited:
                    new_distance = current_distance + edge_cost
                    if neighbor not in distances or new_distance < distances[neighbor]:
                        distances[neighbor] = new_distance
                        heapq.heappush(heap, (new_distance, neighbor))

    # Run Dijkstra's algorithm for each node and update heuristics
    for node in range(n):
        dijkstra(node)

    # The heuristic for each node is the sum of its direct distance and the minimum distance from all other reachable nodes
    heuristics_matrix = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = graph[i][j] + min(distances.values())

    return heuristics_matrix
```

This `heuristics()` function applies Dijkstra's algorithm to each node in the graph to compute the minimum total path cost from each node to all other reachable nodes. Then, it calculates the heuristic value for each edge as the sum of the direct cost and this minimum path cost. This approach, while still a heuristic, tends to perform better than the simple distance matrix reflection or the other presented function, as it takes into account the potential for shorter paths through multiple nodes.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist
from sklearn.manifold import Node2Vec
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance_matrix into a graph where nodes are indices
    graph = np.zeros((len(distance_matrix), len(distance_matrix)))
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(i, len(distance_matrix)):
            graph[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]
            graph[j, i] = graph[i, j] # Symmetric graph

    # Use Node2Vec to capture graph structure
    node2vec = Node2Vec(n_components=1, graph=graph, dim=1, steps=10)
    node2vec.fit(graph)

    # Get vector representation of each node
    node_embeddings = node2vec.get_node_embeddings()

    # Convert the vector back to a heuristic score for each edge
    heuristic_scores = np.dot(node_embeddings, node_embeddings.T)
    heuristic_scores = np.exp(-heuristic_scores)  # Applying softmax

    return heuristic_scores

    heuristics_matrix = [(avg_distance - d) / avg_distance for d in distance_matrix]
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Graph representation as an adjacency list
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    graph = [[] for _ in range(n)]
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i][j]!= 0:
                graph[i].append((distance_matrix[i][j], j))
                graph[j].append((distance_matrix[j][i], i))

    # Set to keep track of included vertices
    included = set()

    # Priority queue for Prim's algorithm
    priority_queue = [(0, 0)]  # (total_weight, root_vertex)

    # Initialize the total weight to 0 and the first vertex included
    total_weight = 0
    root_vertex = 0

    # Build the MST
    while priority_queue:
        weight, current_vertex = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)
        total_weight += weight  # Add the weight of the edge to the total

        # If the vertex is already included, skip it
        if current_vertex in included:
            continue

        # Add the current vertex to the included set
        included.add(current_vertex)

        # Add neighbors to the priority queue
        for neighbor_weight, neighbor in graph[current_vertex]:
            if neighbor not in included:
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (neighbor_weight, neighbor))

    return total_weight



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = [[0]*n for _ in range(n)]

    # Calculate the heuristic values using triangle inequality
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            for k in range(n):
                if i!= j and j!= k and i!= k:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] = min(heuristic_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    
    return heuristic_matrix
