import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # First, convert the distance matrix to a graph
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate the betweenness centrality
    betweenness_centrality = nx.betweenness_centrality(G, weight='weight')
    
    # Convert the centrality scores back to a matrix
    heuristics_matrix = nx.to_numpy_array(G, nodelist=G.nodes(), weight='weight')
    
    # Normalize centrality scores to be between 0 and 1 (optional, depends on specific use case)
    # Here we'll use a simple normalization by dividing each centrality by the max centrality
    normalized_heuristics_matrix = [score / max(betweenness_centrality.values()) for score in betweenness_centrality.values()]

    return normalized_heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get shape of the input distance matrix
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as input
    heuristic_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate the pseudo-distance for each node
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            # The immediate distance is the input distance
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]

            # Potential future dissimilarities are calculated as if these nodes were not connected
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] += min(
                heuristic_matrix[i, k] + heuristic_matrix[k, j] for k in range(num_nodes) if k!= i and k!= j
            )

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the square root of the distance matrix to work with distances
    distances = np.sqrt(distance_matrix)
    
    # Get the shape of the matrix
    rows, cols = distances.shape
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distances)
    
    # Calculate the shortest path to every node from each node
    # Using Floyd-Warshall algorithm for efficiency
    for k in range(rows):
        for i in range(rows):
            for j in range(cols):
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = min(heuristic_matrix[i][j], distances[i][k] + distances[k][j])
    
    return heuristic_matrix

# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize priority queue with all vertices and their distances
    priority_queue = [(0, i) for i in range(n)]
    heapq.heapify(priority_queue)

    # Heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [float('inf')] * n

    # Compute shortest paths
    while priority_queue:
        current_distance, current_vertex = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)
        if current_distance > heuristics_matrix[current_vertex]:
            continue

        for neighbor, weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_vertex]):
            if weight > 0 and heuristics_matrix[neighbor] > current_distance + weight:
                heuristics_matrix[neighbor] = current_distance + weight
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (heuristics_matrix[neighbor], neighbor))

    # Normalize heuristics
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                heuristics_matrix[i] = heuristics_matrix[i] / (distance_matrix[i][j] + heuristics_matrix[j])

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the pairwise distance matrix
    D = squareform(pdist(distance_matrix))

    # Create a graph from the distance matrix
    graph = scipy.sparse.csgraph.create_adjacency_matrix(D, connectivity=1)

    # Find the MST
    MST = minimum_spanning_tree(graph)

    # Initialize heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.copy(D)

    # Iterate over each node (except the last)
    for i in range(MST.shape[0] - 1):
        # Find nearest neighbor for current node
        nearest_neighbor_index = np.argmin(D[i, MST[i].indices])

        # Replace the current edge with its nearest neighbor
        heuristics_matrix[i, nearest_neighbor_index] = D[i, nearest_neighbor_index]
        heuristics_matrix[nearest_neighbor_index, i] = D[nearest_neighbor_index, i]

        # Remove the current node from MST
        MST = minimum_spanning_tree(graph.toarray() - np.diag(np.sum(graph.toarray(), axis=1)))
        MST[i, MST.shape[0] - 1] = np.inf

    # Update the last edge of the MST with the shortest remaining edge
    heuristics_matrix[MST.indices[np.argmin(MST.data)]] = D[MST.indices[np.argmin(MST.data)], MST.indptr[-1]]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the average distance of each node's neighbors
    average_neighbor_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix[np.nonzero(distance_matrix)], axis=1)
    
    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with the same shape as the distance matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Assign negative values to edges with high weight and high average distance
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(len(distance_matrix)):
            if i!= j:  # don't consider diagonal elements
                # Avoid division by zero
                if distance_matrix[i, j] > 0:
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] = -(distance_matrix[i, j] * average_neighbor_distances[j])
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))  # Initialize matrix of zeros, same shape as input

    # Compute nearest neighbor heuristic
    for i in range(n):
        nearest_idx = np.argmin(distance_matrix[i])
        heuristic_matrix[i, nearest_idx] = distance_matrix[i, nearest_idx]

    # Compute 2-Opt heuristic
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            min_cost = float('inf')
            for k in range(n):
                if k!= i and k!= j:
                    cost = distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[j][k] + distance_matrix[i][k]
                    if cost < min_cost:
                        min_cost = cost
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = min_cost
            heuristic_matrix[j][i] = min_cost  # Symmetric 2-Opt

    # Add connectivity weight
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                # Calculate weight based on the number of common neighbors
                common_neighbors = np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix[i] <= distance_matrix[j])
                weight = (1 - np.exp(-(distance_matrix[i, j] / 1000))) * common_neighbors
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] += weight

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def kruskal_mst(distance_matrix):
    """
    Kruskal's Algorithm for Minimum Spanning Tree
    """
    def find(parent, i):
        if parent[i] == i:
            return i
        return find(parent, parent[i])



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def minimum_routing_cost_heuristic(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the sum of the diagonal elements (each vertex's self-distance)
    total_cost = np.sum(distance_matrix)
    
    # Compute the sum of the lower triangular matrix (excluding the diagonal)
    # This represents the sum of pairwise distances
    pairwise_cost = np.tril(distance_matrix).sum()
    
    # Return the heuristic value as a distance matrix
    return 2 * total_cost - pairwise_cost

import numpy as np
def improved_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the density of the matrix
    density = np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix) / (distance_matrix.size ** 2)
    
    # Initialize a new distance matrix with the same shape as input
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Assign lower values where the density is high (dense areas)
    heuristics_matrix[density > 0.5] = -1000  # A very low value
    # Assign higher values where the density is low (sparse areas)
    heuristics_matrix[density <= 0.1] = 1000  # A very high value
    # For intermediate densities, assign a value based on a quadratic function
    heuristics_matrix[np.logical_and(density > 0.1, density < 0.5)] = (1000 - 1000 * (density - 0.1)) ** 2
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    edge_scores = {}
    
    # Sum of most distant edges
    max_dist_edges = [(i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n) if distance_matrix[i][j] > max_dist]
    max_dist = max(max_dist_edges, key=lambda x: distance_matrix[x[0]][x[1]])
    sum_most_dist = sum(distance_matrix[i][j] for i, j in max_dist_edges)
    
    # Average distance
    avg_dist = sum(sum(row) for row in distance_matrix) / (n * n)
    
    # Ratio of highest to lowest distance edge
    min_dist = min(sum(row) for row in distance_matrix)
    ratio = distance_matrix[sum_most_dist.index(max(sum_most_dist))][sum_most_dist.index(max(sum_most_dist))] / min_dist
    
    # Create edge scores
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            score = (sum_most_dist + avg_dist - 2*min_dist) / (2 * min_dist) * ratio
            edge_scores[(i, j)] = score
            edge_scores[(j, i)] = score  # Assuming symmetric graph
    
    return edge_scores



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the difference between each edge and its shortest possible value (minimum value along diagonal)
    min_diagonal_values = np.diag(np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0))
    residual_distances = distance_matrix - min_diagonal_values[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Add these residual distances to the original matrix as a new heuristic
    heuristic_matrix = residual_distances + distance_matrix
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate a diagonal distance matrix for each row
    diagonals = [sum(distance_matrix[i]) for i in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as distance_matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [row.copy() for row in distance_matrix]
    
    # Apply the clustering effect by setting the diagonal elements to be the minimum of the diagonal and the sum of its nearest neighbors
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        sum_neighbors = diagonals[i]
        for j in range(len(distance_matrix[0])):
            if j!= i:  # Avoid self-comparison
                sum_neighbors += distance_matrix[i][j]
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], sum_neighbors)
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.cluster.hierarchy import linkage, dendrogram
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist
def edge_betweenness_centrality(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adj_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j]!= 0:
                adj_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]
                adj_matrix[j, i] = distance_matrix[i, j]  # Undirected graph

    # Calculate edge-betweenness centrality using the clustering hierarchy
    z = linkage(pdist(adj_matrix), method='complete')
    f = 1 / (4 * np.pi * np.linalg.norm(z[:, 2:])**2)
    bc = np.sum(f * z[:, 2:], axis=1)

    return bc

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.linalg import eigs
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Add a small constant to ensure the matrix is positive definite
    distance_matrix += 1e-8 * np.eye(distance_matrix.shape[0])
    
    # Compute the eigenvalues and eigenvectors
    eigenvalues, eigenvectors = eigs(distance_matrix, k=1, which='LM')
    
    # Normalize the Fiedler vector
    eigenvectors = eigenvectors / np.linalg.norm(eigenvectors)
    
    # Create the heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    np.fill_diagonal(heuristics_matrix, 0)  # Self-loops should have zero cost
    
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
            if i!= j:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = eigenvectors[0, j]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    edge_density = distance_matrix.sum() / (num_nodes * (num_nodes - 1))  # Edge density
    local_connectivity = np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix < 1, axis=1) / (num_nodes - 1)  # Local connectivity
    global_connectivity = np.mean(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1) == np.min(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)))  # Global connectivity
    cost_of_inclusion = distance_matrix.diagonal()  # Diagonal elements represent cost of including an edge between a node and itself

    # Combine these metrics into a single heuristic score
    heuristic_score = edge_density * 0.5 + local_connectivity * 0.3 + global_connectivity * 0.1 + cost_of_inclusion * 0.1

    # Normalize the score to a 0-1 range
    return (heuristic_score - min(heuristic_score)) / (max(heuristic_score) - min(heuristic_score))

import numpy as np
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the importance score of each node using degree and betweenness centrality
    node_importance = nx.degree_centrality(G) + nx.betweenness_centrality(G)
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Fill the heuristic matrix based on node importance and distances
    for u, v in zip(G.edges()):
        heuristics_matrix[u, v] = distance_matrix[u, v] + node_importance[u] + node_importance[v]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize potential score matrix with zeros
    potential_score = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Calculate potential score for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                potential = distance_matrix[i][j]  # current edge distance
                
                # Calculate potential contribution
                reduction_potential = distance_matrix[i][i] + distance_matrix[j][j] - distance_matrix[i][j]
                potential += reduction_potential
                
                # Damping factor to avoid over-optimization
                damping_factor = 0.5
                
                potential = potential * damping_factor
                
                potential_score[i][j] = potential
    
    return potential_score



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of distances for each row (node)
    row_sums = sum(distance_matrix, [])
    
    # Calculate the centrality of each edge (inverse of row sums)
    centrality = 1 / row_sums
    
    # Normalize centrality values to be within [0, 1]
    centrality = [min(1, max(0, c)) for c in centrality]
    
    # Assign the centrality values as the heuristic scores
    heuristic_scores = [centrality[i] for i in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # First, find the minimum and second-minimum distance for each row (i.e., each vertex)
    min_distances = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    sec_min_distances = np.sort(np.delete(np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1), 0))[::-1]

    # Create a new matrix where each value represents the 2-Opt ratio for each edge
    # An edge is represented as [u, v, cost] where u and v are the vertices and cost is the distance.
    # The 2-Opt ratio for an edge is (cost / sec_min_distance(u)) if sec_min_distance(u) > min_distances[v] else 0
    heuristic_matrix = np.where(
        (distance_matrix[:, None] >= distance_matrix[None, :]) & 
        (distance_matrix[:, None] < sec_min_distances[np.newaxis, :]),
        distance_matrix[:, None] / sec_min_distances[np.newaxis, :],
        0
    ).astype(float)

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np

    avg_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=0)

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # 1. Flow-based Importance (using Max-Flow Min-Cut)
    flow_based_importance = nx.maximum_flow(G, 0, len(G) - 1)['capacity']
    min_cut = nx.minimum_cut(G, 0, len(G) - 1)
    flow_based_importance /= min_cut
    
    # 2. Rank-based Importance (simplified PageRank)
    rank_based_importance = {}
    for node in G.nodes():
        rank = nx.pagerank(G, alpha=0.85)[node]
        rank_based_importance[node] = rank
    
    return flow_based_importance, rank_based_importance

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate shortest path heuristic using Floyd-Warshall algorithm
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = min(heuristic_matrix[i, j], heuristic_matrix[i, k] + heuristic_matrix[k, j])
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def weighted_distance_and_path_count(distance_matrix, path_matrix):
    """
    heuristics() function that assigns a score to each edge in the distance matrix
    based on its distance and the number of paths passing through it.

    Args:
    distance_matrix (list of list of float): 2D list representing the distance between all pairs of nodes.
    path_matrix (list of list of int): 2D list representing the number of paths between all pairs of nodes.

    Returns:
    list of list of float: A matrix where each element (i, j) is the heuristic score for the edge between nodes i and j.
    """

    # Get the dimensions of the distance matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)

    # Initialize the heuristic score matrix with zeros
    heuristic_scores = [[0.0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

    # Iterate over each node (i, j)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # If i and j are the same, edge not present
            if i == j:
                heuristic_scores[i][j] = float('inf')
            else:
                # Score is the weighted sum of distance and path count
                heuristic_scores[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] * path_matrix[i][j]

    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with negative distance
    heuristic_matrix = -distance_matrix
    
    # Iteratively add cities to the route
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        # Update the heuristic matrix by adding the smallest unvisited distance
        heuristic_matrix[i] = min(heuristic_matrix[i], heuristic_matrix[j] + distance_matrix[j, i])
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the shape of the input matrix
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize a dictionary to store tentative distances
    tentative_distances = {node: (distance_matrix[node][node], node) for node in range(num_nodes)}
    
    # Set of unvisited nodes
    unvisited = set(range(num_nodes))

    # Priority queue to store (distance, node)
    # Lower priority means a shorter path to this node
    priority_queue = [(0, node) for node in unvisited]
    heapq.heapify(priority_queue)

    # Dijkstra's algorithm
    while priority_queue:
        # Get the node with the lowest tentative distance
        current_distance, current_node = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)

        # Skip if we've already computed a better path for this node
        if current_distance > tentative_distances[current_node][0]:
            continue

        # Update tentative distances to neighboring nodes
        for neighbor, weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_node]):
            if neighbor not in unvisited:
                continue

            new_distance = current_distance + weight

            # If a shorter path to this neighbor is found
            if new_distance < tentative_distances[neighbor][0]:
                tentative_distances[neighbor] = (new_distance, neighbor)
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (new_distance, neighbor))

    # Prepare the heuristic matrix
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * num_nodes for _ in range(num_nodes)]
    for node1 in range(num_nodes):
        for node2 in range(num_nodes):
            if node1!= node2:
                heuristic_matrix[node1][node2] = tentative_distances[node2][0]

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the shape of the distance matrix
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same size as the input
    heuristic_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Run bidirectional search
    def bidirectional_search(start, goal):
        queue = [(0, start)]  # (cost, node)
        visited = set([start])
        while queue:
            (cost, current) = queue.pop(0)
            if current == goal:
                return cost
            
            # Explore along the path from current to goal
            for neighbor, edge_cost in enumerate(distance_matrix[current]):
                if neighbor not in visited:
                    visited.add(neighbor)
                    new_cost = cost + edge_cost
                    queue.append((new_cost, neighbor))
            
            # Explore from the goal towards the start
            reverse_queue = [(cost, goal) for (cost, node) in enumerate(distance_matrix[::-1])]
            while reverse_queue:
                (reverse_cost, goal) = reverse_queue.pop(0)
                if goal not in visited:
                    visited.add(goal)
                    new_cost = reverse_cost + distance_matrix[goal][start]
                    heuristic_matrix[goal][start] = new_cost
                    queue.append((new_cost, start))
                
                for neighbor, edge_cost in enumerate(distance_matrix[goal]):
                    if neighbor not in visited:
                        visited.add(neighbor)
                        new_cost = reverse_cost + edge_cost
                        heuristic_matrix[goal][neighbor] = new_cost
                        queue.append((new_cost, neighbor))
        
        return None  # No path found



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
from scipy.sparse import csr_matrix
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to a CSR (Compressed Sparse Row) matrix for efficient processing
    csr_distance = csr_matrix(distance_matrix)

    # Compute the potential for each vertex
    potential = np.min(csr_distance.toarray(), axis=0)

    # Create the adjacency matrix from the CSR distance matrix
    adjacency_matrix = csr_distance.toarray()

    # Perform Kruskal's algorithm to compute the Minimum Spanning Tree (MST)
    try:
        mst = minimum_spanning_tree(csr_distance)
    except ValueError:
        # If the graph is not connected, this exception will be raised. In such a case, we assign a very high potential to all edges.
        max_potential = np.max(potential)
        adjacency_matrix = np.where(csr_distance.sum(axis=0) > 0, potential.reshape(potential.shape[0], 1), max_potential)

    # Initialize the result matrix with potentials
    heuristic_matrix = potential[:, np.newaxis]

    # Assign potentials to the MST edges
    mst_edges = mst.indices
    for edge in mst_edges:
        heuristic_matrix[edge[0], edge[1]] = -1
        heuristic_matrix[edge[1], edge[0]] = -1

    # If the graph is not connected, assign high potentials to all non-MST edges
    if np.any(mst.indices.sum(axis=0) == 0):
        max_potential += 100  # Adjust this value according to your specific needs

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def potential_energy(distance_matrix):
    # This function calculates the potential energy matrix.
    # It considers the negative of the sum of distances for each node.
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    potential_energy = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                potential_energy[i][j] = potential_energy[j][i] = -distance_matrix[i][j]
    return potential_energy



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_ shortest_paths
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    """
    Calculates edge heuristics based on graph centrality measures.

    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (ndarray): A 2D numpy array of shape (n, n) representing the distance matrix.

    Returns:
    ndarray: A 2D numpy array of the same shape as the input, representing edge heuristics.
    """
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Calculate degree centrality
    degree_centrality = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)

    # Calculate betweenness centrality
    shortest_paths_matrix = csgraph_shortest_paths(csgraph=distance_matrix, directed=False)
    betweenness_centrality = np.sum(shortest_paths_matrix, axis=1)

    # Calculate closeness centrality
    closeness_centrality = 1 / np.sum(shortest_paths_matrix, axis=1)

    # Combine centrality measures to form the heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = np.array([degree_centrality, betweenness_centrality, closeness_centrality])
    return heuristics_matrix

    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Get the number of nodes
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Calculate the weighted cost for each edge
    heuristics = np.sqrt(distance_matrix + 1)  # Adding 1 to avoid division by zero

    # Calculate the frequency of each edge
    edge_frequency = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)  # Sum of each row (frequency of connections from a node)
    
    # Combine heuristic and frequency
    heuristics = heuristics * edge_frequency / np.sum(edge_frequency)  # Normalize

    return heuristics

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the average distance
    avg_distance = np.mean(distance_matrix)
    
    # Add a penalty factor for each distance that deviates significantly from the average
    penalty_factor = 0.5  # This factor can be tuned for better results
    distance_matrix_with_penalty = distance_matrix + penalty_factor * np.abs(distance_matrix - avg_distance[:, np.newaxis])

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import shortest_path
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the number of shortest paths between each pair of nodes
    n_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    num_shortest_paths = np.zeros((n_nodes, n_nodes))
    for i in range(n_nodes):
        for j in range(i+1, n_nodes):
            # Use sparse matrix shortest path algorithm for efficiency
            path = shortest_path(csgraph=distance_matrix[i][j], directed=True, return_predecessors=False)
            num_shortest_paths[i][j] = np.sum(path == j)

    # Compute the heuristic value for each edge
    heuristic_matrix = distance_matrix + num_shortest_paths
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_vertices = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initiate a distance matrix of the same shape with large values
    unvisited_distances = [[float('inf')] * num_vertices for _ in range(num_vertices)]

    # Set the distance to self as 0
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        unvisited_distances[i][i] = 0

    # NN heuristic: always pick the nearest unvisited vertex
    for _ in range(num_vertices):
        # Get the index of the nearest unvisited vertex
        min_dist_index = min(range(num_vertices), key=lambda i: unvisited_distances[0][i])

        # Mark this vertex as visited
        unvisited_distances[0][min_dist_index] = 0
        for j in range(num_vertices):
            # Update the distance if it's closer
            unvisited_distances[j][min_dist_index] = distance_matrix[j][min_dist_index]

    return unvisited_distances



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.cluster.hierarchy import linkage, fcluster
def heuristics(distance_matrix, density_threshold=1.0, max_cluster_size=100):
    # Flatten the distance matrix
    dists = np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1)
    
    # Perform hierarchical clustering using Ward method
    Z = linkage(dists, method='ward')
    
    # Compute the cluster labels using fcluster with a specified depth
    cluster_labels = fcluster(Z, max_cluster_size, criterion='distance')
    
    # Create a new NxN matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    # Assign lower values to edges that belong to the same cluster
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        heuristic_matrix[i, :] = cluster_labels[Z.parents[i]]
    
    # Set all distances within the same cluster to a very small value to penalize connecting nodes in the same cluster
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(i, len(distance_matrix[i])):
            if cluster_labels[i] == cluster_labels[j]:
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = 1e-6  # Set a very small number (1e-6)
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.linalg import eigsh
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate degree centrality
    degree_centrality = np.array(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0))
    
    # Calculate betweenness centrality
    # Betweenness Centrality is a measure of the number of shortest paths that pass through a particular vertex
    # We will calculate it for each vertex (row)
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    betweenness = np.zeros((n, n))
    for _ in range(n):
        # Initialize adjacency matrix with ones for undirected graph
        adj_matrix = np.eye(n)
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if distance_matrix[i, j]!= 0:  # Avoid zero division
                    adj_matrix[i, j] = 1 / distance_matrix[i, j]
        
        # Betweenness calculation
        short_paths = eigsh(adj_matrix - np.eye(n), k=1)[0]
        betweenness += short_paths * (short_paths > 0)
    
    # Normalize centrality measures
    degree_centrality = degree_centrality / np.sum(degree_centrality)
    betweenness = betweenness / np.sum(betweenness)
    
    # Combine with distance matrix
    heuristics_matrix = degree_centrality + betweenness + np.abs(distance_matrix)
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Define a road network connectivity and congestion matrix
    # For simplicity, let's assume a 3x3 matrix where 0 represents no connection and 1 represents a connection
    road_network = np.array([
        [1, 0, 1],
        [1, 1, 1],
        [0, 1, 1]
    ])

    # Initialize a new heuristic matrix with the same dimensions as the distance matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Iterate through each vertex
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):

            # If the vertex isn't the same as the current one, consider adding this edge
            if i!= j:
                # Calculate the combined distance (distance + congestion) between the current and potential next vertices
                combined_distance = distance_matrix[i, j] + (1 - road_network[i, j])

                # Add this heuristic to the matrix for the current vertex
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = combined_distance

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def advanced_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of diagonal elements for each edge
    diagonal_sum = [sum(row) for row in distance_matrix]
    
    # Calculate the sum of off-diagonal elements for each edge
    off_diagonal_sum = sum(distance_matrix[i][j] for i in range(len(distance_matrix)) for j in range(i+1, len(distance_matrix)))
    
    # Construct and return the heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [diagonal_sum + off_diagonal_sum for _ in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Check if the input is a 2D numpy array
    if not isinstance(distance_matrix, np.ndarray) or distance_matrix.ndim!= 2:
        raise ValueError("Input should be a 2D numpy array (distance matrix)")
    
    # Calculate the average travel time for each node (edge)
    avg_travel_time = distance_matrix / np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1, keepdims=True)
    
    # Calculate the heuristic score for each edge.
    # A lower score indicates a better edge.
    heuristics_score = np.mean(avg_travel_time, axis=1)
    
    return heuristics_score



# Score: -20000
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Find the minimum spanning tree (MST) of the graph
    mst_cost = nx.minimum_spanning_tree_algorithm(G, weight='weight')
    
    # Create a new matrix to store the heuristic values
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Assign each non-edge (i,j) a heuristic value based on its position in MST
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(i+1, distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # If (i,j) is not in the MST, its cost is the edge weight
            if (i,j) not in mst_cost.edges():
                heuristics_matrix[i,j] = distance_matrix[i,j]
            # If (i,j) is in the MST, its cost is the MST cost between its endpoints
            else:
                a, b = min(i,j), max(i,j)
                heuristics_matrix[i,j] = mst_cost[a,b]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Initialize the result matrix
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((num_nodes, num_nodes))

    # Adaptive edge weight decay
    decay_factor = 0.5  # adjust this value based on your needs
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i == j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
            else:
                distance_ij = distance_matrix[i][j]
                distance_goal = min(distance_matrix[i][goal] for goal in range(num_nodes) if goal!= i)
                distance_heuristic = distance_ij + decay_factor * (distance_goal - distance_ij)
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_heuristic

    # Adjacency-based global influence
    adjacent_edges_count = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)  # count edges connected to each node
    heuristic_matrix += np.transpose(adjacent_edges_count)  # mirror for symmetric matrix

    # Normalize the heuristic matrix
    norm = np.sum(heuristic_matrix, axis=1)
    heuristic_matrix /= norm[:, np.newaxis]

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Weighted Shortest Path
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    weighted_distances = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i == j:
                weighted_distances[i][j] = 0
            else:
                weighted_distances[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
                for k in range(n):
                    if i!= k and j!= k:
                        weighted_distances[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][k] * distance_matrix[k][j]  # Assuming equal weights for edges

    # Step 2: Conflict Matrix
    conflict_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i == j:
                conflict_matrix[i][j] = 0
            else:
                count = sum(weighted_distances[i] >= weighted_distances[j])
                conflict_matrix[i][j] = count / (n - 1)  # Adjust the denominator according to your context

    # Combine both heuristics
    result = weighted_distances + conflict_matrix
    return result



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Calculate the total distance between all pairs
    total_distance = sum(sum(distance_matrix[i][j] for j in range(n)) for i in range(n))
    
    # Calculate the initial total cost without any edges
    initial_total_cost = sum(sum(distance_matrix[i][j] for j in range(n)) for i in range(n))
    
    # Initialize a new matrix to store heuristic values
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Calculate heuristic for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:  # Only consider non-adjacent edges for simplicity
                # Calculate reduction in total distance if edge (i, j) is included
                reduction = total_distance - (distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[j][i])
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = reduction / 2  # Normalize by 2 to get a better scale
    
    return heuristic_matrix

    # Calculate the shortest path matrix
    shortest_path = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1)

    # Calculate the edge density
    max_edges = n * (n - 1) // 2
    edge_density = len(distance_matrix) * len(distance_matrix[0]) / max_edges

    # Define the heuristic scores
    heuristics_matrix = -edge_density - np.mean(shortest_path)

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]

    # Calculate cost to connect each vertex pair
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # Initial cost to reach j from i
            cost_ij = distance_matrix[i][j]

            # Remove edge (i, j) and add new edges (i, k) and (j, l)
            # where k and l are the closest vertices in the remaining graph
            # to i and j, respectively
            removed_cost = cost_ij
            for k in range(n):
                if k!= i and distance_matrix[i][k] < removed_cost:
                    removed_cost = distance_matrix[i][k]

            for l in range(n):
                if l!= j and distance_matrix[j][l] < removed_cost:
                    removed_cost = distance_matrix[j][l]

            new_cost = removed_cost + min(distance_matrix[i][k] for k in range(n) if k!= i) + \
                        min(distance_matrix[j][l] for l in range(n) if l!= j)

            # Heuristic is the difference between the new cost and the removed cost
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = new_cost - removed_cost

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Calculate the triangle inequality heuristic
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # For each edge (i,j), calculate how much the sum of distances to all other nodes (k) deviates from (i,j)
            deviation = sum(distance_matrix[i, k] for k in range(n) if k!= j) - distance_matrix[i, j]
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = max(0, deviation)  # Non-negative value to avoid negative scores
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of each row, representing the total distance from that node
    row_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Calculate the total sum of all distances in the matrix
    total_sum = np.sum(distance_matrix)
    
    # Edge redundancy heuristic: for each edge (i, j), if the path through i also passes through some other node k (i.e., i < k < j), increase the heuristic score for this edge
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(i+1, len(distance_matrix)):
            for k in range(i, len(distance_matrix)):
                if distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j] > distance_matrix[i][j]:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] += row_sums[k] - total_sum
                elif distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j] == distance_matrix[i][j]:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] += row_sums[k]
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_betweenness_centrality
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance matrix into a sparse, undirected graph
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    graph = csgraph_betweenness_centrality(csgraph=distance_matrix, directed=False)
    
    # Create an empty matrix for the heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate edge importance scores
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # If the edge exists (distance[i][j] > 0), use betweenness centrality
            if distance_matrix[i,j] > 0:
                heuristics_matrix[i,j] = graph[i,j]
                heuristics_matrix[j,i] = graph[i,j]  # For symmetry
    
    # Normalize the heuristics matrix by total betweenness centrality
    max_betweenness = max(np.max(graph))
    heuristics_matrix = heuristics_matrix / max_betweenness
    
    return heuristics_matrix

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    farthest_node = max(range(num_nodes), key=lambda i: max(distance_matrix[i]))

    # Initialize a matrix with the same shape as the input, filled with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * num_nodes for _ in range(num_nodes)]

    # Calculate the heuristic values for each edge
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            # Exclude the diagonal entries (i.e., self-loops)
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[farthest_node][i]

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the shape of the distance matrix
    num_vertices = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * num_vertices for _ in range(num_vertices)]
    
    # Calculate Min-Heuristic (shortest edges)
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(i+1, num_vertices):
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]  # same as input
    
    # Calculate Max-Heuristic (longest edges)
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(i+1, num_vertices):
            max_distance = float('-inf')
            for k in range(num_vertices):
                if i!= k and j!= k:
                    max_distance = max(max_distance, distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = max_distance  # update with longest edges
    
    # Create a new heuristic matrix that balances both heuristics
    # Using a weighted sum of Min-Heuristic and Max-Heuristic
    # We will use 0.5 as a starting weight for both heuristics
    weighted_heuristic_matrix = [[0] * num_vertices for _ in range(num_vertices)]
    
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(num_vertices):
            weighted_heuristic_matrix[i][j] = 0.5 * heuristic_matrix[i][j] + 0.5 * (num_vertices - distance_matrix[i][j] - 1)  # subtract 1 to avoid division by zero
    
    return weighted_heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            for k in range(n):
                if distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j] < distance_matrix[i][j]:
                    # If direct path from i to j is not the shortest, 
                    # consider alternative paths through j
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] += (distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    
    # To avoid negative scores, apply a minimum value
    np.maximum(heuristic_matrix, 0, out=heuristic_matrix)
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    clustering = np.mean(np.power(np.abs(np.eye(n) - np.outer(np.ones(n), np.ones(n))), 2))
    
    # Degree distribution
    degree_distribution = np.sum(np.abs(distance_matrix), axis=1)
    degree_distribution /= np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Centrality measures
    betweenness = np.zeros(n)
    for _ in range(100):  # 100 iterations, can be adjusted
        bet = np.zeros(n)
        for i in range(n):
            bet[i] = np.mean(np.abs(np.linalg.matrix_power(distance_matrix + np.eye(n), np.linalg.matrix_rank(distance_matrix) - 1) - distance_matrix))
        betweenness = np.sum(bet, axis=0)

    closeness = 1 / np.sum(np.abs(np.linalg.inv(distance_matrix)), axis=1)
    
    # Weighted distance heuristics
    weighted_distance = np.matmul(distance_matrix, np.ones(n))
    
    # Combine heuristics
    result = (1 - clustering) * (1 - degree_distribution) * (1 - closeness) + weighted_distance
    result = 1 / result  # Normalize to make it a heuristic matrix
    
    return result

import numpy as np
def distances(row, col):
    return np.sqrt((row[0] - col[0])**2 + (row[1] - col[1])**2)



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from heapq import heappop, heappush
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Prim's Algorithm for shortest paths
    visited = [False] * n
    shortest_paths = [float('inf')] * n
    shortest_paths[0] = 0
    
    priority_queue = [(0, 0)]  # (distance, node)
    while priority_queue:
        current_distance, current_node = heappop(priority_queue)
        
        if visited[current_node]:
            continue
        visited[current_node] = True
        
        for neighbor, weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_node]):
            if not visited[neighbor]:
                new_distance = current_distance + weight
                if new_distance < shortest_paths[neighbor]:
                    shortest_paths[neighbor] = new_distance
                    heappush(priority_queue, (new_distance, neighbor))
                    
    # Probabilistic Edge-Weight Update
    prob_update = 0.5  # Adjust this value for sensitivity
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                weight = distance_matrix[i][j]
                new_weight = min(weight, shortest_paths[i] + shortest_paths[j])  # If shortest path between two nodes is shorter than direct edge, use this
                distance_matrix[i][j] = new_weight
                prob_update = min(prob_update, np.random.rand())  # Adjust this value for randomness in probabilistic update
        
    # Edge Prioritization
    edge_priority = np.zeros(n**2)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                edge_priority[i*n + j] = 1 / distance_matrix[i][j]  # More urgent edges should be prioritized with lower priority values
            
    return edge_priority



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get dimensions
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize impact matrix with zeros
    impact_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]

    # Calculate impact for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            impact = distance_matrix[i][j]
            for k in range(n):
                if i!= k and j!= k:  # Avoid self-loop and diagonal
                    impact -= distance_matrix[i][k] * distance_matrix[k][j]
            impact_matrix[i][j] = impact  # Store impact in matrix

    return impact_matrix



# Score: -20000

def novel_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the average distance of the node
    average_distance = sum(sum(distance_matrix)) / (distance_matrix.shape[0] * distance_matrix.shape[1])
    
    # Create a new matrix with the same dimensions as the input
    heuristic_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Fill the matrix by incorporating both distance and node position
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i == 0:  # First row (source nodes)
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] * (1 - (average_distance / distance_matrix[i][j]))  # Higher weight for peripheral nodes
            elif j == 0:  # First column (destination nodes)
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] * (1 - (average_distance / distance_matrix[i][j]))  # Higher weight for peripheral nodes
            else:  # All other nodes
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] * (1 - (average_distance / distance_matrix[i][j])) * (1 - (i + j) / (distance_matrix.shape[0] + distance_matrix.shape[1] - 2))  # Adjust for position and overall average weight
    
    return heuristic_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate reliability scores
    reliability_scores = 1 / distance_matrix
    # Sum all reliability scores
    total_reliability = sum(reliability_scores)
    # Normalize reliability scores
    normalized_reliability_scores = [score / total_reliability for score in reliability_scores]
    return normalized_reliability_scores



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    undesirability_score = [[0 for _ in range(num_nodes)] for _ in range(num_nodes)]

    # Calculate initial score
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i, num_nodes):
            undesirability_score[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
            undesirability_score[j][i] = undesirability_score[i][j]

    # Perform a basic greedy neighborhood search
    for _ in range(5):  # Number of neighborhood iterations
        for node1 in range(num_nodes):
            for node2 in range(node1 + 1, num_nodes):
                # If edge exists, check the cost of replacing it with a direct connection
                if undesirability_score[node1][node2] < undesirability_score[node1][node2] + undesirability_score[node1][node2]:
                    undesirability_score[node1][node2] = undesirability_score[node1][node2] + undesirability_score[node1][node2]
                    undesirability_score[node2][node1] = undesirability_score[node1][node2]

    return undesirability_score

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # To account for potential different weights (e.g., cost, time, etc.)
    weights = np.ones(distance_matrix.shape)  # Using uniform weights for simplicity

    # Calculate total weighted distance for each edge
    total_weighted_distances = distance_matrix + weights  # Adding weights to each element of the distance matrix

    # Sum these values for each row (edge), creating a new matrix
    row_sums = np.sum(total_weighted_distances, axis=1)

    # Normalize these values so that they sum to 1 for each row
    normalized_row_sums = row_sums / np.sum(row_sums)

    return normalized_row_sums



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def karp_shortest_paths(n, distance_matrix):
    # Initialize parent array and dist array
    parent = [None] * n
    dist = [float('inf')] * n
    dist[0] = 0

    # Create list of all vertices
    vertices = list(range(n))
    heap = [[0, 0]]  # (dist, current_vertex)

    # Process vertices in order
    while heap:
        curr_dist, curr_vertex = heapq.heappop(heap)

        # If current vertex is not the starting point, skip it
        if curr_vertex!= 0:
            continue

        # Explore all neighbors of the current vertex
        for next_vertex in range(n):
            if distance_matrix[curr_vertex][next_vertex] < dist[next_vertex]:
                dist[next_vertex] = distance_matrix[curr_vertex][next_vertex]
                parent[next_vertex] = curr_vertex
                heapq.heappush(heap, [dist[next_vertex], next_vertex])

    return dist, parent



# Score: -20000

def weighted_path_count(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    edges = []

    # Add edges with zero weight for every pair of nodes
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i+1, num_nodes):
            edges.append((i, j, 1))
            edges.append((j, i, 1))  # Consider bidirectional edges for path count

    # Calculate the count of paths from each node
    path_count = [[0 for _ in range(num_nodes)] for _ in range(num_nodes)]
    for edge in edges:
        u, v, weight = edge
        for k in range(num_nodes):
            if (u, k) in path_count[v] or (k, v) in path_count[u]:
                path_count[u][k] += weight
                path_count[v][k] += weight

    # Create the heuristic matrix
    heuristics = [[0 for _ in range(num_nodes)] for _ in range(num_nodes)]
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:  # Paths from node i to node j are not considered
                heuristics[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] + path_count[i][j] / (distance_matrix[i][j] + 1)
    return heuristics

import numpy as np
def f_score_heuristics(distance_matrix, k=1000):
    """
    Computes the heuristic score for a given distance matrix.
    
    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (numpy.ndarray): A square matrix where distance_matrix[i, j] represents the distance between node i and node j.
    k (int): The number of k-shortest paths to consider. Higher k provides a more accurate estimate, but at a computational cost.
    
    Returns:
    numpy.ndarray: A matrix of the same shape as the input distance_matrix, containing heuristic scores.
    """
    
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize the heuristic score matrix with a large number
    heuristic_scores = np.full((n, n), np.inf)
    
    # Find the k-shortest paths for each node
    for _ in range(k):
        # Create a copy of the distance matrix to avoid modifying the original one
        dist_copy = np.copy(distance_matrix)
        for node in range(n):
            # Find the shortest paths from this node
            shortest_paths = shortest_path(dist_copy, node)
            if len(shortest_paths) > 1:
                # Calculate the average distance of the shortest paths
                avg_shortest_path_distance = np.mean(shortest_paths)
                # Update the heuristic score for this node
                heuristic_scores[node, :] = min(heuristic_scores[node, :], avg_shortest_path_distance)
                heuristic_scores[:, node] = min(heuristic_scores[:, node], avg_shortest_path_distance)
    
    # Ensure the diagonal elements are updated
    np.fill_diagonal(heuristic_scores, 0)
    
    return heuristic_scores

def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    betweenness_centrality_normalized = (betweenness_centrality - betweenness_centrality.min()) / (betweenness_centrality.max() - betweenness_centrality.min())
    
    # Assign higher undesirability score to more central edges
    heuristics_matrix = 1 - betweenness_centrality_normalized
    return heuristics_matrix

from sklearn.cluster import DBSCAN
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the distance_matrix is a 2D numpy array
    distance_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix)

    # Normalize the distance matrix to avoid bias towards large values
    min_dist = np.min(distance_matrix)
    max_dist = np.max(distance_matrix)
    normalized_dist = (distance_matrix - min_dist) / (max_dist - min_dist)

    # Apply DBSCAN for density-based clustering
    db = DBSCAN(eps=0.5, min_samples=5).fit(normalized_dist)

    # Create a heuristic score matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Assign scores based on cluster labels
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(i+1, distance_matrix.shape[0]):
            if db.labels_[i] == db.labels_[j]:  # If edges from the same cluster
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = 0
            else:  # If edges from different clusters
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = 1  # Higher undesirability, set to 1

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    """
    Calculate edge heuristics for a given distance matrix,
    using Kruskal's algorithm to find a subset of edges.
    """
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Kruskal's algorithm: sort edges by weight and add to the MST
    # if it doesn't form a cycle.
    mst = []
    parent = list(range(n))
    rank = [0] * n
    def find(x):
        if parent[x]!= x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]

    def union(x, y):
        rootX = find(x)
        rootY = find(y)
        if rootX == rootY:
            return False
        if rank[rootX] > rank[rootY]:
            parent[rootY] = rootX
        elif rank[rootX] < rank[rootY]:
            parent[rootX] = rootY
        else:
            parent[rootY] = rootX
            rank[rootX] += 1
        return True



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the negative distance matrix
    heuristic_matrix = -distance_matrix

    # Floyd-Warshall Algorithm to compute shortest paths
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                # If there's a shorter path via node k, update heuristic_matrix
                if distance_matrix[i, j] > distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j]:
                    heuristic_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j]

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
    import random
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np
    import random

    # Step 1: Convert distance matrix into a list of edges
    num_vertices = len(distance_matrix)
    edges = [(i, j, distance_matrix[i][j]) for i in range(num_vertices) for j in range(i+1, num_vertices)]

    def swap_edges(edges, e1, e2):
        nonlocal new_edges
        new_edges = edges[:]
        new_edges.remove(e1)
        new_edges.remove(e2)
        new_edges.append((e1[0], e2[1], e1[2] + e2[2]))
        new_edges.append((e1[1], e2[0], e1[2] + e2[2]))

    def improve(edges, new_edges):
        cost = 0
        for e in edges:
            cost += e[2]
        for e in new_edges:
            cost -= e[2]
        return cost

    # Step 2: Implement basic Lin-Kernighan heuristic
    max_iter = 1000
    current_edges = edges.copy()
    best_cost = improve(current_edges, current_edges)

    for _ in range(max_iter):
        # Step 3: Perform edge swaps
        e1 = random.choice(current_edges)
        e2 = random.choice(current_edges)
        swap_edges(current_edges, e1, e2)
        new_cost = improve(current_edges, current_edges)

        if new_cost < best_cost:
            best_cost = new_cost
            current_edges = current_edges.copy()  # Copy to preserve original edges

    # Step 4: Return the undesirability scores for each edge
    return [(e[1], best_cost - e[2]) for e in current_edges]
```

This heuristics() function will return a list of tuples, where each tuple contains an edge (a pair of vertices) and a float representing the heuristic undesirability score for including that edge in a solution.

The heuristic works by initially constructing an initial tour from the edges and then iteratively swapping pairs of edges to attempt to improve the total tour cost (sum of edge weights). This process mimics a local search strategy, similar to the Lin-Kernighan algorithm used for TSP.

The heuristic score is inversely proportional to the total weight of the selected edges in the solution, as less weight indicates higher desirability in the solution.

While the exact score achieved depends on the specific input data, this approach should generally outperform both the original functions by better exploring the solution space.



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Calculate Local Potential
    local_potential = np.diag(distance_matrix) + np.minimum(distance_matrix, np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1)).sum(axis=1)
    
    # Calculate Global Potential
    max_dist = np.max(distance_matrix, axis=0).reshape(-1, 1) + np.max(distance_matrix, axis=1)[np.newaxis, :]
    global_potential = local_potential + (max_dist - distance_matrix).sum(axis=0) + (max_dist - distance_matrix).sum(axis=1)

    # Normalize Global Potential to comparable scale as Local Potential
    global_potential = global_potential / np.max(global_potential)

    return np.concatenate([local_potential, global_potential], axis=1)

def weighted_node_heuristic(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize a matrix to hold the heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    
    # Calculate weighted node heuristics for each node
    for i in range(n):
        node_heuristic = 0
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:  # Skip self-comparison
                # Calculate a weighted sum of distances to neighboring nodes
                node_heuristic += distance_matrix[i, j] * (1 / np.linalg.norm(np.array(distance_matrix) - i * np.eye(n)))[j]
        heuristics_matrix[i] = node_heuristic  # Set the heuristic for node i
    
    return heuristics_matrix

# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def betweenness_centrality(distance_matrix):
    # This function calculates the betweenness centrality for each edge
    # in the graph represented by the distance matrix
    # The distance_matrix is expected to be a 2D numpy array where the value at
    # distance_matrix[i][j] is the weight of the edge between nodes i and j.
    # It returns a 2D numpy array with the same shape as distance_matrix
    # containing the betweenness centrality score for each edge.

    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    b = np.zeros((n, n))

    # Calculate the number of shortest paths from node i to all other nodes j
    def get_shortest_paths(source):
        num_nodes = n
        paths = np.zeros((num_nodes, num_nodes))
        paths[source][:] = 1  # Source node to itself has 1 path
        for _ in range(num_nodes - 1):
            for j in range(num_nodes):
                for k in range(num_nodes):
                    paths[j][k] = min(paths[j][k], paths[j][source] + distances_matrix[source][k])
        return paths

    # Compute the betweenness centrality for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i == j:
                continue  # Avoid counting paths from a node to itself

            # Find the number of shortest paths from i to j
            s_ij = np.sum(get_shortest_paths(i), axis=0)

            # Find the total number of paths from i to all nodes
            total_paths_i = np.sum(get_shortest_paths(i))

            # Calculate betweenness centrality
            betweenness_score = (total_paths_i - s_ij) / (total_paths_i - 1) if s_ij > 0 else 0
            b[i][j] = betweenness_score

    return b



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, reliability_matrix):
    # Calculate the minimum distance for each edge
    min_distance = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate the maximum reliability for each edge
    max_reliability = np.max(reliability_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Combine distance and reliability using a weighted average
    heuristic_scores = (1 - weight) * min_distance + weight * max_reliability
    weight = 0.5  # Adjust the weight between 0 and 1 to control the influence of reliability

    # Return the result as a matrix of the same shape as input
    return heuristic_scores

    num_edges_nonzero = np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix)

# Score: -20000
import heapq
def kruskal(n, edges):
    result = []
    edges.sort(key=lambda x: x[2]) # sort by edge weight
    visited = [False] * n
    parent = list(range(n))
    rank = [0] * n

    def find(x):
        if parent[x]!= x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]

    def union(x, y):
        rootX = find(x)
        rootY = find(y)
        if rootX == rootY:
            return

        if rank[rootX] > rank[rootY]:
            parent[rootY] = rootX
        elif rank[rootX] < rank[rootY]:
            parent[rootX] = rootY
        else:
            parent[rootY] = rootX
            rank[rootX] += 1

    for u, v, w in edges:
        if find(u)!= find(v):
            result.append((u, v, w))
            union(u, v)

    return result

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    edges = [(u, v, w) for u in range(n) for v in range(u+1, n) for w in distance_matrix[u][v]] # all edges, including self-loops
    mst_edges = kruskal(n, edges)
    mst_weight = sum(w for _, _, w in mst_edges)
    
    # Each edge not in MST contributes at least the weight of MST - its own weight to the total cost
    heuristics_matrix = [[max(0, distance_matrix[u][v] - w) for v in range(n)] for u in range(n)]
    for u, v, w in mst_edges:
        heuristics_matrix[u][v] = heuristics_matrix[v][u] = -w # if edge is in MST, add its negative weight to both ends
    for u in range(n):
        for v in range(u+1, n):
            heuristics_matrix[u][v] += distance_matrix[u][v]
            heuristics_matrix[v][u] += distance_matrix[u][v] # add remaining distance to both ends

    return heuristics_matrix
```

This function calculates the MST weight and then constructs a heuristic matrix where each edge's score is the difference between the edge's weight and the MST edge's weight (if it's in the MST), or just the edge's weight if it's not in the MST. This approach should better reflect the additional cost of including an edge in the solution beyond what's already necessary to form an MST.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a dense adjacency matrix from the distance matrix
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adjacency = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            adjacency[i, j] = adjacency[j, i] = distance_matrix[i, j]

    # Convert the adjacency matrix to a sparse matrix for efficiency
    graph = scipy.sparse.csgraph.adjacency_matrix(adjacency, format='csr')

    # Compute the minimum spanning tree
    mst = minimum_spanning_tree(graph)

    # Create a heuristics matrix where each element represents the cost of adding an edge
    heuristics_matrix = mst.copy()
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # If the edge is not part of the MST, add the potential cost
            if mst[i, j]!= 0:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = heuristics_matrix[j, i] = adjacency[i, j]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Construction Heuristic (Greedy Nearest Neighbor)
    tour = np.argmin(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    edge_costs = distance_matrix[np.arange(len(distance_matrix))[:, None], tour]

    # Step 2: Improvement Heuristic (Swapping Edges)
    for _ in range(100):
        # Create a copy of the current tour
        new_tour = tour.copy()

        # Try to reduce total cost by swapping edges
        for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
            for j in range(i + 1, len(distance_matrix)):
                cost_swap = edge_costs[i, j] + edge_costs[j, i]
                cost_keep = edge_costs[i, tour[i]] + edge_costs[tour[i], j] + edge_costs[j, tour[j]] + edge_costs[tour[j], i]

                if cost_swap < cost_keep:
                    new_tour[i:j+1] = tour[j:i-1:-1]

                    # Re-calculate new edge costs
                    new_edge_costs = distance_matrix[new_tour == np.argmin(distance_matrix[new_tour == np.argmin(distance_matrix[new_tour])][0], axis=1)]
                    edge_costs = new_edge_costs

                # Stop early if no better solution found
                if np.sum(new_edge_costs) > np.sum(edge_costs):
                    break

        # If a better solution was found, update the tour
        if np.sum(new_edge_costs) < np.sum(edge_costs):
            tour = new_tour

    return edge_costs



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.linalg import eigs
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # 1. Average number of neighbors per edge
    num_neighbors = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)

    # 2. Eigenvector centrality of the adjacency matrix
    adj_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    np.fill_diagonal(adj_matrix, 0)  # Self-connections not allowed
    adj_matrix[np.triu_indices(n, 1)] = 1  # Create adjacency matrix
    _, _ = eigs(adj_matrix, k=1, which="LM")  # Compute largest eigenvector
    centrality = np.abs(eigs(adj_matrix, k=1, which="LM")[0])

    # Combine the two scores
    heuristic_matrix = num_neighbors[:, np.newaxis] + centrality[:, np.newaxis]

    # Set values to zero for self-connections (i.e., diagonal elements)
    np.fill_diagonal(heuristic_matrix, 0)

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Compute the degree of each node (number of edges connected)
    node_degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)

    # Calculate the weighted score for each edge
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # Avoid adding edges to the same node (cycle)
            if i == j:
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = 1e10
            else:
                # Higher degree nodes might be more critical
                edge_weight = 1 / node_degrees[i] if i!= j else 1e10  # Symmetry for edges to the same node
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = 1 / distance_matrix[i, j] * edge_weight

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def kruskal_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Sort all edges in non-decreasing order
    sorted_edges = np.argsort(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Initialize a new matrix to store the heuristic scores
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Iterate over sorted edges
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # If the edge is not already included, add its heuristic score
            if sorted_edges[i][j]!= -1:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = heuristics_matrix[j, i] = distance_matrix[i, j]
            else:
                # If not included, include it with its heuristic score
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = heuristics_matrix[j, i] = distance_matrix[i, j] + (i + j) * 2  # (i + j) * 2 is an arbitrary growth factor
                break
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_count, node_degree, total_degree):
    """
    heuristics function calculates a heuristic score for each edge in a distance matrix.
    The score indicates how undesirable it is to include the edge in a solution.
    The function uses a weighted combination of distance and additional factors.

    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (numpy.ndarray): A 2D square matrix of distances between nodes.
    edge_count (int): The total number of edges.
    node_degree (numpy.ndarray): A 1D array representing the degree (number of edges connected to each node).
    total_degree (int): The total degree (sum of all edge degrees)

    Returns:
    numpy.ndarray: A 2D array of heuristic scores, the same shape as the distance_matrix.
    """

    # Compute the total weight for the distance factor
    total_weight = edge_count * 2  # Double the count to emphasize the importance of distance

    # Calculate the weighted distance factor
    weighted_distance = distance_matrix * total_weight

    # Calculate the node degree factor
    node_degree_factor = (1 - node_degree / total_degree)  # Decrease the score as degree increases

    # Combine weighted distance and node degree factors
    heuristic_scores = weighted_distance + node_degree_factor

    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the average distance for each node
    avg_distances = [sum(distance_matrix[i]) / (len(distance_matrix) - 1) for i in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    
    # Calculate the frequency of connections for each node (sum of distances to all other nodes)
    connection_counts = [sum(distance_matrix[i]) for i in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    
    # Create a heuristic matrix with the above information
    heuristic_matrix = [[avg_distances[i] / connection_counts[i] if connection_counts[i] > 0 else 0 for i in range(len(distance_matrix))] for _ in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import shortest_path
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Compute node degrees
    node_degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Step 2: Compute shortest path lengths
    _, shortest_paths = shortest_path(csgraph=distance_matrix, directed=False)
    
    # Step 3: Construct the undesirability matrix
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    undesirability_matrix = -np.ones(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i, num_nodes):
            # Compute edge weight as a function of node degrees and shortest path
            edge_weight = -1 * (node_degrees[i] + node_degrees[j]) + (shortest_paths[i, j] - distance_matrix[i, j])
            
            # Ensure non-negative values (as a heuristic)
            undesirability_matrix[i, j] = max(edge_weight, 0)
    
    return undesirability_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np
    from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
    
    # Convert distance matrix to adjacency matrix
    adj_matrix = distance_matrix.to_numpy()
    # Ensure adjacency matrix is symmetric
    np.fill_diagonal(adj_matrix, 0)
    
    # Convert adjacency matrix to a sparse matrix for efficient computation
    adj_sparse = csgraph.sparse_from_adjacency_matrix(adj_matrix)
    
    # Compute the Minimum Spanning Tree (MST)
    mst = minimum_spanning_tree(csgraph=adj_sparse, return_cost=True)
    
    # Weight edges by their position in the MST (higher cost, less important)
    cost_weights = mst[1]
    
    # Create a new matrix where each edge's value is its position in the cost-weighted MST
    heuristics_matrix = np.full_like(adj_matrix, np.sum(cost_weights))
    
    # Normalize the heuristics_matrix by dividing by the maximum value in each row
    heuristics_matrix = heuristics_matrix / np.max(heuristics_matrix, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def manhattan_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Checking for valid input
    assert distance_matrix.ndim == 2, "Input matrix should be 2D"
    n_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Calculate Manhattan distance heuristic
    manhattan_dist = np.sum(np.abs(np.arange(n_vertices)[:, np.newaxis] - np.arange(n_vertices)[np.newaxis, :]), axis=2)
    
    # Scale the heuristic to ensure it is comparable in magnitude to the distance matrix
    max_dist = np.max(distance_matrix)
    normalized_heuristics = manhattan_dist / max_dist
    
    return normalized_heuristics

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:  # Don't consider the diagonal elements
                path_cost = np.sum(distance_matrix[i]) + np.sum(distance_matrix[j]) - 2 * distance_matrix[i][j]
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = max(path_cost - 1, 0)  # Adjust for a non-zero score

    # Adjust higher-diagonal elements to discourage inclusion of more distant edges
    for k in range(1, n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(i+1, n):
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = min(heuristic_matrix[i][j], heuristic_matrix[i][k] + heuristic_matrix[k][j] - 1)

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def dijkstra(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize distances from the source node (0) to all other nodes as infinite
    distances = [float('inf')] * n
    distances[0] = 0

    # Priority queue to store (distance, node) tuples
    queue = [(0, 0)]

    while queue:
        current_distance, current_node = heapq.heappop(queue)

        if current_distance > distances[current_node]:
            continue

        for neighbor, edge_weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_node]):
            if edge_weight > 0:
                distance = current_distance + edge_weight

                # If a shorter path to the neighbor is found, update the distance
                if distance < distances[neighbor]:
                    distances[neighbor] = distance
                    heapq.heappush(queue, (distance, neighbor))

    return distances



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def closeness_centrality(adjacency_matrix):
    degrees = np.sum(adjacency_matrix, axis=0)
    closeness = 1 / np.sum(np.sqrt(adjacency_matrix * (degrees[None, :] - adjacency_matrix)), axis=0)
    return closeness



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from random import random
def spatial_heuristic_with_stochasticity(distance_matrix):
    # Identify the indices of non-zero elements in the distance matrix (potential edges)
    edge_indices = np.nonzero(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Loop over each non-zero element
    for i, j in zip(*edge_indices):
        # Considering local connectivity, ignore edges connected to an already connected node
        if distance_matrix[i, j] < distance_matrix[i, i] + distance_matrix[j, j]:
            # Add a random factor for stochasticity, between 0 and 1, where 1 means always ignore
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = (random() * 2 - 1) * (distance_matrix[i, j] - distance_matrix[i, i] - distance_matrix[j, j])
            # Also consider the possibility of ignoring a connection based on the global connectivity
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = max(0, heuristic_matrix[i, j])
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import math
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    max_distance = max(max(row) for row in distance_matrix)
    min_distance = min(min(row) for row in distance_matrix)
    
    heuristics_matrix = [[max_distance/min_distance * (d1 - d2) for d2 in row] for d1, row in zip(range(n), distance_matrix)]
    
    return heuristics_matrix
