import numpy as np
def all_pairs_shortest_paths(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    dist = distance_matrix.copy()
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                dist[i][j] = min(dist[i][j], dist[i][k] + dist[k][j])
    return dist



# Score: -20000
import heapq
import random
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_vertices = len(distance_matrix)
    cumulative_weights = [0] * num_vertices
    total_weight = sum(distance_matrix)

    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(num_vertices):
            if i!= j:
                weight = distance_matrix[i][j]
                cumulative_weights[i] += weight
                cumulative_weights[j] += weight

    heuristic_matrix = [[(cumulative_weights[i] + cumulative_weights[j]) / (total_weight) for j in range(num_vertices)] for i in range(num_vertices)]

    def dijkstra(graph, start):
        distances = [float('inf')] * len(graph)
        distances[start] = 0
        priority_queue = [(0, start)]

        while priority_queue:
            current_distance, current_vertex = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)

            if current_distance > distances[current_vertex]:
                continue

            for neighbor, edge_weight in enumerate(graph[current_vertex]):
                if edge_weight > 0:
                    old_distance = distances[neighbor]
                    new_distance = current_distance + edge_weight

                    if new_distance < old_distance:
                        distances[neighbor] = new_distance
                        heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (new_distance, neighbor))
                        heuristic_matrix[current_vertex][neighbor] += new_distance

    dijkstra(distance_matrix, 0)

    # Weighted random selection to get final heuristic
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(num_vertices):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] /= sum(heuristic_matrix[i])
    
    return heuristic_matrix
```

This function first calculates the cumulative weights for each vertex based on the input distance matrix. Then, it applies Dijkstra's algorithm to calculate the shortest distances from each vertex to all others. The heuristic matrix is filled based on these shortest distances and cumulative weights.

Finally, a weighted random selection is performed over the heuristic matrix. This step ensures that edges with higher cumulative weights (which correspond to higher distances) are less likely to be selected, thereby reflecting higher undesirability.

This method should deliver a more accurate estimation of edge undesirability, potentially yielding a higher score.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the shape of the matrix
    m, n = distance_matrix.shape

    # Initialize a new matrix for heuristic values
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((m, n))

    # Calculate the normalized sum of distances for each edge
    edge_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)

    # Normalize by the maximum edge sum
    max_edge_sum = np.max(edge_sums)
    heuristic_matrix = edge_sums / max_edge_sum

    # Add a time-decay factor for future impact
    time_decay = 0.5  # You can adjust this value
    for i in range(m):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] *= time_decay ** np.abs(i - j)  # Distance impact
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] *= time_decay ** distance_matrix[i, j]  # Distance value

    return heuristic_matrix

from scipy.sparse import csr_matrix
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the input is a csr_matrix to maintain the adjacency structure
    distance_matrix = csr_matrix(distance_matrix)
    
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Initialize the result matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    
    # Calculate average distance
    avg_distance_matrix = distance_matrix.sum(axis=1) / distance_matrix.sum(axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Calculate degree
    degree_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix.sum(axis=0)).reshape(-1)
    
    # Calculate triadic closure (common neighbors)
    # Using adjacency matrix for this computation (since distance_matrix only provides unweighted edges)
    adj_matrix = csr_matrix(adjacency_matrix_creation(distance_matrix))
    triadic_closure = np.array(adj_matrix.sum(axis=1)).reshape(-1, 1)
    triadic_closure_matrix = csr_matrix(np.tile(triadic_closure, (1, n))).T
    
    # Define edge weights based on the heuristics
    heuristic_matrix[distance_matrix > 0] = (avg_distance_matrix[distance_matrix.indices, distance_matrix.indptr] + 
                                               degree_matrix[distance_matrix.indices] + 
                                               triadic_closure_matrix[distance_matrix.indices, distance_matrix.data] + 
                                               degree_matrix[distance_matrix.data])
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the total sum of distances
    total_distance = np.sum(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the average distance
    avg_distance = total_distance / (distance_matrix.shape[0] * distance_matrix.shape[1])
    
    # Calculate the variance of distances
    variance_distance = np.var(distance_matrix, axis=None)
    
    # Calculate the edge density (undesirability score)
    # Edge density is a function of average and variance
    undesirability_score = (1 / avg_distance) * (variance_distance / np.mean(distance_matrix))
    
    # Return as a distance matrix of the same shape
    return undesirability_score



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the dimensions of the matrix
    num_nodes, _ = distance_matrix.shape

    # Step 1: Compute the shortest distances from each node to all others (Floyd-Warshall algorithm)
    # This will help us find the nearest unconnected neighbors
    dist_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    for k in range(num_nodes):
        for i in range(num_nodes):
            for j in range(num_nodes):
                dist_matrix[i][j] = min(dist_matrix[i][j], dist_matrix[i][k] + dist_matrix[k][j])

    # Step 2: Calculate the cost to connect each node to its nearest unconnected neighbor
    # This is the minimum of its own distance and the shortest distance to an unconnected neighbor
    cost_to_connectivity = np.minimum(dist_matrix, np.min(dist_matrix, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis])

    return cost_to_connectivity



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def betweenness_centrality(adj_matrix):
    n = adj_matrix.shape[0]
    path_counts = np.ones((n, n))  # Initialize with 1s
    short_paths = np.zeros((n, n))  # Initialize as zero

    for _ in range(1, n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if adj_matrix[i, j] > 0:
                    u, v = np.where(adj_matrix[i] == 1)
                    if len(u) > 0 and len(v) > 0:
                        path_counts[i, j] += short_paths[v[0], u[0]]
                        short_paths[i, j] = min(short_paths[i, j], path_counts[i, j])

    betw_centrality = np.sum(path_counts) / np.sum(short_paths)
    return betw_centrality

import numpy as np
def weighted_travelling_salesman_heuristic(distance_matrix):
    # Compute row sums as initial edge weights
    row_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Add bias term to prevent trivial solution (all shortest paths)
    max_row_sum = np.max(row_sums)
    if max_row_sum == 0:
        max_row_sum = 1  # to avoid division by zero
    heuristic_matrix = row_sums + max_row_sum

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def dijkstra(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize distances and visited status
    dist = [float('inf')] * n
    dist[0] = 0
    visited = [False] * n
    pq = [(0, 0)]  # (priority, current_node)

    while pq:
        priority, current_node = heapq.heappop(pq)

        if visited[current_node]:
            continue

        visited[current_node] = True

        for neighbor, weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_node]):
            if not visited[neighbor] and weight!= float('inf'):
                new_dist = dist[current_node] + weight
                if new_dist < dist[neighbor]:
                    dist[neighbor] = new_dist
                    heapq.heappush(pq, (new_dist, neighbor))

    return dist



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, nodes_count):
    # Get the dimensions of the distance matrix
    row, col = distance_matrix.shape
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Function to calculate a weighted farness based on distance and local connectivity bias
    def weighted_farness(d, n1, n2):
        # Assume a constant for local connectivity bias, LCB
        LCB = 1  # Adjust this value to control the impact of local connectivity
        
        # Calculate the difference in the number of edges connected to the nodes
        edge_diff = int(distance_matrix[n1, :].sum()) - int(distance_matrix[:, n2].sum())
        
        # Calculate the weighted farness
        return d + (LCB * edge_diff)
    
    # Calculate and populate the heuristic matrix
    for i in range(row):
        for j in range(col):
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = weighted_farness(distance_matrix[i][j], i, j)
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # First, we normalize the distance matrix.
    D = distance_matrix / np.max(distance_matrix)

    n = D.shape[0]
    E = np.zeros((n, n))

    # Step 1: Create residual capacities
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            E[i, j] = D[i, j] - D[i, j] * (D[i, j] <= D[j, i])

    # Step 2: Relax edges
    for _ in range(n - 1):
        E_copy = E.copy()
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                # Find the minimum flow from i to j
                if i == n - 1 and j == 0:
                    # Terminal nodes, no need for relaxation
                    continue
                u = j
                while E[u, i] > 0 and E[u, j] < E[i, j]:
                    u = np.argmin([E[u, k] for k in range(n) if k!= i and k!= u])
                if E[u, j] < E[i, j]:
                    # Update the residual capacity
                    E[i, j] -= E[u, j]
                    E[u, j] = np.inf
                    E[u, i] += E[j, u]
                    E[j, u] = 0

    # Step 3: Return the final flow matrix as heuristic scores
    return E



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def triangle_inequality_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]  # number of nodes
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Get all neighboring nodes k
            k_indices = np.where(distance_matrix[i, :] < np.inf)[0]
            
            # Only consider valid neighbors (not including i or j)
            k_indices = k_indices[(k_indices!= i) & (k_indices!= j)]
            
            if len(k_indices) > 0:
                # Find the minimum distance through any k
                min_through_k = min([distance_matrix[k, j] for k in k_indices])
                
                # Update the heuristic for the edge (i, j)
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = min(distance_matrix[i, j], distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j] - min_through_k)
    
    return heuristic_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import networkx as nx
    import numpy as np
    
    # Create a NetworkX graph
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Find the minimum spanning tree (MST)
    MST = nx.minimum_spanning_tree(G)
    
    # Convert MST to a list of edges
    MST_edges = list(MST.edges())
    
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize a matrix to store heuristic values
    heuristic_values = np.zeros((n, n))
    
    # Add edges to the heuristic matrix
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # Check if adding an edge (i, j) to the MST would form a cycle of size < n/2
            if nx.has_path(G, i, j) and nx.has_path(G, j, i) and sum(G.get_edge_attributes(i, j, 'weight')) + sum(G.get_edge_attributes(j, i, 'weight')) < n/2:
                heuristic_values[i][j] = 0  # Edge (i, j) should be included
            else:
                heuristic_values[i][j] = np.inf  # Edge (i, j) should not be included
    
    return heuristic_values



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import diameter
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Compute the adjacency matrix from distance matrix
    adj_matrix = np.pad(distance_matrix, ((1, 0), (0, 1)), mode='constant') > 0

    # Calculate the Relaxed Steinhaus Center
    dist_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            dist_matrix[i, j] = dist_matrix[i, j] if adj_matrix[i, j] else np.inf  # Prevent self-loops
        center = np.min(dist_matrix, axis=1)
        center_index = np.argmin(center)
        dist_matrix[center_index, :] = np.inf
        dist_matrix[:, center_index] = np.inf

    # Compute minimum spanning tree
    mst = minimum_spanning_tree(csgraph=dist_matrix)

    # Calculate diameter of the MST
    diameter_val = diameter(csgraph=mst)

    # Normalize diameter to get a centrality measure
    centrality_scores = np.power(diameter_val, -1)
    centrality_scores /= np.sum(centrality_scores)  # Normalize to sum up to 1

    # Combine with distance matrix
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    heuristics_matrix[np.arange(n), np.arange(n)] = centrality_scores

    return heuristics_matrix

    # Normalize the degree centrality scores to sum up to 1 for each row
    normalized_degree = degree_centrality / np.sum(degree_centrality)

# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)  # number of vertices
    path_weights = np.zeros((n, n))  # initialize the path weights matrix

    # Compute the path weights from each vertex to all others
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            for k in range(n):
                if i!= k and j!= k:
                    path_weights[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j]  # add edge weight to total path weight

    # Normalize the path weights to make them comparable
    path_weights = np.minimum(path_weights, distance_matrix)  # prevent unrealistically high weights

    # The heuristics score for each edge is the normalized path weight through that edge
    heuristics_matrix = np.where(distance_matrix > path_weights, path_weights, distance_matrix)

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get dimensions of the distance matrix
    rows, cols = distance_matrix.shape
    
    # Initialize heuristic matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((rows, cols))
    
    # Calculate heuristic value for each edge
    for i in range(rows):
        for j in range(cols):
            # Calculate in-degree and out-degree for nodes i and j
            in_degree_i = sum(distance_matrix[i] < distance_matrix[j])
            out_degree_j = sum(distance_matrix[i] < distance_matrix[j])
            
            # Use a more sophisticated weighting scheme (e.g., linear combination)
            heuristic_value = 0.6 * in_degree_i + 0.4 * out_degree_j
            
            # Assign the calculated heuristic value
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = heuristic_value
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def reliability_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the mean and standard deviation for each row (edge)
    mean_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    std_distances = np.std(distance_matrix, axis=1)

    # Initialize the result matrix
    result_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Populate the result matrix
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # Assign higher penalty to edges closer but with higher variance
            result_matrix[i, j] = (distance_matrix[i, j] - mean_distances[i])**2 / std_distances[i]**2

    return result_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get number of nodes and edges
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    edges = [(dist, i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)]
    
    # Sort edges in non-decreasing order of weight (distance)
    edges.sort()

    # Kruskal's algorithm
    result = [0] * (n*(n-1)//2)
    rank = [0] * n
    size = [1] * n
    component_count = n

    def find(x):
        if x!= parent[x]:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]

    def union(x, y):
        root_x = find(x)
        root_y = find(y)
        if root_x!= root_y:
            if size[root_x] < size[root_y]:
                x, y = y, x
            parent[root_y] = root_x
            size[root_x] += size[root_y]

    parent = list(range(n))

    for dist, u, v in edges:
        if find(u)!= find(v):
            result[(-dist, u, v)] = 1
            union(u, v)
            component_count -= 1

            # Steering factor
            if component_count < n - 1:
                steering_factor = (n - component_count) / n
                result[(-dist, u, v)] *= steering_factor

    return result
```

This function uses Kruskal's algorithm to construct a minimum spanning tree from the given distance matrix. It assigns a heuristic score to each edge that is the product of its weight and a steering factor. The steering factor discourages the inclusion of edges when the network is nearly connected (low density), favoring edges that break up clusters or connect distant parts of the graph. This approach should generally produce better results than the simple distance matrix, as it considers the overall structure of the network.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, network_structure, traffic_data):
    """
    Computes heuristic scores for edges based on distance, network connectivity, and traffic data.

    Parameters:
    distance_matrix: 2D numpy array - represents the distance between all pairs of nodes.
    network_structure: 2D numpy array (boolean) - indicates whether the connection between nodes is present.
    traffic_data: 2D numpy array (float) - represents traffic conditions for each edge.

    Returns:
    heuristic_matrix: 2D numpy array - indicates the undesirability of each edge.
    """

    # Edge weights considering distance, network connectivity, and traffic
    edge_weights = np.minimum(distance_matrix, network_structure) + traffic_data

    # Adjust weights based on network connectivity
    adjacency_matrix = np.outer(network_structure.sum(axis=0), network_structure.sum(axis=1))
    connected_pairs = np.tril_indices(edge_weights.shape[0], -1)
    edge_weights[connected_pairs] *= adjacency_matrix[connected_pairs]

    # Ensure positive heuristic weights
    heuristic_matrix = np.maximum(edge_weights, 1)

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Calculate the average distance of neighboring nodes for each node
    avg_neighbor_distance = np.apply_along_axis(lambda x: np.mean(x[x!= i]), axis=1, arr=distance_matrix, i=np.arange(distance_matrix.shape[0]))
    
    # Step 2: Calculate the difference in distance to each of its neighbors
    distance_differences = distance_matrix - avg_neighbor_distance[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Step 3: Normalize the differences by dividing by the average distance of all neighbors
    normalization_factor = np.mean(distance_differences, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]
    normalized_differences = distance_differences / normalization_factor
    
    # Step 4: Combine the three factors into a single heuristic score
    heuristic_scores = distance_matrix + normalized_differences + np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import heapq
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Floyd-Warshall algorithm to compute shortest paths between all pairs of nodes
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    shortest_paths = distance_matrix.copy()
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                shortest_paths[i, j] = min(shortest_paths[i, j], shortest_paths[i, k] + shortest_paths[k, j])
    
    # Step 2: Create a priority queue (min-heap) to store edges, where priority is determined by the potential cost to reach the last node
    # Each edge (i, j) is represented as a tuple (i, j, current_cost + shortest_path from i to j)
    edge_costs = []
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):  # Only consider edges between different nodes
            current_cost = shortest_paths[i, j]
            shortest_path_from_i = shortest_paths[i, n-1]  # Assume the last node is 'n-1'
            total_cost = current_cost + shortest_path_from_i
            edge_costs.append((i, j, total_cost))
    
    # Step 3: Use heapq to sort the edges by their total cost
    heapq.heapify(edge_costs)

    # Step 4: Create a matrix to store the undesirability of each edge
    undesirability = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Pop elements from the priority queue and assign their costs to the corresponding edges in the undesirability matrix
    for _ in range(n):
        _, _, current_cost = heapq.heappop(edge_costs)
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(i+1, n):
                undesirability[i, j] = current_cost
                undesirability[j, i] = current_cost

    return undesirability

import numpy as np
def floyd_warshall(distance_matrix):
    num_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    for k in range(num_vertices):
        for i in range(num_vertices):
            for j in range(num_vertices):
                distance_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    return distance_matrix

import numpy as np
from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import cosine_similarity
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # First, compute the weighted degree centrality for each node
    degree_centrality = dict(zip(range(len(distance_matrix)),
                                     np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)))
    
    # For each edge (i, j), calculate cosine similarity between the degree vectors of (i)'s and (j)'s neighbors
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        neighbors_i_degrees = [degree_centrality[j] for j in range(len(distance_matrix)) if distance_matrix[i, j]!= 0]
        neighbors_j_degrees = [degree_centrality[j] for j in range(len(distance_matrix)) if distance_matrix[j, i]!= 0]
        
        # Normalize the vectors and calculate cosine similarity
        norm_neighbors_i = np.array([np.sqrt(d) for d in neighbors_i_degrees])
        norm_neighbors_j = np.array([np.sqrt(d) for d in neighbors_j_degrees])
        similarity_ij = cosine_similarity([norm_neighbors_i, norm_neighbors_j])[0][1]
        
        heuristics_matrix[i, j] = similarity_ij
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Convert the distance matrix into a list of edges
    edges = [(distance_matrix[i][j], i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)]
    # Initialize the MST using Prim's algorithm
    mst = []
    visited = [False] * n
    parent = [-1] * n
    min_edge = float('inf')

    while edges:
        # Select the smallest edge
        cur_edge = heapq.heappop(edges)
        if not visited[cur_edge[1]] and not visited[cur_edge[2]]:
            mst.append(cur_edge)
            visited[cur_edge[1]] = visited[cur_edge[2]] = True

            # Relaxation: For each neighbor of the newly added vertex
            for i, edge in enumerate(edges):
                if visited[i] and i not in mst:
                    new_edge = (edge[0], mst[-1][1], i)
                    if new_edge[0] < parent[i]:
                        parent[i] = new_edge[0]
                        edges[i] = new_edge

    # Construct the heuristic score matrix
    heuristic_scores = [[min(distance_matrix[u][v], distance_matrix[v][u]) for v in range(n)] for u in range(n)]

    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize Chebyshev polynomial matrix
    T = np.eye(n)
    
    # Compute Chebyshev polynomials
    for i in range(1, n):
        T = 2 * T @ T - np.eye(n)
        
    # Normalize the polynomial matrix to match the original distance matrix
    T = T / np.sum(T, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Create heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.abs(T - distance_matrix)
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Create a new matrix where each entry is the negative logarithm of the corresponding distance
    neg_log_distances = -np.log(distance_matrix + 1e-8)
    
    # We add a small constant to avoid taking the log of zero
    # This operation helps to dampen the effect of very large distances
    # and makes sure that small distances have a more significant influence
    
    # To further encourage paths with more intermediate nodes, we sum the neg_log_distances along the rows
    # This reflects the notion that edges leading to a significant number of nearby points might be more useful
    heuristics_matrix = np.sum(neg_log_distances, axis=1)
    
    return heuristics_matrix

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Calculate topological sort and indegree
    indegree = [0]*n
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i):
            if distance_matrix[i][j]!= 0:
                indegree[j] += 1

    # Create a list to hold edges with negative weight
    edges_with_negatives = []
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i][j] < 0 and indegree[i] > 0 and indegree[j] == 0:
                edges_with_negatives.append((i, j))

    # Calculate heuristics score for each edge
    heuristics_matrix = [[0]*n for _ in range(n)]
    for i, j in edges_with_negatives:
        heuristics_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
        heuristics_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[j][i]

    # Add more weight to edges with lower indegree (higher importance)
    for i in range(n):
        heuristics_matrix[i][i] = indegree[i]

    # Normalize the matrix
    max_score = max(max(row) for row in heuristics_matrix)
    return [max_score if heuristics_matrix[i][j] == 0 else heuristics_matrix[i][j]/max_score for i in range(n) for j in range(n)]

import numpy as np
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Betweenness Centrality
    betweenness = nx.betweenness_centrality(G)
    
    # Closeness Centrality
    closeness = nx.closeness_centrality(G)
    
    # Eigenvector Centrality (graph Laplacian)
    laplacian_eigenvector = np.linalg.eigvalsh(nx.laplacian_matrix(G))
    
    # Degree of each node
    degrees = np.array(list(G.degree()))
    
    # Combine into a single matrix
    result_matrix = np.zeros((distance_matrix.shape[0], distance_matrix.shape[0]))
    
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(i+1, distance_matrix.shape[0]):
            # Edge (i, j)
            result_matrix[i, j] = -distance_matrix[i, j] * (betweenness[i] + betweenness[j])
            result_matrix[j, i] = result_matrix[i, j]

            result_matrix[i, j] += closeness[i] + closeness[j] / degrees[i] / degrees[j]
            result_matrix[j, i] += result_matrix[i, j]

            result_matrix[i, j] += laplacian_eigenvector[0] * (1 / degrees[i]) * (1 / degrees[j])
            result_matrix[j, i] += result_matrix[i, j]

    return result_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.spatial.distance import squareform
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree, kernighan_lin
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to a sparse graph using squareform
    graph = squareform(1 - distance_matrix)

    # Perform graph partitioning
    new_order, _ = kernighan_lin(graph)
    
    # Calculate local densities for each node
    local_densities = np.array([np.count_nonzero(graph[i, :]) / (np.count_nonzero(graph) - 1) for i in range(len(graph))])

    # Initialize heuristics matrix with zeros
    heuristics = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Assign heuristics based on graph partitioning
    for i in range(len(heuristics)):
        for j in range(i + 1, len(heuristics)):
            if new_order[i] < new_order[j]:
                u, v = new_order[i], new_order[j]
            else:
                u, v = new_order[j], new_order[i]

            heuristics[u, v] = local_densities[u] + local_densities[v] - 2 * local_densities[np.argmin(np.linalg.norm(graph[u, :], axis=0))] * local_densities[np.argmin(np.linalg.norm(graph[v, :], axis=0))]

    # Ensure heuristics are non-negative
    heuristics = np.maximum(0, heuristics)

    return heuristics

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the shortest path for each vertex (excluding itself)
    shortest_path = np.min(distance_matrix[:, 1:], axis=0) - distance_matrix[:, 0]
    
    # Create a heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.full(distance_matrix.shape, np.inf)
    
    # Assign heuristic values for each edge
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i == j:
                # For edges within the same vertex, no impact
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 0
            else:
                # For edges (i, j) between two different vertices
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] + shortest_path[j]
    
    return heuristics_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_weights):
    """
    This function takes a distance_matrix and edge_weights as input,
    and returns a heuristic matrix that indicates the undesirability
    of including each edge in a solution.
    
    :param distance_matrix: 2D list representing the distances between nodes
    :param edge_weights: 1D list representing the weight of each edge
    :return: 2D list representing the heuristic matrix
    """
    # Calculate total cost for each edge
    total_cost = [[dist * weight for dist in row] for row in distance_matrix]
    
    # Calculate the sum of total costs per node
    node_sums = [sum(cost) for cost in total_cost]
    
    # Create a heuristic matrix where each entry is the total cost of its corresponding edge
    heuristic_matrix = [[cost if i == j else -cost for i, cost in enumerate(row)] for j, row in enumerate(total_cost)]
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.optimize import linear_sum_assignment
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Add a small constant to the diagonal to avoid zero division
    distance_matrix += np.finfo(float).eps
    
    # Create a new matrix to store intermediate costs
    intermediate_cost_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Compute the minimum additional cost to pair nodes
    _, _ = linear_sum_assignment(intermediate_cost_matrix)
    
    # Subtract the minimum additional costs from the original distance matrix
    heuristic_scores = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_scores -= np.array(intermediate_cost_matrix[np.newaxis, :]).repeat(len(distance_matrix), axis=0)
    heuristic_scores -= np.array(intermediate_cost_matrix[:, np.newaxis]).repeat(len(distance_matrix), axis=1)
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the number of nodes
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the distance matrix
    heuristic_matrix = [[0.0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Calculate the weighted sum
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Avoid diagonal elements (self-loop) by assigning a large value
            if i == j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = float('inf')
            else:
                # Assign a smaller value for diagonal elements to prioritize existing edges
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], 5.0)
                # Use a higher weight for larger distances, with a maximum weight of 5.0
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] *= (distance_matrix[i][j] / 5.0)
    
    # Normalize the heuristic values to ensure they are between 0 and 1 (for better comparison)
    for i in range(n):
        heuristic_matrix[i][i] = 0.0  # Set diagonal elements to 0
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] /= sum(heuristic_matrix[i])
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the shape of the matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with the same shape
    heuristics_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Compute initial distance heuristics
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
            heuristics_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j] # To make it symmetric
    
    # Compute connectivity heuristics
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(i+1, n):
                # Add 1 to the heuristic for each direct connection from node k to node i or j
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] += (distance_matrix[k][i] + distance_matrix[k][j] > 0)
                # Add 1 to the heuristic for each direct connection from node i or j to node k
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] += (distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[j][k] > 0)
    
    # Normalize the heuristics to range [0, 1]
    max_heuristic = max([max(row) for row in heuristics_matrix])
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] /= max_heuristic
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def connectivity_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same dimensions as the distance matrix
    heuristic_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Use a simple flood-fill algorithm (similar to Dijkstra's) to find potential short paths
    def flood_fill(source):
        queue = [(source, 0)]  # (node, total_distance)
        visited = set()
        
        while queue:
            node, total_dist = queue.pop(0)
            if node not in visited:
                visited.add(node)
                for neighbor in range(len(distance_matrix)):
                    if distance_matrix[node][neighbor] < float('inf'):
                        queue.append((neighbor, total_dist + distance_matrix[node][neighbor]))
        return visited
    
    # Calculate the heuristic score for each edge
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(i+1, len(distance_matrix)):
            # If nodes i and j are not directly connected, consider the shortest path that includes both
            if i not in flood_fill(j) or j not in flood_fill(i):
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]  # Direct edge weight
                heuristic_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j]  # Edge symmetry
            else:
                # Calculate a potential reduction in total distance
                reduction = min(distance_matrix[i][neighbor] for neighbor in flood_fill(j) if i!= neighbor)
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] + reduction
                heuristic_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j] + reduction  # Edge symmetry
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, weights=[0.4, 0.3, 0.2, 0.1]):
    """
    Calculate a heuristic score for each edge in the distance matrix.

    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (numpy.ndarray): A square matrix of shape (n, n) where n is the number of nodes.
                                   The matrix should be symmetric and contain non-negative distances.
    weights (list, optional): A list of 4 weights for the different aspects of edge undesirability. 
                             Defaults to [0.4, 0.3, 0.2, 0.1].

    Returns:
    numpy.ndarray: A matrix of the same shape as the input, representing the heuristic score for each edge.
    """
    
    # Check if input is a valid square matrix
    if distance_matrix.shape!= (distance_matrix.shape[0], distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        raise ValueError("Input matrix should be a square matrix.")
    
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Compute scores
    direct_cost = distance_matrix
    indirect_cost = np.minimum(distance_matrix[:, :-1], distance_matrix[:, 1:])  # Neighboring elements
    edge_frequency = np.full(distance_matrix.shape, 1/n)  # Assuming all edges appear once
    edge_length = np.full(distance_matrix.shape, np.sqrt(distance_matrix))  # Euclidean length of edges

    # Combine scores
    heuristic_scores = (
        weights[0] * direct_cost +
        weights[1] * np.minimum(indirect_cost, distance_matrix) +
        weights[2] * edge_frequency +
        weights[3] * edge_length  # Euclidean distance is used for simplicity; other measures could be employed
    )

    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a binary adjacency matrix to represent the graph
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    graph = np.eye(n, n, k=-1)
    
    # Initialize the MST with Kruskal's algorithm
    mst = []
    uf = UnionFind(n)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i][j] < 0:  # Assuming negative values indicate edges
                if uf.find(i)!= uf.find(j):
                    mst.append((i, j, distance_matrix[i][j]))
                    graph[i][j] = 0  # Connect the vertices
                    graph[j][i] = 0  # Reflect the connection
    
    # Calculate initial heuristic score
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if graph[i][j]:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = float('inf')
                heuristic_matrix[j][i] = float('inf')  # Reflect the connection
                # Add penalty for the edge's weight and the number of connected vertices in MST
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][j]
                heuristic_matrix[j][i] += distance_matrix[i][j]
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] += uf.size() - 1  # Penalize edge if it connects two distinct components in the MST
                heuristic_matrix[j][i] += uf.size() - 1  # Reflect the penalty
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute average distance from each node to all others
    avg_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Apply congestion factors
    congestion_factor = np.array([avg_distances[i] for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0])])
    congestion_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    congestion_matrix *= congestion_factor[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Apply lower bound to decrease distances between nodes with high congestion
    lower_bound = 0.1 * congestion_factor  # You may adjust this value based on your needs
    congestion_matrix[congestion_matrix > lower_bound] = lower_bound
    
    return congestion_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristics_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Floyd-Warshall algorithm to calculate the worst-case travel time from i to j via k
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                # Current path weight is through node k: distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j]
                new_cost = distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[k][j]
                
                # If adding the edge (i, j) improves the total travel time,
                # update the heuristic_matrix[i][j]
                if new_cost < heuristics_matrix[i][j]:
                    heuristics_matrix[i][j] = new_cost
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def edge_betweenness_centrality(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to adjacency matrix
    adjacency_matrix = np.where(distance_matrix < 0, 1, 0)
    
    # Calculate edge betweenness centrality
    num_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    betweenness = np.zeros(num_vertices * (num_vertices - 1) // 2)
    
    for edge in range(num_vertices * (num_vertices - 1) // 2):
        u, v = divmod(edge, num_vertices)
        num_paths = 0
        for i in range(num_vertices):
            if u!= i and v!= i:
                path_count = np.count_nonzero(np.all(adjacency_matrix[np.arange(num_vertices)!= i, :] == np.array([0, 1]), axis=0))
                if path_count > 1:
                    betweenness[edge] += (path_count / (num_vertices - 1)) * (1 / (adjacency_matrix[u, i] + adjacency_matrix[i, v]))
    
    return betweenness



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the number of nodes and the shape of the distance matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    _, m = distance_matrix.shape  # m is the number of edges

    # Create a new matrix to store undesirability scores
    undesirability_scores = [[0] * m for _ in range(n)]

    # Iterate through each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):  # Consider edges only between different nodes
            # If the distance is shorter, the edge is considered more undesirable
            if distance_matrix[i, j] < distance_matrix[i, k] and distance_matrix[i, j] < distance_matrix[j, k] for some k in range(n):
                undesirability_scores[i][j] = distance_matrix[i, j] * 1.1  # Increase by a factor to make shorter edges more undesirable
            else:
                undesirability_scores[i][j] = distance_matrix[i, j]  # Undesirability score is the distance itself

    return undesirability_scores

import numpy as np
from scipy.stats import entropy
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Normalize the distance matrix
    norm_dist = distance_matrix / np.max(distance_matrix)
    
    # Create a weighted adjacency matrix
    weighted_adj = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            weighted_adj[i, j] = 1 / (1 + distance_matrix[i, j])
    
    # Compute the second order matrix
    second_order_matrix = weighted_adj ** 2
    
    # Calculate entropy of second-order matrix
    entropy_value = entropy(second_order_matrix.flatten(), base=2)
    
    # Normalize entropy by the maximum entropy possible
    max_entropy = np.log2(distance_matrix.shape[0]) * distance_matrix.shape[1]
    heuristics_matrix = entropy_value / max_entropy
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Compute local density
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    density_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i, n):
            # Neighbors indices in a spherical cap
            neighbors = np.where(pdist(distance_matrix[i:j+1].reshape(-1, 1), 'euclidean') < (distance_matrix[i, j] * 0.5))[0] + i
            density_matrix[i, j] = len(neighbors) / (j - i + 1)
            density_matrix[j, i] = density_matrix[i, j]  # Symmetric matrix

    # Step 2: Calculate average distance heuristic
    avg_distance_matrix = np.mean(distance_matrix)

    # Combine local density and average distance
    result_matrix = avg_distance_matrix + 10 * density_matrix  # Adjust the scaling factor for optimal performance

    return result_matrix

import numpy as np
def cef(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the degree of each node
    degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate CEF for each edge
    cef_matrix = np.multiply(degrees, distance_matrix)
    
    return cef_matrix

import numpy as np
def weighted_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the cost for each edge using the inverse of the distance
    # This means, shorter distances have lower 'cost'
    edge_costs = 1 / distance_matrix  # Edge costs are reciprocal of distances

    # Normalize the costs so that they sum up to 1. This means each edge contributes equally to the total cost
    total_cost = np.sum(edge_costs)
    edge_costs /= total_cost

    return edge_costs

import numpy as np
def sparsity_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the number of non-zero elements (edges) in the distance matrix
    num_edges = np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the sum of all distances (total weight)
    total_weight = np.sum(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the sparsity score, which is the total weight divided by the number of edges
    sparsity_score = total_weight / num_edges
    
    # Create a new distance matrix where each edge has the sparsity score as its value
    return sparsity_score * distance_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance matrix into a sparse adjacency matrix
    adjacency_matrix = csgraph_betweenness(distance_matrix, symmetric_paths=True, directed=False)
    
    # Calculate the betweenness centrality scores
    betweenness_centrality = csgraph_betweenness(adjacency_matrix, symmetric_paths=True, directed=False)[0]
    
    # Normalize the scores to be between 0 and 1
    max_centrality = np.max(betweenness_centrality)
    normalized_centrality = betweenness_centrality / max_centrality
    
    # Create the heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.array(normalized_centrality).reshape(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    return heuristics_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np
    
    # Calculate the degree of each vertex (number of edges connected to it)
    vertex_degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Calculate the average distance of each vertex to all other vertices
    avg_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Create a heuristic matrix.
    # Each cell (i,j) contains a negative value if adding an edge between vertices i and j would be undesirable,
    # and a positive value if it would be desirable.
    heuristic_matrix = np.where(distance_matrix > 1, # Assuming cost > 1 for an undesirable edge
                               -vertex_degrees[np.arange(len(distance_matrix))][distance_matrix[np.arange(len(distance_matrix)), np.arange(len(distance_matrix)) > 1]] +
                               avg_distances[np.arange(len(distance_matrix))][distance_matrix[np.arange(len(distance_matrix)), np.arange(len(distance_matrix)) > 1]] - 1,  # Subtract 1 to make it a desirable score for undesirable edges
                               0)
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import heapq
from collections import defaultdict
import numpy as np
def mst_kruskal(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    edges = [(distance_matrix[i][j], i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)]
    heapq.heapify(edges)
    parent = list(range(n))
    mst = [0] * n

    while edges:
        cost, u, v = heapq.heappop(edges)
        if parent[u]!= parent[v]:
            mst[u] = mst[v] = 1
            parent[v] = parent[u]
            for w in range(n):
                if parent[w] == parent[v]:
                    heapq.heappush(edges, (distance_matrix[v][w], v, w))

    return mst

    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]  # Number of nodes
    # Frequency count of each edge
    edge_freq = np.sum(distance_matrix!= 0, axis=1)  # 1 for non-zero distances, 0 otherwise

    # Create a weight vector where lower frequencies get lower weights
    freq_weights = 1 / (edge_freq + 1)  # Adding 1 in the denominator to avoid division by zero
    freq_weights /= np.sum(freq_weights)  # Normalize to get probabilities

    # Combine the frequency weights with the original distances
    weighted_distances = distance_matrix * freq_weights

    return weighted_distances

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Add diagonal elements to the distance matrix as 0 (self-distance)
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    distance_matrix = [0] + [0] * (n - 1) + [0]

    # Calculate estimated cost-to-come (ECTC)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            distance_matrix[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][0]

    return distance_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Calculate average distance from each node to all others
    avg_distance = distance_matrix.mean(axis=1).A1
    
    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with same dimensions as the distance_matrix
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Fill the heuristics matrix with CESP values
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        heuristics_matrix[i] += avg_distance[i]
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:
                heuristics_matrix[i] += distance_matrix[i, j]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the diagonal of the matrix to be the sum of all distances
    # This value represents the total cost if we ignore all edges.
    total_cost = np.diag(distance_matrix)
    
    # Create an identity matrix for the number of vertices, with the sum of all edge weights as the initial heuristic value for each edge.
    # This represents our initial guess of the cost to reach a vertex from itself.
    identity_matrix = np.eye(distance_matrix.shape[0]) * total_cost
    
    # Update each vertex's heuristic value based on the neighboring vertices' heuristic values
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i!= j:
                # Calculate the heuristic for the edge (i,j) based on the probability of it being part of an optimal path
                heuristic_value = -np.log(distance_matrix[i, j] / (total_cost - identity_matrix[i, :].sum() + distance_matrix[i, :].sum() - distance_matrix[j, :].sum()))
                identity_matrix[i, j] = heuristic_value
    
    return identity_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def centrality_score(adj_matrix):
    # Calculate the adjacency matrix
    n = adj_matrix.shape[0]
    centrality = np.zeros((n, n))

    # Calculate shortest path distances using Floyd-Warshall algorithm
    dist = adj_matrix.copy()
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                dist[i, j] = min(dist[i, j], dist[i, k] + dist[k, j])

    # Calculate centrality scores (sum of distances from each node to all other nodes)
    for i in range(n):
        centrality[i, i] = 0  # Ignore self-loops
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                centrality[i, j] = dist[i, j]

    return centrality

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    edges_scores = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    # Sort edges in ascending order
    sorted_edges = np.argsort(distance_matrix, axis=None)
    
    # Calculate the number of edges already included in the MST
    m = 0
    
    # Iterate over sorted edges
    for i in sorted_edges:
        # Get the current edge's distance
        current_edge = distance_matrix[i]
        
        # If adding this edge doesn't form a cycle, include it
        if m < n - 1 and not any(current_edge <= edges_scores[j]):
            edges_scores[i] = current_edge
            m += 1
            
    return edges_scores



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Priority queue to store (cost, edge) tuples. Cost = (weight + factor).
    priority_queue = [(distance_matrix[i][j] + factor, (i, j)) for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)]
    heapq.heapify(priority_queue)  # Convert list to a heap for efficient extraction of minimum.

    # To keep track of the best edge in terms of total cost
    best_edge = (0, None)

    # Process each edge
    while priority_queue:
        cost, (u, v) = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)

        # If the current edge is better than the previously known best, update the best.
        if cost < best_edge[0]:
            best_edge = (cost, (u, v))

        # Push the opposite edge onto the priority queue.
        if u!= v:
            cost = distance_matrix[u][v] + factor
            heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (cost, (v, u)))

    # The best_edge tuple contains the minimum total cost and the corresponding edge.
    # To get the heuristic matrix, we divide this total cost by 2 (assuming each edge is bidirectional).
    heuristic_matrix = [[best_edge[0] / 2] * n for _ in range(n)]
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate local distortion
    local_distortion = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]
    dist_sq_diff = np.sum((distance_matrix - local_distortion)**2, axis=1)

    # Calculate global context
    total_edges = distance_matrix.size // 2  # Assuming it's a square matrix

    # Combine local distortion and global context into a single heuristic score
    heuristic_matrix = -dist_sq_diff - total_edges

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
from collections import defaultdict
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Build a graph from the distance matrix
    graph = defaultdict(list)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                graph[i].append((j, distance_matrix[i][j]))
    
    # Initialize the capacity matrix with infinite capacity, except for self-loops
    capacity = [[float('inf')] * n for _ in range(n)]
    for i in range(n):
        capacity[i][i] = 0
    
    # Initialize the flow matrix with 0
    flow = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    def bfs(start):
        queue = [(0, start)]
        visited = set()
        while queue:
            (cost, current) = heapq.heappop(queue)
            visited.add(current)
            if current == n - 1:
                return cost
            for neighbor, weight in graph[current]:
                if neighbor not in visited and capacity[current][neighbor] > 0:
                    heapq.heappush(queue, (cost + weight, neighbor))
        return float('inf')



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * num_nodes for _ in range(num_nodes)]
    
    # First, consider the edge weights
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i+1, num_nodes):
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
            heuristic_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j]  # Symmetry
    
    # Second, incorporate neighborhood analysis (for simplicity, we consider only adjacent nodes here)
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:
                neighbors_sum = sum([distance_matrix[i][k] for k in range(num_nodes) if k!= j])
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] += (neighbors_sum - distance_matrix[i][j]) * 0.5  # Adjustment factor
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Initialize a new matrix for heuristics
    heuristic_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Compute matrix B (matrix of pairwise distances)
    matrix_B = np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1) + distance_matrix
    
    # Compute matrix D (matrix of transitive distances)
    matrix_D = np.linalg.matrix_power(matrix_B, 2) - matrix_B
    
    # Use Floyd-Warshall to compute shortest paths
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if distance_matrix[i, j] > matrix_D[i, k] + matrix_D[k, j]:
                    heuristic_matrix[i, j] = matrix_D[i, k] + matrix_D[k, j]
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def floyd_warshall(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                distance_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    return distance_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def local_global_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Number of nodes in the graph
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Pre-compute the average distance to all other nodes (local density)
    local_density = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)

    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate the heuristic score for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i, n):  # Loop only for non-duplicate edges
            # Skip diagonal elements
            if i == j:
                continue

            # Local Density Component
            local_contribution = -1 * distance_matrix[i, j] / local_density[i]

            # Global Connectivity Component
            global_contribution = 0.5 * (n - 1) * (n - 2) / distance_matrix[i, j]  # Assuming average degree of the graph

            # Combine local and global components with a weighted sum
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = local_contribution + global_contribution

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize a matrix to store the f-scores (heuristics)
    f_scores = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Apply Nearest Neighbor (NN) move
    for i in range(n):
        f_scores[i] = distance_matrix[i][i]

    # Apply 2-opt move to iteratively improve the solution
    for _ in range(1000):  # Arbitrarily set the number of iterations
        improved = False
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(i+1, n):
                # Swap the i-th and j-th elements
                temp = distance_matrix[i][j]
                distance_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[j][i]
                distance_matrix[j][i] = temp

                # Calculate the new f-score
                new_f_score = 0
                for k in range(n):
                    new_f_score += min(distance_matrix[i][k], distance_matrix[j][k])

                # If the new f-score is lower than the old one, update the matrix
                if new_f_score < f_scores[i] + f_scores[j]:
                    f_scores[i] = new_f_score
                    f_scores[j] = new_f_score
                    improved = True

        # If no improvement, the current solution is the best we can do
        if not improved:
            break

    return f_scores



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_vertices = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * num_vertices for _ in range(num_vertices)]
    
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(num_vertices):
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]  # Euclidean distance
            
            # Manhattan Distance Heuristic
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] += abs(i - j)  # Horizontal movement
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] += abs(distance_matrix[i][0] - distance_matrix[j][0])  # Vertical movement
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the number of nodes (n)
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros, same shape as distance_matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate expected cost change for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):  # Consider only edges between distinct nodes to avoid redundancy
            # Calculate the maximum potential saving by excluding this edge
            max_save = distance_matrix[i, j]
            for k in range(n):
                if k!= i and k!= j:  # Avoid including node i or j in the potential saving calculation
                    max_save = max(max_save, distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j] - distance_matrix[i, j])
            
            # Assign heuristic value as the maximum potential saving
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = max_save
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def entropy(array):
    """ Calculate the entropy of a given array """
    probs = array / array.sum()
    return -np.sum(probs * np.log2(probs))

# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def structural_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Number of nodes in the graph
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Calculate graph density
    density = np.sum(distance_matrix) / (num_nodes * (num_nodes - 1))
    
    # Calculate connectedness (number of connected components)
    # We use the reverse of the distance matrix and find the connected components using Depth-First Search (DFS)
    reverse_dist_matrix = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    connected_components = len(np.unique(np.concatenate(np.where(reverse_dist_matrix!= np.inf, 
                                                np.array([np.searchsorted(reverse_dist_matrix, 
                                                                               np.inf) + 1, 
                                                                -1]), 
                                                axis=1))))

    # Create an edge undesirability score matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)

    # Populate heuristics matrix based on edge weights and connectedness
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i+1, num_nodes):
            # If nodes i and j are connected
            if connected_components > 1:
                # Calculate the weighted sum of neighbors' distances
                weight_sum = np.sum(distance_matrix[i, :]) + np.sum(distance_matrix[j, :])
                # If this edge is heavier than its neighbors, increase its undesirability score
                if distance_matrix[i, j] > weight_sum:
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] = (1 - density) * (1 - weight_sum / np.sum(distance_matrix[i, :]))
                    heuristics_matrix[j, i] = heuristics_matrix[i, j]  # Assuming undirected graph

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the degree of each node (number of edges connected to it)
    node_degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate the sum of edge weights for each node
    edge_sum_per_node = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Create a new distance matrix, where the diagonal represents node degrees
    new_distance_matrix = np.diag(node_degrees)
    
    # Add the sum of edge weights for each node to the diagonal
    new_distance_matrix[np.arange(len(node_degrees)), node_degrees] = edge_sum_per_node
    
    # To discourage overly complex structures, we'll introduce a 'complexity' term
    # This term will be proportional to the square of the sum of distances from the node to all others
    complexity_factor = np.sum(new_distance_matrix, axis=1) ** 2
    
    # Normalize the complexity factor by dividing by the node degrees
    complexity_factor = complexity_factor / node_degrees[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Combine the normalized complexity factor with the original distance matrix
    heuristics_matrix = new_distance_matrix + complexity_factor
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the matrix to keep track of the Steinhaus-Johnson-Trotter permutations
    perm = [[i, j] for i in range(n) for j in range(i + 1, n)]
    # Initialize the current permutation and its cost
    current_permutation, current_cost = 0, 0

    # Function to calculate the Steinhaus-Johnson-Trotter move
    def steinhaus_johnson_trotter_move(i):
        j = i
        while j > 0 and distance_matrix[j - 1] <= distance_matrix[j]:
            j -= 1
        if j == 0: return None  # No swap needed
        while perm[current_permutation][0] > j:
            current_permutation = (current_permutation + 1) % len(perm)
        current_permutation = (current_permutation + 1) % len(perm)
        perm[current_permutation], (j, perm[j]) = (j, perm[j]), perm[current_permutation]
        return i, j

    # Perform the Steinhaus-Johnson-Trotter permutation and keep track of the cost
    while perm:
        i, j = steinhaus_john_trotter_move(perm[current_permutation])
        if i is not None:
            current_cost += distance_matrix[i] - distance_matrix[j]
        else:
            break
        current_permutation = (current_permutation + 1) % len(perm)

    # The matrix of undesirability scores for each edge
    heuristics_matrix = [[distance_matrix[i] + distance_matrix[j] - current_cost for j in range(n)] for i in range(n)]
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def chebyshev_bound(dist_matrix):
    """Estimate upper and lower bounds based on Chebyshev's inequality."""
    n = len(dist_matrix)
    max_dist = np.max(np.max(dist_matrix, axis=0))  # Max distance in the worst case
    min_dist = np.min(np.min(dist_matrix, axis=1))  # Min distance in the worst case
    return max_dist, min_dist



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def novel_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    
    # Compute the sum of reciprocals of diagonal elements
    diag_sum = np.sum(np.reciprocal(distance_matrix.diagonal()))
    
    # Compute heuristics for off-diagonal elements
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                # Penalize larger distances
                penalty = np.exp(-(distance_matrix[i, j] - np.mean(distance_matrix.diagonal())) ** 2)
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 1 / (distance_matrix[i, j] * (1 / diag_sum + penalty))
            else:
                # Special case for diagonal elements: no penalty
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 1 / (distance_matrix[i, j] * (1 / diag_sum))
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, importance_vector):
    # Calculate decay factor based on distance
    decay_factor = 1 / (distance_matrix + 1)

    # Apply decay to importance vector
    decayed_importance = importance_vector * decay_factor

    # Normalize decayed importance vector
    total_importance = decayed_importance.sum()
    if total_importance!= 0:
        return decayed_importance / total_importance

def heuristics(distance_matrix, terrain_data):
    """
    heuristics() function for more sophisticated edge selection.

    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (list of lists): The distance matrix for all edges.
    terrain_data (list of tuples): A list of tuples where each tuple contains:
                                    (1) start coordinate (x, y),
                                    (2) end coordinate (x, y),
                                    (3) terrain type (e.g.,'mountain', 'river', 'city')

    Returns:
    list of lists: A matrix of heuristic scores for each edge.
    """

    def get_terrain_cost(start, end):
        """
        Calculate the cost of traversing a segment based on terrain.

        Parameters:
        start (tuple): Starting coordinates.
        end (tuple): Ending coordinates.

        Returns:
        float: The cost based on terrain type.
        """
        x1, y1 = start
        x2, y2 = end

        if terrain_data[x1][y1][2] =='mountain':
            return 2.0  # Assume double the distance due to mountain's difficulty
        elif terrain_data[x1][y1][2] == 'river':
            return 1.5  # Assume 1.5 times the distance due to river's friction



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to adjacency list
    adj_list = {(u, v): d for u, u_dists in enumerate(distance_matrix) for v, d in enumerate(u_dists)}

    # Calculate weighted heuristic
    weighted_heuristic = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for u, v_dists in adj_list.items():
        for v, d in v_dists.items():
            # For direct connections (lower Dijkstra's score), use Dijkstra
            if u < v:
                weighted_heuristic[u, v] = d
            # For indirect connections (higher Manhattan score), use Manhattan
            else:
                weighted_heuristic[u, v] = d  # Assuming Manhattan distance
                for w, w_dist in adj_list.get((u, v), {}).items():
                    weighted_heuristic[u, v] += abs(w - v)

    return weighted_heuristic



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the inverse of the diagonal elements (distance to itself)
    diag_inv_distance = 1 / distance_matrix.diagonal()

    # Compute the sum of each row (distance to all other nodes)
    row_sums = distance_matrix.sum(axis=1)

    # Apply the inverse distance to each element in the matrix
    heuristic_matrix = diag_inv_distance - row_sums

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # We start by initializing a matrix with zeros, where the entry at index (i, j) represents the potential cut-value
    # of edge (i, j).
    
    cut_values = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # For each edge (i, j), we calculate its contribution to the cut-value
    # as the minimum distance from i to the other nodes (i.e., the other nodes' indices minus i)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            cut_values[i, j] = min(distance_matrix[i, k] for k in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]) if k!= j)

    # Here, we've created a heuristic that evaluates each edge by its potential to disrupt the network.
    # The edges with lower cut-values represent those that are more critical and should be avoided.
    return cut_values

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance matrix to a sparse matrix (if it's not already)
    sparse_matrix = sparse_from_dense(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the minimum spanning tree using csr_matrix from scipy
    mst = minimum_spanning_tree(sparse_matrix)
    
    # Initialize a matrix of the same shape as the input to store our heuristics
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    # Iterate over each edge (i, j) in the distance matrix
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(i+1, distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # If the edge is not in the MST, its cost (heuristic) is the distance
            if mst[i, j] == 0:
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]
            else:
                # If the edge is in the MST, its cost (heuristic) is the weight of the edge in MST
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = mst[i, j]
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, importance_factor):
    # Input validation
    if distance_matrix.shape!= importance_factor.shape:
        raise ValueError("The shape of distance_matrix and importance_factor must match.")

    # Calculate the negative of the distance matrix as a heuristic score
    score_matrix = -distance_matrix

    # Apply importance bias
    for i in range(len(score_matrix)):
        for j in range(i + 1, len(score_matrix)):
            score_matrix[i][j] += importance_factor[i] + importance_factor[j]

    return score_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_importance):
    """
    distance_matrix: 2D list representing the distances between nodes
    edge_importance: 2D list representing the relative importance of each edge

    Returns:
    A cost matrix where each entry represents the combined cost of including an edge,
    considering both its distance and the importance of the edge.
    """
    # Multiply the distance matrix by the edge importance matrix
    weighted_distance_matrix = [
        [distance * importance for distance in row] for row in distance_matrix
    ]

    # Sum up each row to get the total cost for each edge
    cost_matrix = [sum(row) for row in weighted_distance_matrix]

    return cost_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)  # assuming a square matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [0] * n  # initialize the output matrix

    # First pass: fill heuristics_matrix with negative of diagonal elements (smaller diagonal = smaller edge)
    for i in range(n):
        heuristics_matrix[i] = -distance_matrix[i][i]

    # Second pass: for each pair of vertices (i, j)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:  # exclude self-loops
                heuristics_matrix[i] += distance_matrix[i][j]  # sum of all non-diagonal elements that vertex i contributes to

    # normalize heuristics_matrix (optional, to ensure non-negative values)
    heuristics_matrix = [max(0, h) for h in heuristics_matrix]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Create an adjacency matrix
    adj_matrix = np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1)
    
    # Initialize minimum distances to the root for each node
    dist_to_root = np.full(n, float('inf'))
    
    # Initialize the current path with the root node
    current_path = np.zeros(n, dtype=int)
    current_path[0] = 0
    
    # MST Heuristic
    for _ in range(n - 1):
        # Find the minimum cost edge from the current path to unvisited nodes
        min_edge = np.min(adj_matrix[current_path])
        min_edge_node = np.where(adj_matrix[current_path] == min_edge)[0][0]
        
        # Update the current path and minimum distance to the root
        current_path[min_edge_node] = min_edge_node
        dist_to_root[min_edge_node] = min_edge
    
    # Return the heuristic values
    return dist_to_root



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def dijkstra(graph, start):
    """
    Function to perform Dijkstra's shortest path algorithm
    """
    N = len(graph)
    dist = np.inf * np.ones(N, dtype=np.float32)
    dist[start] = 0
    prev = np.empty(N, dtype=np.int32)
    queue = [(0, start)]
    
    while queue:
        d, u = queue.pop(0)
        if d!= dist[u]:
            continue
        for v, weight in enumerate(graph[u]):
            if weight and dist[v] > dist[u] + weight:
                dist[v] = dist[u] + weight
                prev[v] = u
                queue.append((dist[v], v))
    
    return dist, prev



# Score: -20000

def triangle_inequality_violations(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # For each edge (i, j), calculate the difference between the direct distance and the distance via any third vertex
    violations = [[abs(distance_matrix[i][j] - min(distance_matrix[i][k] for k in range(n) if k!= i and k!= j)) for k in range(n) if k!= i and k!= j] for i in range(n)]
    
    # Add these values to the original matrix
    result = [[distance_matrix[i][j] + v for v in vi] for i, vi in enumerate(violations)]
    
    return result

import numpy as np
def flow_based_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the distance matrix is a 2D numpy array
    distance_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the capacity (1/distance) for each edge
    capacity = 1 / distance_matrix
    
    # Ensure the capacity matrix is of the same shape as the input distance matrix
    capacity = np.repeat(capacity[:, :, np.newaxis], capacity.shape[1], axis=2)
    
    # Return the capacity matrix, which will serve as the heuristic
    return capacity

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a graph from the distance matrix
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the effective resistance (inverse of squared shortest path)
    effective_resistances = np.linalg.inv(nx.shortest_path_length(G)**2)
    
    # Ensure the result is of the same shape as the input matrix
    return effective_resistances

    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np
    
    # Calculate edge importance based on local connectivity
    local_importance = np.diag(distance_matrix)  # Diagonal elements represent each node's intrinsic importance
    local_importance = 1 / local_importance  # Inverse to make importance higher for less connected nodes
    
    # Calculate global connectivity and path efficiency
    connectivity = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)  # Sum of distances from each node
    path_efficiency = 1 - (distance_matrix / np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]).mean(axis=0)  # Path efficiency between all pairs of nodes
    
    # Combine local and global importance
    total_importance = local_importance * path_efficiency
    
    # Normalize importance for edges
    max_importance = np.max(total_importance)
    heuristics_matrix = total_importance / max_importance
    
    return heuristics_matrix
