from community import community_louvain
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the affinity matrix
    affinity = 1 - distance_matrix
    
    # Perform Louvain community detection
    communities = community_louvain.best_partition(affinity)
    
    # Initialize the output matrix
    result_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)

    # Assign undesirability scores based on community structure
    for node in range(affinity.shape[0]):
        for neighbor in range(node + 1, affinity.shape[0]):
            community_node = communities[node]
            community_neighbor = communities[neighbor]
            
            # If the nodes belong to different communities
            if community_node!= community_neighbor:
                # Increase the undesirability score
                result_matrix[node, neighbor] = result_matrix[neighbor, node] = 100  # Arbitrary high score

    return result_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure distance_matrix is a square numpy array
    distance_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix)
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the result matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristics_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Implement Kruskal's Algorithm for TSP
    # Sort all edges (i,j) in ascending order based on their weights
    edges = np.array(np.ndindex(distance_matrix.shape)).reshape(-1, 2)
    edges = edges[np.argsort(distance_matrix[edges[:, 0], edges[:, 1]])]
    
    # Initialize a forest (set of disjoint groups), initially each vertex is its own group
    forest = list(range(n))
    
    # Number of edges in the TSP
    m = n - 1
    
    # Result matrix: for each edge, store the largest distance among its endpoints (i.e., the edge itself)
    for edge in edges:
        u, v = edge
        if len(set([u, v])) < 2:  # If the edge connects the same vertex
            continue
        
        # U and V are in different trees
        if not (forest[u] == forest[v]):
            # Find the forest containing the smaller element
            smaller = min(forest[u], forest[v])
            
            # Add the edge to the result matrix (heuristics_matrix)
            heuristics_matrix[u, v] = distance_matrix[u, v]
            
            # Make the smaller element the root of the larger tree
            forest[forest == smaller] = max(u, v)
    
    # If the number of edges is not m, we need to find the shortest cycle
    cycle_length = m - len(forest)
    if cycle_length > 0:
        # Find the smallest unvisited edge that forms a cycle
        cycle_edges = [e for e in edges if distance_matrix[e[0], e[1]] > 0 and forest[e[0]] == forest[e[1]]]
        if cycle_edges:
            heuristics_matrix[cycle_edges[0][0], cycle_edges[-1][1]] += cycle_length
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
from numpy.random import randint
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Build Minimum Spanning Tree (MST)
    mst = minimum_spanning_tree(csgraph=distance_matrix)
    mst_edges = np.argwhere(mst)

    # Step 2: Calculate nearest neighbor heuristic
    nn_heuristic = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix, dtype=float)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        nn_indices = np.argmin(distance_matrix[i, :])
        nn_heuristic[i, nn_indices] = distance_matrix[i, nn_indices]
        nn_heuristic[nn_indices, i] = distance_matrix[nn_indices, i]

    # Step 3: Combine heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = nn_heuristic + distance_matrix - mst_edges[:, 0] * mst_edges[:, 1]

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Assuming the input is a square matrix representing a graph where the diagonal is zero
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Compute the sum of squares of distances (to penalize long paths)
    distance_sum_of_squares = np.sum(distance_matrix**2)
    # Compute the degree (number of edges connected to each node)
    degree = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Create a new matrix where each entry is a combination of distance_sum_of_squares and degree
    heuristics_matrix = distance_sum_of_squares + degree
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def frequency_based_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    total_sum = sum(distance_matrix)  # Sum of all edge weights
    edge_frequencies = {(i, j): count for i, row in enumerate(distance_matrix) for j, count in enumerate(row) if i < j}  # Frequency of each edge
    
    # Normalize frequencies
    total_frequency = sum(edge_frequencies.values())
    normalized_frequencies = {k: v / total_frequency for k, v in edge_frequencies.items()}
    
    # Assign heuristic scores
    heuristic_matrix = [[1 - (v / total_sum) for v in normalized_frequencies.values()] for _ in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def modified_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]

    # Apply triangle inequality
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            for k in range(j+1, n):
                if distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[j][k] <= distance_matrix[i][k]:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][k] = max(heuristic_matrix[i][k], distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[j][k])

    # Decompose the problem for better efficiency
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(k):
            for j in range(i, k):
                if heuristic_matrix[i][j] < heuristic_matrix[i][k] + heuristic_matrix[k][j]:
                    # Update heuristic matrix based on the found better path
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] = heuristic_matrix[i][k] + heuristic_matrix[k][j]

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the input is a square matrix
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    assert n == distance_matrix.shape[1], "The input must be a square distance matrix."

    # Compute the capacity matrix
    capacity = np.eye(n) - distance_matrix

    # Compute the residual matrix (a distance matrix representing remaining flow)
    residual = np.minimum(distance_matrix, capacity)

    # Number of vertices
    num_vertices = n
    # Number of edges
    num_edges = num_vertices * (num_vertices - 1) // 2

    # Initialize the heuristic matrix (desirability of each edge)
    heuristic = np.zeros((num_edges, 1))

    # Iterate over each vertex pair
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(i+1, num_vertices):
            # Edge from i to j
            edge_ij = j * num_vertices + i
            # Edge from j to i (symmetric graph)
            edge_ji = i * num_vertices + j

            # Heuristic score for edge (i, j)
            # This score will be higher if the flow between i and j is large
            # and there are many other edges with high flow
            heuristic[edge_ij] = capacity[i, j] * residual[i, j]
            heuristic[edge_ji] = capacity[j, i] * residual[j, i]

            # If edge (i, j) has flow (residual), it disrupts the flow
            # between vertices i and j
            heuristic[edge_ij] *= residual[i, j]
            heuristic[edge_ji] *= residual[j, i]

    # Normalize the heuristic matrix to make scores comparable
    heuristic /= np.sum(heuristic)

    return heuristic



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, centrality_weights=0.3, avg_dist_weight=0.5, var_weight=0.2):
    N, _ = distance_matrix.shape

    # Calculate centrality for each node
    centrality = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    centrality = centrality / np.sum(centrality)  # Normalize centrality to sum to 1

    # Calculate average distance to each node
    avg_dist = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)

    # Calculate weighted sum with uncertainty
    heuristics_matrix = centrality_weights * centrality + \
                         avg_dist_weight * avg_dist + \
                         var_weight * np.std(distance_matrix, axis=0)

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = [[0]*n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Perform Bellman-Ford Algorithm to detect negative cycles
    for _ in range(n-1):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = min(heuristic_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][j])
                for k in range(n):
                    if i!= j and distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j] < heuristic_matrix[i][j]:
                        heuristic_matrix[i][j] = min(heuristic_matrix[i][j], heuristic_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    
    # If there are negative weight cycles, set the heuristic values to large negative number
    if any(heuristic_matrix[i][j] < 0 for i in range(n) for j in range(n)):
        # Assign a large negative number to the heuristic matrix
        max_value = max(max(row) for row in heuristic_matrix)
        heuristic_matrix = [[max_value - abs(value) for value in row] for row in heuristic_matrix]
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculating the Floyd-Warshall algorithm to get all pair shortest paths
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    shortest_paths = distance_matrix.copy()
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                shortest_paths[i, j] = min(shortest_paths[i, j], shortest_paths[i, k] + shortest_paths[k, j])

    # Applying the Christofides-Serdyukov algorithm to get an approximate TSP tour and its edge weights
    # The Christofides-Serdyukov algorithm finds a 1.5-approximation for the TSP problem
    # We'll ignore the tour and focus on the edge weights as our heuristic values
    n_approx = int(1.5 * n)
    unvisited = set(range(n))
    tour = []
    edge_weights = []

    while len(tour) < n_approx:
        u = min(unvisited, key=lambda x: shortest_paths[x, -1])
        tour.append(u)
        unvisited.remove(u)
        for v in unvisited:
            if shortest_paths[u, v] + shortest_paths[-1, v] == shortest_paths[u, -1]:
                edge_weights.append(shortest_paths[u, v])
                break

    heuristic_values = np.array(edge_weights)

    return heuristic_values



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def negative_weight_cycle(distance_matrix):
    # Using Bellman-Ford algorithm to detect negative-weight cycles
    num_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    dist = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    for _ in range(num_vertices):
        # Relax all edges
        for u in range(num_vertices):
            for v, weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[u]):
                if weight!= float('inf') and dist[u] + weight < dist[v]:
                    dist[v] = dist[u] + weight

    # Check for negative-weight cycles
    for u in range(num_vertices):
        for v, weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[u]):
            if weight!= float('inf') and dist[u] + weight < dist[v]:
                return True  # Negative-weight cycle detected



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
def quality_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    """
    This function calculates a heuristic score for each edge in a graph,
    based on both the direct distance and the quality of the connection.

    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (numpy.ndarray): A 2D square matrix where each element represents the distance between two nodes.

    Returns:
    numpy.ndarray: A 2D square matrix of the same shape as the input, indicating the heuristic score for each edge.
    """

    # Calculate the adjacency matrix from the distance matrix
    adj_matrix = (distance_matrix == np.inf).astype(int)
    np.fill_diagonal(adj_matrix, 0)
    
    # Compute the minimum spanning tree (MST) of the graph
    mst_indices = minimum_spanning_tree(csgraph=adj_matrix).indices
    mst_distances = minimum_spanning_tree(csgraph=adj_matrix).data
    
    # Create a new matrix of the same shape as the input
    heuristics_matrix = np.empty_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Compute the quality heuristic for each edge
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # If the edge is in the MST, use the MST distance
            if i in mst_indices and j in mst_indices:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = mst_distances[mst_indices.tolist().index((i, j))]
            # If the edge is not in the MST, use the direct distance
            else:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]
    
    # Compute the quality ratio and normalize it
    quality_ratios = distance_matrix / heuristics_matrix
    heuristics_matrix *= quality_ratios
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from sklearn.cluster import SpectralClustering
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance matrix to a similarity matrix
    similarity_matrix = np.exp(-distance_matrix) / np.sum(np.exp(-distance_matrix), axis=1, keepdims=True)

    # Use Spectral Clustering on the similarity matrix
    clustering = SpectralClustering(n_clusters=len(distance_matrix), affinity="precomputed", assign_labels="hierarchical").fit(similarity_matrix)

    # Assign a higher undesirability score to edges between clusters
    undesirability_score_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(i, len(distance_matrix)):
            if clustering.labels_[i]!= clustering.labels_[j]:
                undesirability_score_matrix[i, j] = 1.0  # Set score to 1 for edges between clusters
            else:
                # Calculate the within-cluster distance as a measure of undesirability
                undesirability_score_matrix[i, j] = 1.0 - similarity_matrix[i, j]  # Higher values indicate more undesirability

    return undesirability_score_matrix

import numpy as np
from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import euclidean_distances
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate degree centrality
    degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    degrees = np.reshape(degrees, (-1, 1))
    degree_centrality = degrees / np.max(degrees)

    # Calculate clustering coefficient
    clustering_coefficients = _clustering_coefficients(distance_matrix)
    clustering_coefficients = np.reshape(clustering_coefficients, (-1, 1))

    # Calculate betweenness centrality
    betweenness_centralities = _betweenness_centrality(distance_matrix)
    betweenness_centralities = np.reshape(betweenness_centralities, (-1, 1))

    # Combine the centralities with distance
    heuristic_matrix = (
        distance_matrix * (degree_centrality + clustering_coefficients + betweenness_centralities)
    )

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    m, n = distance_matrix.shape
    # 1. Connection Strength: Sum of absolute differences of distances between nodes divided by the total distance.
    connection_strength = np.sum(np.abs(distance_matrix), axis=0) / np.sum(distance_matrix)

    # 2. Position in the Matrix: A simple function that assigns lower values for edges in the center and higher values for edges on the periphery.
    position = np.sqrt((m - 1) / 3) - np.abs(m - 1) / (2 * np.sqrt(m)) + 1 / m

    # 3. Average Distance to Neighbors: Calculate the average distance of neighbors for each node and then average those values.
    avg_dist_to_neighbors = 0
    for i in range(m):
        neighbors_distances = distance_matrix[i, :][:, :].sum(axis=0)
        avg_dist_to_neighbors += neighbors_distances.mean()
    avg_dist_to_neighbors /= m

    # Combine the three factors
    heuristics_matrix = connection_strength + position + avg_dist_to_neighbors
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    laplacian = calculate_laplacian(distance_matrix)  # Assume a function to compute Laplacian matrix
    D = np.diag(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1))  # Diagonal matrix of vertex degrees
    weights = 1 / distance_matrix  # Edge weights
    
    # Diversity measure
    diversity = np.sum(weights * np.matmul(laplacian, D), axis=1)  # Element-wise multiplication, sum, and sum across columns
    
    return diversity



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)

    # Initialize the MST
    mst_set = set()
    mst_edges = []
    total_weight = 0
    previous = {}

    # Prim's algorithm to find MST
    for i in range(n):
        min_distance = float('inf')
        min_index = -1

        for j in range(n):
            if (j not in mst_set) and (distance_matrix[i][j] < min_distance):
                min_distance = distance_matrix[i][j]
                min_index = j

        heapq.heappush(mst_edges, (min_distance, i, min_index))
        total_weight += min_distance
        previous[min_index] = i

    # Now, we build the MST and create heuristics for each edge
    mst = []
    while mst_edges:
        d, u, v = heapq.heappop(mst_edges)
        mst.append((u, v))

        if u in previous and v in previous[u]:
            # v is already in the MST
            continue

        # v is not in the MST, calculate heuristic
        edge_weight = distance_matrix[previous[u]][v]
        undesirability_factor = max(total_weight - distance_matrix[u][v], 0) / total_weight
        heuristic = edge_weight + undesirability_factor

        # Add to heuristics matrix
        for i in range(n):
            if (u, i) in mst_set or (i, v) in mst_set:
                distance_matrix[u][i] = max(distance_matrix[u][i], heuristic)
                distance_matrix[i][u] = heuristic

    return distance_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    diagonal_sum = sum(distance_matrix[i][i] for i in range(len(distance_matrix)))
    total_sum = sum(sum(distance_matrix[i]) for i in range(len(distance_matrix)))
    
    # Normalize the diagonal sum
    normalized_diagonal_sum = diagonal_sum / total_sum if total_sum!= 0 else 0
    
    # Create an undesirability matrix with normalized diagonal values
    undesirability_matrix = [
        [normalized_diagonal_sum] * len(distance_matrix) for _ in range(len(distance_matrix))
    ]
    
    return undesirability_matrix



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Calculate the triangle inequality cost
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    triangle_inequality_costs = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            for k in range(n):
                if i!= j and j!= k and i!= k:
                    triangle_inequality_costs[i, j] = min(
                        triangle_inequality_costs[i, j],
                        distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j]
                    )

    # Calculate the heuristic values
    heuristic_values = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristic_values[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] + triangle_inequality_costs[i, j] - min(
                distance_matrix[i, j], triangle_inequality_costs[i, j]
            )

    # Normalize heuristic values to ensure they range between 0 and 1
    heuristic_values = (heuristic_values - min(heuristic_values.min(), triangle_inequality_costs.min())) / (
        max(heuristic_values.max(), triangle_inequality_costs.max()) - min(heuristic_values.min(), triangle_inequality_costs.min())
    )

    return heuristic_values

    return heuristic_values



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the adjacency matrix to store path lengths
    path_lengths = [[float('inf')] * n for _ in range(n)]

    # Floyd-Warshall algorithm to compute shortest paths
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                path_lengths[i][j] = min(path_lengths[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])

    # Create a new matrix to hold edge heuristics
    heuristic_matrix = [[distance_matrix[i][j] / path_lengths[i][j] for j in range(n)] for i in range(n)]
    
    return heuristic_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    # Calculate betweenness centrality
    betweenness = betweenness_centrality(G)

    # Combine with original distances for a weighted heuristic
    weighted_heuristic = {edge: (1 / dist) + (1 / betweenness[edge]) for edge, dist in distance_matrix.items()}

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with the same values as the distance matrix
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Calculate improvement costs
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if i!= k and j!= k:
                    # Compute the improvement cost for edge (i, j)
                    improvement_cost = distance_matrix[i, j] - distance_matrix[i, k] - distance_matrix[k, j] + distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j]
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] += improvement_cost
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics_advanced(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Calculate the sum of diagonal elements. This represents self-connections.
    diagonal_sum = sum(distance_matrix.diagonal())

    # Initialize the result matrix with the same shape as the input
    result_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()

    # Density-based heuristics: penalize dense clusters
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i+1, num_nodes):
            if distance_matrix[i,j] > diagonal_sum:
                # If there's an edge between nodes i and j, subtract the average of self-distances
                result_matrix[i,j] -= (diagonal_sum / num_nodes)
                result_matrix[j,i] -= (diagonal_sum / num_nodes)

    # Path-based heuristics: penalize long paths
    for k in range(num_nodes):
        for i in range(num_nodes):
            for j in range(num_nodes):
                if i!= j and i!= k and j!= k:
                    # Calculate the average path length to k from i and j
                    path_length_i_k = 0.5 * (distance_matrix[i,k] + distance_matrix[k,i])
                    path_length_j_k = 0.5 * (distance_matrix[j,k] + distance_matrix[k,j])
                    total_path_length = path_length_i_k + path_length_j_k
                    
                    # If there's an edge between i and j, add the inverse of the total path length
                    if result_matrix[i,j] > 0:
                        result_matrix[i,j] += 1 / total_path_length
                        result_matrix[j,i] += 1 / total_path_length

    return result_matrix

    total_weight = sum(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate the average weight per edge
    average_weight = total_weight / len(distance_matrix)

    # Create a new distance matrix where each element represents undesirability
    undesirability = [1 / (weight / average_weight) for weight in distance_matrix]

    return undesirability

import numpy as np
def weights(distance_matrix):
    """Assign weights to nodes based on their positions or importance."""
    # Assuming nodes are in a 2D plane
    weights = np.exp(-distance_matrix**2)  # Here, we use an exponential decay function to give more importance to nearby nodes
    return weights / np.sum(weights)  # Normalize so that weights sum up to 1

import numpy as np
def floyd_warshall(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                distance_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    return distance_matrix

    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Calculate the density of the graph
    num_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    density = np.sum(distance_matrix > 0) / (num_vertices * (num_vertices - 1))
    
    # Calculate the connectedness
    adjacency_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    adjacency_matrix[distance_matrix > 0] = 1  # 1 if there's an edge, 0 otherwise
    connected_components = len(np.unique(np.argwhere(adjacency_matrix).flatten()))

    # Create a heuristics matrix with lower weights for denser and more connected subgraphs
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    heuristics_matrix[connected_components > 1, connected_components > 1] *= density

    return heuristics_matrix

# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize costs for all vertices as infinity, except the source vertex
    costs = [float('inf')] * n
    costs[0] = 0
    # Priority queue for Dijkstra's algorithm
    queue = [(0, 0)]  # (cost_so_far, current_vertex)

    # Dijkstra's algorithm
    while queue:
        current_cost, current_vertex = heapq.heappop(queue)

        if current_cost > costs[current_vertex]:
            continue  # Already visited, skip
        
        for next_vertex in range(n):
            edge_cost = distance_matrix[current_vertex][next_vertex]

            # Cost adjustment: more common edges get a discount
            adjusted_cost = current_cost + (1 - min(costs[next_vertex], current_cost)) * 0.5
            
            # Only update if the new path is shorter
            if adjusted_cost < costs[next_vertex]:
                costs[next_vertex] = adjusted_cost
                heapq.heappush(queue, (adjusted_cost, next_vertex))

    # Return the cost matrix where each element (i,j) indicates the desirability
    # of including edge (i,j) in a solution
    return costs



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)  # Assuming a square matrix
    distance_matrix_inv = 1 / distance_matrix  # Inverse distances
    balance_factor = 0.5  # You can adjust this value
    avg_proximity = [sum(distance_matrix[i][j]) / (n - 1) for i in range(n)]  # Average distance to neighbors
    
    # Create a new matrix where each entry is a combination of direct distance, inverse distance, and proximity
    heuristics_matrix = (1 - balance_factor) * distance_matrix + balance_factor * distance_matrix_inv + avg_proximity
    
    return heuristics_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Calculate the sum of the elements in each row of the distance matrix
    row_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Create a new matrix to store heuristic values
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Populate the heuristics matrix
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # The heuristic value for edge (i, j) is the maximum distance plus the sum of the weights

# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    m, n = distance_matrix.shape
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the heuristic for each edge
    for i in range(m):
        for j in range(n):
            # Negative-weight cycle penalty
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]
                for k in range(m):
                    if k!= i and k!= j:
                        heuristic_matrix[i, j] += distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j]
    
    # Convert negative values to a maximum possible positive value
    max_distance = np.max(heuristic_matrix[np.triu_indices(n)])
    heuristic_matrix[np.triu_indices(n)] = max_distance - heuristic_matrix[np.triu_indices(n)]
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, avg_distance=np.mean(distance_matrix), threshold=3):
    m, n = distance_matrix.shape
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    for i in range(m):
        for j in range(n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j] > avg_distance * threshold:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 1
            else:
                # Use inverse distance as heuristic
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 1 / distance_matrix[i, j]
    
    return heuristics_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix, traffic, road_type, obstacle_cost):
    # 'traffic' is a matrix representing the current traffic level for each edge
    # 'road_type' is a matrix representing the type of road for each edge (e.g., 0 for city, 1 for highway, 2 for rural)
    # 'obstacle_cost' is a cost added if an edge crosses an '1' in the obstacle_cost matrix

    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Add traffic factor
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] += traffic[i][j]
    
    # Add road type factor
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] += road_type[i][j] * 10  # Adjust factor as needed
                # Assume 0 is city, 1 is highway, 2 is rural

    # Add obstacle cost factor
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                if obstacle_cost[i][j] > 0:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] += obstacle_cost[i][j] * 5  # Adjust factor as needed

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the inverse of the diagonal elements to penalize local edges
    distance_matrix[np.diag_indices_from(distance_matrix)] = 1 / np.max(distance_matrix)
    
    # Adjust the off-diagonal elements based on the sum of distances to nearby nodes
    # This makes edges connecting nodes with many neighbors more desirable
    adjusted_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    for i in range(len(adjusted_matrix)):
        for j in range(i+1, len(adjusted_matrix)):
            adjusted_matrix[i,j] = distance_matrix[i,j] * min(distance_matrix[i][:], key=distance_matrix[i,:].sum)
            adjusted_matrix[j,i] = adjusted_matrix[i,j]
    
    return adjusted_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the standard Euclidean heuristic
    euclidean_heuristic = np.sqrt(np.sum(distance_matrix**2, axis=1))
    
    # Initialize the costly detours matrix with the same shape as the input
    costly_detours = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate costly detours for each edge
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
            if i!= j:  # Only consider edges that are not diagonal
                for k in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
                    if k!= i and k!= j:  # Avoid self-loops
                        costly_detours[i, j] += min(distance_matrix[i, k], distance_matrix[j, k])  # Minimum distance to bypass

    # Combine the Euclidean heuristic with costly detours
    heuristics_matrix = euclidean_heuristic - costly_detours
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics_advanced(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Compute the degree of each vertex
    degree = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Initialize the heuristics matrix
    heuristics = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate edge-towers (a heuristic to capture local graph structure)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            # Get neighbors
            nbr_i = np.where(distance_matrix[i] < distance_matrix.min())[0]
            nbr_j = np.where(distance_matrix[j] < distance_matrix.min())[0]

            # Get the minimum distance among the neighbors
            min_dist_i = distance_matrix[i, nbr_i].min()
            min_dist_j = distance_matrix[j, nbr_j].min()

            # Edge-towers: higher min_dist_i and min_dist_j
            heuristics[i, j] = max(min_dist_i, min_dist_j)
            heuristics[j, i] = heuristics[i, j]  # Symmetry

    # Normalize by degree to prevent edges connecting low-degree vertices from being penalized excessively
    heuristics /= degree[:, np.newaxis]

    # Add graph density as a secondary indicator
    density = 2 * np.sum(distance_matrix) / (n * (n - 1))
    heuristics += density[:, np.newaxis]

    return heuristics

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import connected_components
from collections import defaultdict
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Calculate local density
    local_densities = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1) / (n - 1)
    
    # Calculate global density
    global_density = np.sum(distance_matrix) / (n * (n - 1))
    
    # Define a function to calculate node centrality
    def node_centrality(row_indices, col_indices, distance_matrix):
        comms = connected_components(csgraph=distance_matrix, directed=False)
        num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
        centrality = defaultdict(int)
        for comm in range(comms):
            node_in_component = np.where(np.arange(num_nodes) == row_indices)[0]
            centrality[comm] += 1.0 / len(node_in_component)
        return centrality
    
    # Calculate node centrality
    node_centrality_values = {i: node_centrality(np.array([i]), np.array([i]), distance_matrix) for i in range(n)}
    
    # Combine metrics
    heuristics_matrix = - (local_densities + global_density) * (1 - np.array(list(node_centrality_values.values())) ** 2)
    
    return heuristics_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    local_costs = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1)

    # Calculate the global cost
    global_costs = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Balance local and global costs
    weighted_local_cost = local_costs * 0.6  # Adjust this weight as needed
    weighted_global_cost = global_costs * 0.4  # Adjust this weight as needed
    
    # Combine local and global costs
    heuristic_matrix = weighted_local_cost + weighted_global_cost

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)  # assuming square distance matrix

    # Step 1: Calculate total distance
    total_distance = sum(distance_matrix.diagonal())

    # Step 2: Normalize distances
    normalized_distances = [x / total_distance for x in distance_matrix.flatten()]

    # Step 3: Assign frequency weight
    frequency_weight = 2

    # Step 4: Calculate importance scores
    importance_scores = [norm * freq_weight for norm, freq in zip(normalized_distances, range(1, n*n+1))]

    # Step 5: Reshape to match the original matrix shape
    heuristics_matrix = np.reshape(importance_scores, (n, n))

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Degree centrality
    degree_centrality = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Clustering coefficient
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    clustering_coefficient = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j]!= 0:
                clustering_coefficient[i, j] = 2 * distance_matrix[i, j] / np.sum(distance_matrix[i, :])
                clustering_coefficient[j, i] = clustering_coefficient[i, j]
    
    # Eigenvector centrality
    _, _ = np.linalg.eig(np.dot(distance_matrix, distance_matrix.T))
    eigenvector_centrality = np.linalg.inv(np.eye(n) - np.dot(distance_matrix, distance_matrix.T)).sum(axis=1)
    
    # Combine using weighted sum
    score_matrix = 0.3 * degree_centrality + 0.4 * clustering_coefficient + 0.3 * eigenvector_centrality
    
    return score_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the input is a square numpy array
    distance_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix)
    if distance_matrix.shape[0]!= distance_matrix.shape[1]:
        raise ValueError("Input matrix must be square.")
    
    # Compute the Pseudoinverse
    pseudoinverse = np.linalg.pinv(distance_matrix)
    
    # Adjust for zeros (these will remain zeros in pseudoinverse)
    pseudoinverse[np.isclose(pseudoinverse, 0)] = 1
    
    return pseudoinverse

import numpy as np
def weighted_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Calculate density (number of edges) per node
    node_density = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1) / num_nodes

    # Calculate centrality (betweenness centrality for simplicity)
    betweenness_centrality = np.zeros(num_nodes)
    for _ in range(10):  # Run the calculation 10 times to improve accuracy
        betweenness = np.zeros(num_nodes)
        for i in range(num_nodes):
            for j in range(num_nodes):
                if i!= j:
                    sub_matrix = distance_matrix[np.ix_(np.concatenate([np.arange(num_nodes)!= i, np.arange(num_nodes)!= j]), np.concatenate([np.arange(num_nodes)!= i, np.arange(num_nodes)!= j])))
                    betweenness[i] += sub_matrix[j, :].sum() / (sub_matrix.shape[0] - 1)
        betweenness_centrality = (betweenness / np.sum(betweenness)) if np.sum(betweenness) > 0 else betweenness

    # Combine distance and density/centrality metrics
    heuristic_matrix = -distance_matrix - node_density / 2 - betweenness_centrality  # Negative to maximize
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from sklearn.cluster import SpectralClustering
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the symmetric distance matrix.
    distance_matrix = np.maximum(distance_matrix, distance_matrix.T)
    
    # Perform spectral clustering.
    # We'll treat the distance matrix as a similarity matrix and use the normalized Laplacian matrix.
    laplacian_matrix = np.eye(distance_matrix.shape[0]) - distance_matrix
    eigen_values, eigen_vectors = np.linalg.eig(laplacian_matrix)
    
    # Normalize the eigenvalues.
    norm_eigen_values = eigen_values / np.sum(eigen_values)
    
    # Use spectral clustering to partition into groups.
    clustering = SpectralClustering(n_clusters=distance_matrix.shape[0], affinity="precomputed", assign_labels="kmeans").fit(laplacian_matrix)
    
    # Assign each edge a heuristic score based on its cluster membership.
    heuristic_scores = norm_eigen_values[clustering.labels_]
    
    return heuristic_scores.reshape(-1, distance_matrix.shape[0])



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Degree of each node
    degrees = [sum(distance_matrix[i]) for i in range(n)]
    
    # Initialize heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Calculate closeness centrality with degree-penalty
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i == j:
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] = 0  # Self-edge penalty
            else:
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] = 1 / distance_matrix[i][j]
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] *= degrees[i] / degrees[j]  # Degree-penalty
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize priority queue and distances to all nodes from the source node
    priority_queue = [(0, 0)]  # (cost so far, node)
    distances = [float('inf')] * n
    distances[0] = 0
    
    # Dijkstra's algorithm
    while priority_queue:
        current_cost, current_node = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)
        
        if current_cost > distances[current_node]:
            continue
        
        for neighbor, edge_cost in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_node]):
            if edge_cost == 0:  # Assuming edge_cost is 0 for neighbor nodes
                continue
            
            if distances[neighbor] > current_cost + edge_cost:
                distances[neighbor] = current_cost + edge_cost
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (distances[neighbor], neighbor))
    
    # Calculate heuristic values as the difference between total cost to node and cost to neighbor
    heuristic_values = [[distance_matrix[i][j] - distances[i] for j in range(n)] for i in range(n)]
    
    return heuristic_values



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Add a row of ones for self-distance, to consider the edge from a vertex to itself
    distance_matrix = np.vstack([np.ones(distance_matrix.shape[1]), distance_matrix])
    
    # Compute the sum of distances for each node
    row_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Introduce an "importance" factor, based on the number of connections each node has
    importance_factor = 1 / row_sums
    importance_factor[0] = 0  # Exclude self-distance from importance calculation
    importance_factor = importance_factor / np.sum(importance_factor)  # Normalize
    
    # Compute the "least-connectedness" heuristic
    heuristics_matrix = (1 / importance_factor) * (1 - distance_matrix)
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the result matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]

    # Create priority queue and distance dictionary
    priority_queue = [(0, 0)]  # (current distance, current node)
    shortest_paths = {i: float('inf') for i in range(n)}
    shortest_paths[0] = 0

    while priority_queue:
        current_distance, current_node = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)

        # If we've found a shorter path to the current node, update
        if current_distance > shortest_paths[current_node]:
            continue

        # Explore neighbors
        for neighbor, weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_node]):
            if weight + shortest_paths[current_node] < shortest_paths[neighbor]:
                shortest_paths[neighbor] = weight + shortest_paths[current_node]
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (shortest_paths[neighbor], neighbor))

        # Assign heuristic values based on shortest path distances
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if i == j:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
                else:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] = shortest_paths[i] + distance_matrix[i][j]

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_betweenness_centrality
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to an undirected graph
    graph = np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1)
    
    # Calculate betweenness centrality for each edge (node pair)
    centrality, _ = csgraph_betweenness_centrality(csgraph=graph, directed=False, return_distances=False)
    
    # Scale betweenness centrality scores to be within a reasonable range (0-1)
    max_centrality = np.max(centrality)
    normalized_centrality = (centrality - np.min(centrality)) / (max_centrality - np.min(centrality))
    
    # The normalized betweenness centrality now serves as the heuristic score for each edge
    # The higher the score, the more undesirable the edge is to include in a solution
    heuristics_matrix = np.array(normalized_centrality).reshape(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, travel_frequency, edge_weights):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Compute the heuristic score for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Distance component
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][j]
            
            # Frequency component
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] -= travel_frequency[i][j]
            
            # Weight component
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] += edge_weights[i][j]
            
            # Alternative edge component
            for k in range(n):
                if k!= j:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] -= distance_matrix[i][k]
            
            # Normalize the heuristic score for better comparison
            total_heuristic = sum(sum(row) for row in heuristic_matrix)
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] /= total_heuristic
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)  # Keep the original matrix

    # Select a random edge
    i, j = np.random.choice(n, size=2, replace=False)
    min_distance = min(distance_matrix[i, :], distance_matrix[:, j])

    # Find the optimal replacement for the selected edge
    current_node = i
    for k in range(n):
        if distance_matrix[current_node, k] < min_distance:
            current_node = k

    current_path = [i]
    new_path = [current_node]

    while current_node!= j:
        min_distance_adj = min(distance_matrix[current_node, new_path[-1]], 
                               distance_matrix[new_path[-1], current_node])
        if min_distance_adj < distance_matrix[current_node, new_path[-1]]:
            new_path.append(current_node)
            current_node = min_distance_adj
        else:
            new_path.append(new_path[-1])
            current_node = new_path[-1]

    new_path.append(j)

    # Calculate the heuristic score
    new_distance = sum(distance_matrix[p, q] for p, q in zip(new_path, new_path[1:]))
    heuristics_matrix[i, j] = new_distance

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the Manhattan distance for each row to capture the proximity effect
    row_manhattan_distances = np.sum(np.abs(distance_matrix - np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)), axis=1)
    
    # Inversely scale these distances to emphasize the importance of smaller, more distant edges
    heuristics_matrix = np.maximum(1, 1 / row_manhattan_distances)
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, alpha=0.5):
    num_vertices = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = [[0]*num_vertices for _ in range(num_vertices)]

    # Calculate Manhattan and Euclidean distances
    manhattan_distances = [sum(abs(a-b) for a, b in zip(row, col)) for row in distance_matrix]
    euclidean_distances = [((a-b)**2).sum()**0.5 for a, b in zip(distance_matrix, distance_matrix)]

    # Apply the learning factor alpha
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(num_vertices):
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = alpha * manhattan_distances[i] + (1 - alpha) * euclidean_distances[i]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adjacency_matrix = np.abs(distance_matrix)  # Square of distances, assumed unweighted
    degree = np.sum(adjacency_matrix, axis=0)  # Degree of each node
    clustering_coefficients = np.zeros((n, n))

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if adjacency_matrix[i, j] > 0:
                triangles = np.sum(adjacency_matrix[i, :] * adjacency_matrix[:, j] * adjacency_matrix[np.outer(np.arange(n), np.arange(n)) == np.outer(i, j)])
                clustering_coefficients[i, j] = 2 * triangles / (degree[i] * (degree[i] - 1))

    max_cc = np.max(clustering_coefficients)
    normalized_heuristics = clustering_coefficients / max_cc

    return normalized_heuristics



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    cost_to_complete = [sum(distance_matrix[i]) for i in range(n)]

    # Calculate cost-to-complete for each node
    for node in range(n):
        cost_to_complete[node] += distance_matrix[node][node]  # Connecting a node to itself

    # Create and return the undesirability matrix
    undesirability_matrix = [[(cost_to_complete[i] + cost_to_complete[j] - distance_matrix[i][j]) / 2 for j in range(n)] for i in range(n)]
    return undesirability_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def betweenness_centrality(graph, nodes):
    n = graph.shape[0]
    degree = np.sum(graph, axis=0)
    path_length = np.diag(np.sqrt(np.sum(graph**2, axis=1)))
    trans_graph = np.eye(n) - np.linalg.inv(degree)
    b = np.zeros(n)
    
    for _ in range(2, n+1):
        new_b = np.copy(b)
        for node in nodes:
            for i in range(n):
                if i!= node:
                    parallel_edges = trans_graph[i, :].dot(graph[:, node])
                    if parallel_edges.sum() > 0:
                        b[node] += 1 / parallel_edges[i] * (path_length[i, node] - path_length[node, i])
        b = np.maximum(b, new_b)
    
    return b



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Calculate the sum of distances for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = heuristics_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j]
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[j][k] for k in range(n) if k!= i and k!= j
    
    # Normalize the heuristics matrix to values between 0 and 1
    min_value = min(min(row) for row in heuristics_matrix)
    max_value = max(max(row) for row in heuristics_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = [[(x - min_value) / (max_value - min_value) for x in row] for row in heuristics_matrix]
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the source and destination nodes
    src, dest = np.unravel_index(np.argmin(distance_matrix, axis=None), distance_matrix.shape)
    
    # Initialize heuristics matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Compute shortest paths using Dijkstra's algorithm
    path_lengths = dijkstra(distance_matrix, src, dest)
    
    # Update heuristics based on shortest path lengths
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i!= src and j!= dest:
                # If current node is not source or destination
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] += path_lengths[i]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize a matrix to store the potential function values
    potential = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Potential function: negative sum of distances in shortest paths
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            potential[i][j] = -distance_matrix[i][j]
    
    # Update the potential based on negative cycles using Floyd-Warshall algorithm
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                if potential[i][j] > potential[i][k] + potential[k][j]:
                    potential[i][j] = potential[i][k] + potential[k][j]
    
    # Create a heuristics matrix where each value represents the undesirability of including an edge
    heuristics_matrix = [[-p if p < 0 else 0 for p in potential[i]] for i in range(n)]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
import random
def heuristics_NN(distance_matrix):
    num_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize tour with a random vertex
    tour = np.random.choice(num_vertices)
    # Initialize total heuristic value
    total_heuristic = 0
    # Initialize a queue for neighbors
    neighbors_queue = []
    
    for _ in range(num_vertices):
        # Calculate potential neighbors
        potential_neighbors = [v for v in range(num_vertices) if v!= tour and distance_matrix[tour, v] < distance_matrix[tour, tour]]
        
        if len(potential_neighbors) == 0:
            # If no neighbors, perturb and choose a random vertex
            heuristic_perturbation = random.uniform(0, 1)
            if heuristic_perturbation < 0.1:  # Arbitrary threshold for perturbation
                potential_neighbors = [v for v in range(num_vertices) if v!= tour]
        
        # Choose the next vertex using nearest neighbor with perturbation
        next_vertex = potential_neighbors[np.argmin([distance_matrix[tour, v] + distance_matrix[v, np.random.randint(num_vertices)] for v in potential_neighbors])]
        
        # Add the chosen vertex to the tour and update total heuristic
        tour = next_vertex
        total_heuristic += distance_matrix[tour, next_vertex]
        
        # Add the new edge to the neighbors queue
        neighbors_queue.append((tour, next_vertex))
        
        # Move the current vertex to the end of the queue to consider its effect on the partial tour's endpoints
        neighbors_queue.append((next_vertex, tour))
    
    return total_heuristic

import numpy as np
import scipy.sparse.csgraph as csgraph
def reverse_delete_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a sparse adjacency matrix from the distance matrix
    graph = csgraph.create_adjacency_matrix(distance_matrix, diagonal=False)
    
    # Compute the MST of the graph using Kruskal's algorithm
    _, _ = csgraph.minimum_spanning_tree(graph)
    
    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristics_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Iterate to remove edges from the MST
    for _ in range(len(distance_matrix) - 1):
        # Find the highest-weight edge in the MST
        max_weight_edge = np.unravel_index(graph.nonzero()[0][np.argmax(graph[np.unravel_index(graph.nonzero())[0][0], np.unravel_index(graph.nonzero())[1][0])]), graph.shape)
        
        # If the edge exists in the MST, remove it
        if heuristics_matrix[max_weight_edge] > 0:
            heuristics_matrix[max_weight_edge] = -10000  # Replace with a very high value
        
        # Find the next highest-weight edge
        next_max_weight_edge = np.unravel_index(graph.nonzero()[0][np.argmax(graph[np.unravel_index(graph.nonzero())[0][0], np.unravel_index(graph.nonzero())[1][0]) + 1])], graph.shape)
        
        # If the edge exists in the MST, remove it
        if heuristics_matrix[next_max_weight_edge] > 0:
            heuristics_matrix[next_max_weight_edge] = -10000  # Replace with a very high value
        
        # Update the graph and MST
        graph[max_weight_edge] = np.inf
        graph[next_max_weight_edge] = np.inf
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def weighted_neighborhood_heuristics(distance_matrix, k):
    """
    This function computes an effective distance score for each edge in the input distance matrix,
    taking into account the neighborhood within a radius of `k`.
    """
    
    # Create a copy of the distance matrix to avoid modifying the input
    effective_dist = distance_matrix.copy()

    # Iterate over each node and calculate its effective distance
    for node in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        # Get the node's coordinates
        node_coordinates = node
        
        # For each edge (i, j)
        for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
            for j in range(len(distance_matrix)):
                # Calculate the effective distance as the weighted sum of distance and neighborhood distances
                effective_dist[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] + min(
                    distance_matrix[node_coordinates][n] 
                    for n in range(len(distance_matrix)) 
                    if abs(n - node_coordinates) <= k
                )
    
    return effective_dist



# Score: -20000

def cost_to_connect_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the dimensions of the matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the cost-to-connect matrix
    cost_to_connect = np.full_like(distance_matrix, np.inf)
    
    # Fill the diagonal with 0 (connecting a node to itself has a cost of 0)
    np.fill_diagonal(cost_to_connect, 0)
    
    # Fill the upper triangular part with 1/distance
    cost_to_connect[np.triu_indices(n)] = 1 / distance_matrix[np.triu_indices(n)]
    
    # Fill the lower triangular part with the same values (since cost of connecting is symmetric)
    cost_to_connect[np.tril_indices(n, -1)] = cost_to_connect[np.tril_indices(n, -1)]
    
    return cost_to_connect



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Start with the same shape as the input distance matrix
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = [[0] * num_nodes for _ in range(num_nodes)]
    
    # Iterate over each node
    for node in range(num_nodes):
        # Initialize the closest node with a large value
        min_distance = float('inf')
        closest_node = -1
        
        # Loop through unvisited nodes
        for other_node in range(node+1, num_nodes):
            if distance_matrix[node][other_node] < min_distance:
                min_distance = distance_matrix[node][other_node]
                closest_node = other_node
        
        # Set the heuristic for the current node as the distance to its nearest unvisited neighbor
        heuristics_matrix[node][closest_node] = min_distance
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Union-find data structure to keep track of connected components
    parent = list(range(n))
    
    def find(x):
        if parent[x]!= x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]
    
    def union(x, y):
        root_x = find(x)
        root_y = find(y)
        
        if root_x == root_y:
            return False
        
        parent[root_x] = root_y
        return True



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    
    # Initial pheromone and heuristic values
    pheromone = np.ones((n, n)) / n
    heuristics = np.array(distance_matrix)  # use the original distance as a heuristic initially
    
    # ACO parameters
    alpha = 2  # heuristic contribution
    beta = 1   # pheromone contribution
    repair = False  # whether to repair solutions if they go out of bounds
    
    for _ in range(100):  # iterations
        # Epsilon-greedy action selection for ants
        selection = np.random.choice([0, 1], size=n*n, p=[alpha, beta])
        selected_indices = np.unravel_index(selection, (n, n))
        
        u, v = selected_indices
        w = np.random.randint(0, n)  # neighbor node
        
        # Pheromone update
        heuristics_uv = heuristics[u, v] + heuristics[v, w] - heuristics[u, w]
        heuristics_uv_phero = pheromone[u, v] * (1 - pheromone[u, v])  # pheromone evaporation
        pheromone[u, v] += heuristics_uv_phero * (1 - pheromone[u, v])
        
        # Epsilon-greedy heuristic update
        if np.random.rand() < alpha:
            heuristics_uv = heuristics[u, v] + np.random.uniform(0, 1)  # random heuristic update
        
        # Edge construction probability
        if repair:
            if heuristics_uv > 0:
                heuristics[u, v] += heuristics_uv
                heuristics[v, w] += heuristics_uv
                pheromone[u, w] += heuristics_uv_phero * (1 - pheromone[u, w])
            else:
                heuristics[u, v] = np.inf
                pheromone[u, w] = 0
        else:
            if heuristics_uv < heuristics[u, w]:
                heuristics[u, v] = heuristics_uv
                heuristics[v, w] = heuristics_uv
                pheromone[u, w] += heuristics_uv_phero * (1 - pheromone[u, w])
            else:
                heuristics[u, v] = np.inf
                pheromone[u, w] = 0
        
        # Apply the repair mechanism
        if repair and heuristics[u, v] == np.inf:
            heuristics[u, v] = heuristics[v, w]
            heuristics[v, w] = heuristics[u, w]
            pheromone[u, w] = pheromone[v, w]
    
    return heuristics



# Score: -20000
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import floyd_warshall
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute all-pairs shortest paths (Floyd-Warshall algorithm)
    dist = distance_matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    for k in range(n):
        dist = np.minimum(dist, np.add.outer(dist, dist[k]))
    dist = np.minimum(dist, np.linalg.norm(dist, axis=1))
    
    # Calculate centrality scores for each node
    centrality = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            centrality[i][j] = dist[i][j]**2 / np.sum(dist**2)

    # Create a heuristics matrix where each entry represents the undesirability
    # of including an edge between two nodes. Edges connecting central nodes are
    # less undesirable.
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = centrality[i][j]

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def simple_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Simple heuristic: Minimize the sum of distances
    return distance_matrix.sum(axis=0)



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Create an initial solution (perhaps the one given by the distance matrix itself)
    initial_tour = np.arange(n)
    current_tour = initial_tour.copy()
    # Initialize a list to keep track of potential improvements (2-opt moves)
    potential_improvements = []

    # Iterate over every possible edge pair in the tour
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # If swapping edges improves the tour
            improved_tour = np.delete(current_tour, np.concatenate(([i], [j], [i], [j])))
            new_distance = np.sum(distance_matrix[improved_tour[1:-1], improved_tour[1:-1]])

            # If a 2-opt move resulted in a shorter tour, keep track of it
            if new_distance < np.sum(distance_matrix[current_tour[1:-1], current_tour[1:-1]]):
                potential_improvements.append((i, j, new_distance))

    # If no improvements were found, return the initial tour
    if not potential_improvements:
        return distance_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.linalg import eig
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix into a similarity matrix, where similarity = 1 / distance
    similarity_matrix = 1 / distance_matrix

    # Compute the Laplacian matrix, L = D - W, where D is the degree matrix, and W is the similarity matrix
    degree_matrix = np.diag(np.sum(similarity_matrix, axis=0))
    laplacian_matrix = degree_matrix - similarity_matrix

    # Compute the second smallest eigenvalue (algebraic connectivity) of the Laplacian matrix
    eigenvalues, _ = eig(laplacian_matrix)
    second_smallest_eigenvalue = eigenvalues[1]

    # Create a heuristic score matrix, where each cell represents the normalized second smallest eigenvalue
    heuristic_scores = 1 / second_smallest_eigenvalue

    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def advanced_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Number of vertices
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the MST and priority queue
    mst = [(-1, -1) for _ in range(n)]  # (-weight, vertex)
    parent = [None] * n
    min_heap = [(0, 0)]  # (weight, current_vertex)
    
    # Initialize the visited set
    visited = set()
    
    # Priority queue operations
    while min_heap:
        weight, current_vertex = heapq.heappop(min_heap)
        
        # If vertex is already visited, skip it
        if current_vertex in visited:
            continue
        
        # Mark current vertex as visited
        visited.add(current_vertex)
        
        # Traverse the graph to find the minimum-weight edge to this vertex
        for next_vertex, edge_weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_vertex]):
            if edge_weight!= float('inf') and next_vertex not in visited:
                if (weight + edge_weight, next_vertex) < mst[next_vertex]:
                    mst[next_vertex] = (weight + edge_weight, next_vertex)
                    parent[next_vertex] = current_vertex
                    heapq.heappush(min_heap, (weight + edge_weight, next_vertex))
    
    # Construct the MST from the minimum-weight edges
    mst_edges = [(mst[i][1], mst[i][0], i) for i in range(n) if parent[i] is not None]
    return mst_edges

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import shortest_path
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate vertex degrees
    degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate the number of edges
    num_edges = distance_matrix.size // 2
    
    # Calculate shortest path lengths from each node to all others
    dist_matrix, _ = shortest_path(distance_matrix, directed=False)
    
    # Calculate a simple edge undesirability score based on degrees and shortest path length
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(i, distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            # Exclude diagonal elements (self-loops)
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = degrees[i] * (num_edges - degrees[i]) * dist_matrix[i, j]
                heuristic_matrix[j, i] = heuristic_matrix[i, j]
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Local Connectivity: Proportion of neighboring nodes within a certain radius
    radius = 2  # Define the radius. Smaller values emphasize local connections.
    local_connectivity = np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix < radius, axis=1) / len(distance_matrix[0])

    # Global Connectivity: Reciprocal of average shortest path from each node
    avg_shortest_paths = np.mean([np.min(dijkstra(distance_matrix, i)) for i in range(len(distance_matrix))])
    global_connectivity = 1 / avg_shortest_paths if avg_shortest_paths > 0 else 0

    # Combine local and global connectivity, multiply by edge weights for emphasis
    heuristics_matrix = local_connectivity * distance_matrix + global_connectivity * distance_matrix
    return heuristics_matrix

import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize SPT priority queue with (cost, node) for each node
    spt = [(0, i) for i in range(n)]
    heapq.heapify(spt)
    # Initialize parent and cost arrays for SPT
    parent = [None] * n
    cost = [float('inf')] * n
    cost[0] = 0

    while spt:
        current_cost, current_node = heapq.heappop(spt)

        # If we've reached the target node, construct the path and add to heuristics
        if current_node == n - 1:
            path = []
            while current_node is not None:
                path.append(current_node)
                current_node = parent[current_node]
            path.reverse()
            return distance_matrix[path[0]][path[-1]]

import networkx as nx
from heapq import nsmallest
def heuristics(distance_matrix, k=3):
    # Create a graph from distance matrix
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Find the indices of all nodes
    N = list(range(len(distance_matrix)))
    
    # Find the shortest paths from each node to the last node
    shortest_paths = nx.all_pairs_dijkstra_path(G)
    
    # Calculate heuristic scores for each edge
    heuristics_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(len(distance_matrix[i]))] for i in N]
    for node in N:
        for neighbor in G.neighbors(node):
            # Consider paths from each source node to the neighbor
            for source in N:
                if source == node:
                    continue
                # Get the shortest path from source to neighbor
                path = shortest_paths[source][neighbor]
                # Weight the path by the number of edges in it
                weights = [distance_matrix[p[i-1]][p[i]] for i in range(1, len(path))]
                # Find the k-shortest paths
                k_shortest = nsmallest(k, [weights], key=sum)
                heuristics_matrix[node][neighbor] = sum(k_shortest)

    return heuristics_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    # Step 2: Calculate the closeness centrality
    closeness = _closeness_centrality(distance_matrix)
    
    # Step 3: Combine the centrality values to form the heuristic matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Step 4: Use a weighted combination of betweenness and closeness
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] = 1 / (betweenness[i][j] + closeness[i][j])

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristic_matrix = -1 * np.ones_like(distance_matrix)

    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i == j:
                continue

            # First penalty: distance from current node
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][j]

            # Second penalty: sum of distances from all other nodes to this edge
            edge_distances = np.array([distance_matrix[k][j] for k in range(num_nodes) if k!= i])
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] += np.sum(edge_distances)

            # Third penalty: sum of distances from other edges to this edge
            other_edges = np.array([np.linalg.norm(distance_matrix[k][l] - distance_matrix[k][j], ord=1) for k in range(num_nodes) for l in range(num_nodes) if k < l and k!= i and l!= j])
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] += np.sum(other_edges)

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get dimensions of the matrix
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Calculate the shortest path (SP) heuristic
    sp_heuristic = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate the cheapest path (CP) heuristic
    cp_heuristic = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Combine the two heuristics
    combined_heuristic = cp_heuristic + sp_heuristic
    
    return combined_heuristic



# Score: -20000
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a graph from the distance matrix
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate node degrees
    node_degrees = dict(G.degree())

    # Calculate node closeness centrality
    closeness = nx.closeness_centrality(G)

    # Calculate node betweenness centrality
    betweenness = nx.betweenness_centrality(G)

    # Initialize the undesirability matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.full_like(distance_matrix, -np.inf)

    # Define a threshold for modularity gain
    modularity_threshold = 0.1  # Adjust this value based on your specific problem

    for u, v in G.edges():
        # Degree heuristic: -log(node_degrees[u]) - log(node_degrees[v])
        heuristics_matrix[u, v] -= np.log(node_degrees[u])
        heuristics_matrix[v, u] -= np.log(node_degrees[v])

        # Closeness heuristic: inverse of average closeness
        avg_closeness = np.mean(list(closeness.values()))
        heuristics_matrix[u, v] += 1 / avg_closeness
        heuristics_matrix[v, u] += 1 / avg_closeness

        # Betweenness heuristic: -betweenness[u, v] * (1 - betweenness[u, v] / sum(betweenness.values()))
        heuristics_matrix[u, v] -= betweenness[u, v] * (1 - betweenness[u, v] / sum(betweenness.values()))
        heuristics_matrix[v, u] -= betweenness[v, u] * (1 - betweenness[v, u] / sum(betweenness.values()))

    # Adjust heuristics based on modularity gain
    for u, v in G.edges():
        edge_weight = G[u][v]['weight']
        avg_weight = np.mean([G[u][w]['weight'] for w in G.neighbors(u)])
        avg_weight_between_communities = np.mean([G[u][w]['weight'] for w in G.neighbors(G.subgraph(list(nx.connected_components(G)[0])).nodes())])

        if edge_weight / avg_weight > modularity_threshold:
            heuristics_matrix[u, v] += 100
            heuristics_matrix[v, u] += 100

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_from_adjacency
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import dijkstra
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Create an adjacency matrix from the distance matrix
    adj_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i, n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j]!= 0:
                adj_matrix[i, j] = 1
                adj_matrix[j, i] = 1

    # Convert adjacency matrix to a graph
    graph = csgraph_from_adjacency(adj_matrix)

    # Compute centrality measures
    degree_centrality = np.sum(adj_matrix, axis=0)
    betweenness_centrality, _ = csgraph_betweenness(graph)
    closeness_centrality, _ = csgraph_closeness(graph)

    # Normalize centrality measures to create a single score for each edge
    edge_scores = np.concatenate((degree_centrality[:, np.newaxis],
                                   betweenness_centrality[:, np.newaxis],
                                   closeness_centrality[:, np.newaxis]), axis=1)
    edge_scores = edge_scores / np.sum(edge_scores, axis=1)[:, np.newaxis]

    # Transform scores back to the distance matrix shape
    heuristics_matrix = squareform(pdist(edge_scores))

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert to sparse matrix for efficient processing
    dist_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix)
    adj_matrix = csgraph.create_adjacency_matrix(minimum_spanning_tree(dist_matrix))
    
    # Calculate shortest path between each pair of nodes using Floyd-Warshall algorithm
    shortest_paths = csgraph.floyd_warshall(csgraph.reverse_cweighted(adj_matrix))
    
    # Initialize heuristic matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate heuristic values
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(i+1, len(distance_matrix)):
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] - shortest_paths[i, j]
            heuristic_matrix[j, i] = heuristic_matrix[i, j]  # Make it symmetric
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Normalize the distance matrix to a range between 0 and 1
    min_distance = min(min(row) for row in distance_matrix)
    max_distance = max(max(row) for row in distance_matrix)
    normalized_distance = [(d - min_distance) / (max_distance - min_distance) for d in distance_matrix]
    
    # Introduce a risk factor that increases with the distance
    risk_factor = 1 - normalized_distance  # Lower values suggest higher risk (distance)
    
    # To maintain the matrix format, we add the risk_factor column
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(len(distance_matrix[0])):
            distance_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] + risk_factor[i][j]
    
    return distance_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize a list to store edges in the order of their weights
    edges = [(distance_matrix[i][j], i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)]
    # Use a min-heap to maintain the edges in non-increasing order of weight
    heapq.heapify(edges)

    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the input distance matrix
    heuristic_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

    while edges:
        # Extract the edge with the smallest weight
        weight, u, v = heapq.heappop(edges)
        # If including this edge (u, v) doesn't create a cycle, add it to the heuristic matrix
        if not any(u in path and v in path[::-1] for path in heuristic_matrix):
            heuristic_matrix[u][v] = weight
            for e in edges:
                if e[1] == u and e[2] == v:
                    heapq.heappush(edges, e)
                    break

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Shortest path distance via node i (using Floyd-Warshall algorithm)
            shortest_path_via_i = np.minimum.reduce([distance_matrix[i, k] + heuristics_matrix[k, j] for k in range(n) if k!= i])

            # If j can be reached via i, add the number of hops as a heuristic
            if shortest_path_via_i!= float('inf'):
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = shortest_path_via_i + 1  # +1 for including the edge i-j
        else:
            # If i is a source node, set heuristic for all j to infinity
            heuristics_matrix[i, :] = float('inf')

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def weighted_distance_heuristic(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of distances from each node to all other nodes
    node_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    # Calculate the sum of distances from all nodes to a specific reference node
    ref_node_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    # Calculate the absolute differences between these sums
    diff_matrix = np.abs(node_sums - ref_node_sums)
    
    # Normalize the differences by dividing by the sum of all differences
    norm_diff_matrix = diff_matrix / np.sum(diff_matrix)
    
    # Assign smaller values to nodes with larger neighborhoods
    # Larger neighborhood implies higher possibility of edges being undesirable
    # This is achieved by multiplying the normalized differences with the inverse of the neighborhood size (here assumed to be the number of edges)
    neighborhood_size = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    result_matrix = norm_diff_matrix * (1 / neighborhood_size[:, np.newaxis])
    
    return result_matrix

import pulp
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    milp = pulp.LpProblem("TravelingSalesman", pulp.LpMinimize)

    # Variables for each pair of cities (i,j)
    x = {(i, j): milp.variable(vtype=pulp.LpContinuous, cat='Continuous') for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)}

    # Objective function
    milp += pulp.lpSum([distance_matrix[i][j] * x[(i, j)] for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)])

    # Constraints
    for i in range(n):
        milp += pulp.lpSum([x[(i, j)] for j in range(n)]) == 1  # Each city is visited exactly once
    milp += pulp.lpSum([x[(i, j)] for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)]) == 1  # The tour ends at the starting city

    # Solve the MILP
    milp.solve()

    # Optimal tour
    tour = [None] * n
    for i in range(n):
        tour[i] = 0
        for j in range(n):
            if tour[j] is not None and x[(j, i)].value() > 0.5:
                tour[i] = j
                break

    # Undesirability score matrix
    undesirability_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if tour[i]!= j and tour[j]!= i:
                undesirability_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[tour[i]][tour[j]]
                undesirability_matrix[j, i] = undesirability_matrix[i, j]  # Reverse the score for edge (j,i)

    return undesirability_matrix
