import numpy as np
from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import rbf_kernel
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to a binary adjacency matrix (1s for connected pairs, 0s otherwise)
    adj_matrix = distance_matrix < 1
    n = len(adj_matrix)

    # Compute the betweenness centrality of each edge
    betweenness_centrality = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i, n):
            # Compute the product of the distance matrix entries between the i-th and j-th nodes
            product = np.prod(distance_matrix[i, :j] * distance_matrix[j, i:])
            # Compute the betweenness centrality using RBF kernel
            betweenness_centrality[i, j] = betweenness_centrality[j, i] = rbf_kernel(adj_matrix, i, j, gamma=1.0 / np.max(distance_matrix)) / product

    return betweenness_centrality

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_weights):
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros((num_nodes, num_nodes))

    # Calculate edge weights
    edge_weights = np.array(edge_weights) / np.sum(edge_weights)

    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:  # Avoid self-loops and duplicate edges
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] = edge_weights[i][j] * np.sqrt(distance_matrix[i][j] ** 2 + distance_matrix[j][i] ** 2)

    # Potential path length
    potential_path_lengths = np.diag(distance_matrix) + np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0) + np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1) - 2 * distance_matrix
    heuristics_matrix += potential_path_lengths

    # Deviation from optimal
    # This step is more complex and may require a specific model for the network.
    # For this example, let's assume a simple random deviation:
    deviation = np.random.rand(num_nodes, num_nodes) - 0.5  # -0.5 bias towards higher deviation
    heuristics_matrix += deviation

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure input is a valid distance matrix
    distance_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix)
    assert np.all(distance_matrix >= 0), "Distance matrix should be non-negative."
    assert np.all(np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1) == np.zeros((len(distance_matrix), len(distance_matrix)-1))), "Distance matrix should be lower-triangular."

    # Create a graph from the distance matrix
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Compute betweenness centrality
    betweenness = nx.betweenness_centrality(G, normalized=False)
    
    # Scale betweenness values to the range of the distance matrix
    min_distance = np.min(distance_matrix)
    max_distance = np.max(distance_matrix)
    betweenness_scaled = (betweenness - min(betweenness)) / (max(betweenness) - min(betweenness))
    
    # Adjust for the range of the original distance matrix
    betweenness_scaled = np.clip(betweenness_scaled, 0, 1)

    # Combine distance matrix and betweenness scores
    heuristics_matrix = np.stack([distance_matrix, betweenness_scaled], axis=1)

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def degree_centrality(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    degree_centrality = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                degree_centrality[i,j] = degree_of_node_i + degree_of_node_j
                degree_of_node_i = np.sum(distance_matrix[i])
                degree_of_node_j = np.sum(distance_matrix[j])
    
    return degree_centrality



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def dijkstra(graph, start):
    dist = {node: float('infinity') for node in graph}
    dist[start] = 0
    priority_queue = [(0, start)]
    
    while priority_queue:
        current_dist, current_node = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)
        
        if current_dist > dist[current_node]:
            continue
        
        for neighbor, weight in graph[current_node].items():
            distance = current_dist + weight
            
            if distance < dist[neighbor]:
                dist[neighbor] = distance
                heapq.heappush(priority_queue, (distance, neighbor))
    
    return dist



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a disjoint set data structure
    parent = list(range(len(distance_matrix)))

    def find(x):
        if parent[x]!= x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]

    def union(x, y):
        root_x = find(x)
        root_y = find(y)
        if root_x!= root_y:
            parent[root_x] = root_y

    # Kruskal's algorithm to maintain a set of edges forming an MST
    mst_edges = []
    edges_heap = [(distance_matrix[i][j], i, j) for i in range(len(distance_matrix)) for j in range(i+1, len(distance_matrix))]
    heapq.heapify(edges_heap)

    while edges_heap:
        cost, u, v = heapq.heappop(edges_heap)
        if find(u)!= find(v):  # Ensure they are not already connected
            union(u, v)
            mst_edges.append((u, v, cost))

    # Create the heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [[0] * len(distance_matrix) for _ in range(len(distance_matrix))]
    for u, v, _ in mst_edges:
        heuristics_matrix[u][v] = heuristics_matrix[v][u] = -distance_matrix[u][v]  # Necessary for symmetry

    return heuristics_matrix
```

This function works by constructing a Minimum Spanning Tree (MST) from the input distance matrix. The heuristic score for each edge is then the negative of its weight in the MST. The disjoint set data structure ensures that duplicate edges are not included in the MST, thus preventing over-counting of potential undesirable edges.

The score improvement would depend on the specific characteristics of the input distance matrix, but this approach should generally yield better results than simply returning the distance matrix, as it incorporates graph-theoretic insights about connectivity and local structure.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Dijkstra's algorithm for global heuristic: find the shortest paths from each node
    shortest_paths = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    global_scores = shortest_paths  # Each node is at most this distance from any other node

    # Local heuristic: avoid high-cost edges
    high_cost_edges = np.where(distance_matrix > 2 * global_scores[:, np.newaxis])  # Adjust the threshold as needed
    local_scores = global_scores[:, np.newaxis] - distance_matrix[high_cost_edges]  # Cost of replacing high-cost edges

    # Combine global and local scores
    heuristic_matrix = global_scores + local_scores

    # Negative scores to optimize minimization problem (edges with lower values are more desirable to include)
    heuristic_matrix = -heuristic_matrix

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Calculate the sum of effective resistances (distances) for each pair of nodes
    sum_of_distances = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Calculate the total possible distance for all edges in a complete graph
    total_possible_distance = n * (n - 1) / 2
    
    # Heuristics: (Sum of distances) - (Total possible distance)
    heuristics_matrix = sum_of_distances - total_possible_distance
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def PFR(distance_matrix, new_node):
    # Calculate the PFR for each existing node
    distances_to_existing = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    pfr_values = distance_matrix[new_node] - distances_to_existing
    
    return pfr_values



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def mst_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_vertices = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the minimum edge heaps with (weight, source, destination) pairs
    heaps = [[distance_matrix[i][j], i, j] for i in range(num_vertices) for j in range(i+1, num_vertices)]
    heapq.heapify(heaps)
    
    # Initialize the result matrix with zeros
    result = [[0] * num_vertices for _ in range(num_vertices)]
    
    # Process edges in increasing order of weight
    while heaps:
        # Get the edge with minimum weight
        weight, u, v = heapq.heappop(heaps)
        
        # If both endpoints are included in the tree, there's no need to add this edge
        if result[u][v]:
            continue
        
        # Include this edge in the tree and update the result matrix
        result[u][v] = result[v][u] = 1
        # Remove the other endpoint from the heaps
        if u!= v:
            heapq.heappush(heaps, [distance_matrix[u][w], u, w] for w in range(num_vertices) if w!= v)
    
    return result



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from sklearn.cluster import AgglomerativeClustering
from sklearn.preprocessing import normalize
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Normalize the distance matrix
    norm_dist = normalize(distance_matrix, norm='l2', axis=0)
    
    # Apply hierarchical clustering (AgglomerativeClustering with linkage 'ward')
    clustering = AgglomerativeClustering(n_clusters=None, linkage='ward')
    clusters = clustering.fit_predict(norm_dist)
    
    # Create a similar-shaped output matrix to store heuristic scores
    heuristic_score_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    # Assign heuristic scores based on density and connectivity within clusters
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if clusters[i] == clusters[j]:
                # If both vertices are in the same cluster, they are likely 'desirable'
                heuristic_score_matrix[i, j] = -np.log(distance_matrix[i, j] / np.mean(distance_matrix[clusters == clusters[i]]))
            else:
                # If they are in different clusters, they are likely 'undesirable'
                heuristic_score_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j]
    
    return heuristic_score_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Degree of connectivity heuristic
    degree = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Proximity to optimality heuristic
    optimal_distance = np.min(np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0))
    proximity = np.inf
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i+1, num_nodes):
            dist = distance_matrix[i, j]
            proximity = min(proximity, dist + optimal_distance)
    
    # Combine heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = degree + proximity - (distance_matrix.diagonal() * 2)
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Number of rows/columns in the distance matrix, assuming it's undirected
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same dimensions as the input
    heuristic_matrix = [row.copy() for row in distance_matrix]

    # Calculate the connection potential for each edge
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            # If i == j, this edge doesn't exist, so its connection potential is 0
            if i == j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = 0
            else:
                # Calculate the potential based on both the distance and the number of remaining edges
                potential = distance_matrix[i][j] * (num_nodes - distance_matrix.index(max(distance_matrix[i], distance_matrix[j])) - 1)  # Subtract one for the edge itself
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = potential

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the number of non-zero elements (edges) in the distance matrix
    num_edges = np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate the total number of possible edges (assuming a square matrix of size n x n)
    total_edges = num_edges * (num_edges - 1) // 2

    # Compute the density of the graph
    density = num_edges / total_edges

    # Multiply by a factor to emphasize the undesirability of sparse graphs
    return density * 10

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    m, n = len(distance_matrix), len(distance_matrix[0])
    # Create a new matrix to store the heuristic values
    heuristic_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(m)]
    
    # Add direct distance as a primary criterion
    for i in range(m):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][j]
    
    # Add proximity to previous decisions
    # Assuming previous decisions are stored in a similar manner, e.g., prev_decisions
    if prev_decisions is not None:
        for i in range(m):
            for j in range(n):
                if i > 0 and j > 0:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] += min(heuristic_matrix[i-1][j], heuristic_matrix[i][j-1])
    
    # Add importance based on edge weights (simplified by absolute values)
    for i in range(m):
        for j in range(n):
            if i > 0 and j > 0:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] += abs(distance_matrix[i][j])
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
    import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate degree centrality
    degree_centrality = np.sum(distance_matrix > 0, axis=1)

    # Calculate betweenness centrality using NetworkX (since it's not part of scipy)
    import networkx as nx
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix > 0)
    betweenness_centrality = nx.betweenness_centrality(G)

    # Calculate closeness centrality
    closeness_centrality = nx.closeness_centrality(G)

    # Normalize centrality scores to a common range (0 to 1)
    max_centrality = np.max([np.max(degree_centrality), np.max(betweenness_centrality), np.max(closeness_centrality)])
    normalized_centrality = (centrality - np.min([np.min(degree_centrality), np.min(betweenness_centrality), np.min(closeness_centrality)])) / max_centrality

    # Combine all centrality measures into a single matrix
    undesirability_score = np.column_stack((degree_centrality, betweenness_centrality, closeness_centrality))

    # Add some bias towards higher scores to ensure a positive range
    undesirability_score += 1e-6  # This prevents zero-crossing in optimization and maintains smoothness

    return undesirability_score

import numpy as np
def distance_priority_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the inverse of each element
    inverse_distances = 1 / distance_matrix
    # Normalize the inverse distances to form the priority scores
    priorities = (inverse_distances - inverse_distances.min()) / (inverse_distances.max() - inverse_distances.min())
    return priorities

import math
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the square root of each element in the distance matrix
    # This has the effect of making large distances more manageable
    heuristic_matrix = [math.sqrt(distance) for distance in distance_matrix]

    # Normalize to sum up to 1 for each row, so they represent probabilities
    total = sum(heuristic_matrix, [])
    normalized_heuristic_matrix = [h / total for h in heuristic_matrix]

    return normalized_heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the matrix is square
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    if n!= distance_matrix.shape[1]:
        raise ValueError("Input matrix should be square.")

    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate the weighted negative geodesic distances
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # Calculate the geodesic distance (shortest path)
            geodesic_distance = np.fmin(distance_matrix[i, j], distance_matrix[i, :].min(), distance_matrix[:, j].min())

            # Calculate the negative of the geodesic distance as the weight
            weight = -geodesic_distance

            # Distribute the weight evenly among all other edges
            for k in range(n):
                if k!= i and k!= j:
                    heuristic_matrix[i, k] -= weight
                    heuristic_matrix[k, j] -= weight

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)  # Number of nodes
    max_distance = max(max(row) for row in distance_matrix)  # Maximum distance in the matrix

    # Create a new matrix with the same dimensions
    heuristic_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]

    # Compute heuristic values for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = max_distance - distance_matrix[i][j]  # Subtract the edge distance

    return heuristic_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of each row
    row_sums = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Create a new matrix where each entry corresponds to the undesirability score
    # of including the corresponding edge in the solution
    undesirability_scores = 1 / row_sums
    
    # Ensure the matrix is non-negative by setting any potential negative scores to 0
    undesirability_scores[undesirability_scores < 0] = 0
    
    return undesirability_scores

import numpy as np
from sklearn.cluster import AgglomerativeClustering
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist
def advanced_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    d = pdist(distance_matrix)  # Calculate pairwise distances

    # Entropy for edge weights
    edge_weights = np.ones(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            edge_weights[i, j] = d[i, j]
            edge_weights[j, i] = edge_weights[i, j]

    entropy = -np.sum(edge_weights * np.log(edge_weights)) / n

    # Clustering coefficient
    avg_distance = np.mean(d)
    clustering_coefficient = np.mean(np.array([np.mean(d[np.where(cluster == cluster_idx)]) / avg_distance
                                              for cluster_idx in np.unique(AgglomerativeClustering(n_clusters=2).fit_predict(distance_matrix))]))

    # Shortest path distance
    shortest_paths = np.min(pdist(distance_matrix), axis=1)

    heuristics_matrix = np.empty(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i == j:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 0  # Diagonal elements are 0
            elif distance_matrix[i, j] < shortest_paths[i] + shortest_paths[j] + 1:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = (1 - entropy) * (1 - clustering_coefficient) + 0.5 * (distance_matrix[i, j] - shortest_paths[i] - shortest_paths[j])
            else:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = (1 - entropy) * (1 - clustering_coefficient)

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
from sklearn.metrics import normalized_cut_score
from collections import Counter
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Entropy measure of edge weights
    entropy = -np.sum(np.bincount(distance_matrix.flatten(), minlength=n**2)) / (n**2 - n)

    # Normalized Cut Score
    mst = minimum_spanning_tree(csgraph=csgraph_from_adjacency(distance_matrix))
    cut_score = normalized_cut_score(csgraph=mst, labels_true=np.arange(n))

    # Edge importance based on degree
    degree_count = Counter(distance_matrix.flatten())
    degree_heuristic = [count / sum(degree_count.values()) for count in degree_count.values()]

    # Hybrid heuristic function
    hybrid_heuristic = (
        entropy + 
        cut_score + 
        np.array(degree_heuristic) * 10  # Adjust the weight of degree heuristic
    )

    return hybrid_heuristic

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate graph density (average degree)
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    avg_degree = sum(sum(distance_matrix[i]) for i in range(n)) / (n * (n - 1))
    
    # Calculate individual edge heuristic (cost / density)
    heuristics_matrix = [
        [min(1.0, d / avg_degree) for d in dist] for dist in distance_matrix
    ]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute shortest path between all pairs using Floyd-Warshall algorithm
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    shortest_paths = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                shortest_paths[i, j] = min(shortest_paths[i, j], shortest_paths[i, k] + shortest_paths[k, j])
    
    # Square root transformation for heuristic adjustment
    sqrt_shortest_paths = np.sqrt(shortest_paths)
    
    # Apply a custom heuristic function (a simple example: multiply by a constant)
    # This can be replaced with a more complex function based on specific problem characteristics
    heuristic_factors = np.array([10, 5, 2, 1])
    heuristic_scores = distance_matrix * heuristic_factors[np.arange(n), np.arange(n)] * sqrt_shortest_paths
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def LKH_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    solution = np.random.permutation(n)  # Random partial solution
    prev_dist = np.sum(distance_matrix[solution[0], solution[1:]])  # Initial distance

    while True:
        improved = False
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(i+1, n):
                if solution[i]!= solution[j] and solution[i]!= (solution[j] + 1) % n and solution[j]!= (solution[i] + 1) % n:
                    curr_dist = prev_dist + distance_matrix[solution[i], solution[j]]
                    next_solution = np.insert(solution, j+1, i)
                    next_dist = np.sum(distance_matrix[next_solution[0], next_solution[1:]])
                    if curr_dist < next_dist:
                        solution = next_solution
                        prev_dist = curr_dist
                        improved = True
                        break
                if improved:
                    break
        
        if not improved:
            break
    
    # Create heuristic matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristics_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[solution[i], solution[j]] if i <= j else distance_matrix[solution[i], solution[(i+1) % n]]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def betweenness_centrality_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adjacency_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))

    # Construct adjacency matrix
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j]!= 0:  # only consider non-zero distances
                adjacency_matrix[i, j] = 1
                adjacency_matrix[j, i] = 1

    # Calculate betweenness centrality
    betw_centrality = np.zeros((n, n))
    for _ in range(2 * n - 2):  # 2*n-2 is the number of edges in a complete graph
        for j in range(n):
            delta = np.copy(adjacency_matrix)
            delta[j] = 0
            delta[j][j] = 0
            delta[j] += np.eye(n) * adjacency_matrix[j]
            betw_centrality += (adjacency_matrix * (np.linalg.matrix_power(delta, 2) - delta)) * (1 / np.sum(adjacency_matrix))

    # Normalize betweenness centrality to get undesirability score
    betw_centrality_norm = np.maximum(betw_centrality, 0) / np.sum(betw_centrality)

    # Ensure result is of the same shape as input distance matrix
    betw_centrality_norm = betw_centrality_norm.reshape(distance_matrix.shape)

    return betw_centrality_norm



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Get the dimensions of the input matrix
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Compute the distance from each node to every other node
    # Using Floyd-Warshall algorithm for all-pairs shortest paths
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                distance_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])

    # Create a parent array to trace the path from each node to the root
    parent = np.zeros((n, n), dtype=int)
    rank = [0] * n

    def find(x):
        if parent[x][x]!= x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x][x])  # Path compression
        return parent[x][x]

    def union(x, y):
        root_x = find(x)
        root_y = find(y)

        if root_x == root_y:
            return

        if rank[root_x] > rank[root_y]:
            parent[root_y] = root_x
        elif rank[root_x] < rank[root_y]:
            parent[root_x] = root_y
        else:
            parent[root_y] = root_x
            rank[root_x] += 1

    # Kruskal's Algorithm using Key Path
    mst_edges = []
    i, e = 0, 0
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i][j] < float('inf'):
                e += 1
                mst_edges.append((i, j, distance_matrix[i][j]))
                union(i, j)

    return np.array(mst_edges).reshape(e, 3)
```

This function uses Kruskal's algorithm with the key path optimization to calculate the heuristic values, which may lead to a more accurate ranking of edges. The function returns an array of shape (e, 3), where e is the number of edges in the MST, and each row contains the source, destination, and weight of an edge in the MST.

Please note that the score for this function is not provided since it depends on the specific dataset and problem context. You should evaluate this function in your particular use case to determine its performance.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from sklearn.neighbors import NearestNeighbors
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Perform LSH for similarity ranking
    lsh = NearestNeighbors(n_neighbors=2, algorithm='auto', metric='precomputed')
    lsh.fit(distance_matrix)
    _, idx = lsh.kneighbors(distance_matrix)
    
    # Create a new heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            # Greedy optimization: Choose the lower-ranked neighbor
            lower_ranked_idx = np.argmin(idx[i][j + 1:]) + j + 1
            heuristics_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] + distance_matrix[i, lower_ranked_idx]
            heuristics_matrix[j, i] = heuristics_matrix[i, j]
    
    # Normalize the heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = (heuristics_matrix - np.min(heuristics_matrix)) / (np.max(heuristics_matrix) - np.min(heuristics_matrix))
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Convert distance matrix into a list of edges and their weights
    edges = [(distance_matrix[i][j], i, j) for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)]
    # Sort edges by weight
    edges.sort()

    # Initialize MST and result matrix
    mst = []
    heuristics_matrix = [[0]*n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Kruskal's algorithm
    for edge_weight, u, v in edges:
        if len(mst) < n-1:
            # Add the edge if it doesn't form a cycle
            if not any(mst[i][1] == u and mst[i][2] == v for i in range(len(mst))):
                mst.append(edge_weight)
                heapq.heappush(edges, (0, u, v))  # Re-add edge with 0 weight for next iterations
        else:
            # If MST is complete, stop
            break

    # Assign heuristics
    for u, v in mst:
        heuristics_matrix[u][v] = distance_matrix[u][v] - heuristics_matrix[v][u]  # Make sure heuristics are negative for better scoring

    # For edges not in MST, assign higher negative values
    for u, v in [(u, v) for u in range(n) for v in range(u+1, n) if (u, v) not in edges]:
        heuristics_matrix[u][v] = -distance_matrix[u][v]

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

    # Calculate the novelty factor for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:  # Avoid self-loops
                neighbors = [k for k in range(n) if (i!= k and j!= k)]
                differences = [abs(distance_matrix[i][j] - distance_matrix[i][k]) + abs(distance_matrix[i][j] - distance_matrix[j][k]) for k in neighbors]
                novelty_factor = sum(differences)
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] = 1 / novelty_factor  # Inverse of novelty factor to penalize highly out-of-the-ordinary edges

    return heuristics_matrix

            impact_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] - scaling_factor*(i + j)  # Adjust scaling factor as needed

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initial value to a large number
    max_score = 100000
    
    # Calculate weighted sum of distances
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            weight = (1 / (distance_matrix[i][j] + 1))  # Using a small value to avoid division by zero
            max_score = min(max_score, distance_matrix[i][j] * weight)
    
    # Add a simple connectivity factor
    connectivity_score = 0
    for k in range(n):
        for l in range(k+1, n):
            connectivity_score += min(distance_matrix[k][l], distance_matrix[l][k])
    
    max_score += connectivity_score
    
    # Normalize the score to be between 0 and 1
    max_score /= (n * (n-1) / 2)
    
    return max_score



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Compute the average distance to neighboring nodes
    avg_neighbor_distance = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Step 2: Compute the density of neighboring nodes for each node
    node_densities = np.sum(distance_matrix > 0, axis=1) / (distance_matrix.shape[1] - 1)
    
    # Step 3: Combine these two factors into a heuristic score
    heuristic_scores = -avg_neighbor_distance + node_densities  # Lower scores are better
    
    # Ensure the heuristic scores are non-negative
    heuristic_scores = np.clip(heuristic_scores, 0, np.inf)
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the heap with the first unvisited node and its edge weight
    heap = [(distance_matrix[0][1], 0, 1)]
    visited = set([0])
    unvisited_neighbors = set(range(1, n))
    
    # Initialize the result matrix
    result = [0] * n
    result[0] = distance_matrix[0][1]
    
    while unvisited_neighbors:
        # Get the smallest edge from the heap
        min_weight, u, v = heapq.heappop(heap)
        
        # If the destination node 'v' is already in the visited set, skip it
        if v in visited:
            continue
        
        # Include the edge in the result and mark the destination node as visited
        result[v] = min_weight
        visited.add(v)
        unvisited_neighbors.remove(v)
        
        # Add neighbors of 'v' to the heap
        for w in unvisited_neighbors:
            heapq.heappush(heap, (distance_matrix[v][w], v, w))
    
    return result



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_weights):
    # Check if the dimensions of distance_matrix and edge_weights match
    if len(distance_matrix)!= len(edge_weights) or len(distance_matrix[0])!= len(edge_weights[0]):
        raise ValueError("Distance matrix and edge weights must have the same dimensions.")
    
    # Initialize heuristics matrix with the same shape as distance_matrix
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Iterate through each edge (i, j)
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(len(distance_matrix[0])):
            # If there's an edge weight, incorporate it into the heuristic
            if edge_weights[i][j] is not None:
                # Calculate the cost to connect nodes i and j by adding the distance and the weight
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][j] + edge_weights[i][j]
            # If there's no edge weight, just add the distance
            else:
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] += distance_matrix[i][j]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_ shortest_paths
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Compute the shortest path matrix using scipy's csgraph
    shortest_path = csgraph_shortest_paths(csgraph=csgraph_from_dense(distance_matrix),
                                         method='dijkstra')

    # Calculate the edge betweenness centrality
    betweenness_centrality = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            path_length = shortest_path[i, j]
            num_paths = np.sum(np.isfinite(shortest_path[i, :])) * np.sum(np.isfinite(shortest_path[:, j]))
            if path_length < n:
                betweenness_centrality[i, j] = np.sum((shortest_path[i, :][np.argsort(shortest_path[i, :])] == j) & (shortest_path[:, j][np.argsort(shortest_path[:, j])] == i)) / (num_paths - 1)
            elif path_length == n:
                betweenness_centrality[i, j] = 0

    # Normalize betweenness centrality to achieve a matrix of values between 0 and 1
    betweenness_centrality = (betweenness_centrality - np.min(betweenness_centrality)) / (np.max(betweenness_centrality) - np.min(betweenness_centrality))

    return betweenness_centrality



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance matrix to adjacency matrix
    adj_matrix = pdist(distance_matrix, 'euclidean')
    
    # Create a minimum spanning tree (MST) using Prim's algorithm
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    parent = np.zeros(n, dtype=int)
    rank = np.zeros(n, dtype=int)
    mst_edges = 0
    for i in range(n):
        parent[i] = -1
    
    def find(x):
        if parent[x]!= x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]

    def union(x, y):
        rootX = find(x)
        rootY = find(y)
        if rootX == rootY:
            return
        if rank[rootX] < rank[rootY]:
            parent[rootX] = rootY
        elif rank[rootX] > rank[rootY]:
            parent[rootY] = rootX
        else:
            parent[rootY] = rootX
            rank[rootX] += 1
        mst_edges += 1

    for i in range(n):
        min_val = np.inf
        min_idx = -1
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j and adj_matrix[i][j] < min_val:
                min_val = adj_matrix[i][j]
                min_idx = j
        if min_idx!= -1:
            union(i, min_idx)
    
    # Calculate Primal Heuristic score
    heuristic_scores = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_scores[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], adj_matrix[i][j])
                heuristic_scores[j][i] = heuristic_scores[i][j]  # to ensure symmetry
    
    return heuristic_scores
```

This function first converts the input distance matrix into an adjacency matrix, then applies Prim's algorithm to construct a minimum spanning tree (MST). It subsequently computes the Primal Heuristic score for each edge by taking the minimum of the input distance and the MST distance, ensuring that the scores are non-negative.

The score achieved with this function should be better than the previous two, as it takes into account the global structure of the problem by creating a tree that spans all nodes, and it uses the minimum spanning tree to approximate the optimal tour. This method should result in a lower average path length in the resulting Hamiltonian cycle, and thus a better heuristic score.

Remember, the performance of this function will largely depend on the specific characteristics of your problem instances, such as the scale and sparsity of the input matrices. You may need to fine-tune this or other aspects based on your specific use case.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
import random
def heuristics(distance_matrix, tabu_list=None, temperature=1000, alpha=0.9, max_iterations=1000):
    """
    This function computes a heuristic matrix indicating the undesirability of including each edge in a solution.

    Parameters:
    - distance_matrix (numpy array): A square matrix of non-negative distances between nodes.
    - tabu_list (list, optional): List storing indices of recently visited nodes (for tabu list). If None, no tabu list is used.
    - temperature (float, optional): Current temperature in the simulated annealing process (default is 1000).
    - alpha (float, optional): Cooling rate for the simulated annealing process (default is 0.9).
    - max_iterations (int, optional): Maximum number of iterations for the simulated annealing process (default is 1000).

    Returns:
    - numpy array: A matrix of the same shape as the input, indicating the undesirability of including each edge.
    """

    # Initialize the heuristic matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize the current node and its path cost
    current_node = 0
    current_path_cost = 0
    visited_nodes = set()

    # Run simulated annealing
    for _ in range(max_iterations):
        # Generate a neighbor
        neighbors = [node for node in range(len(distance_matrix)) if (node, current_node) in distance_matrix.indices and (current_node, node) not in visited_nodes]
        if neighbors:
            neighbor_node = random.choice(neighbors)
            neighbor_cost = distance_matrix[current_node, neighbor_node]

            # Check tabu list
            if tabu_list is not None and neighbor_node in tabu_list:
                continue

            # Calculate potential gain and accept/reject neighbor based on simulated annealing
            gain = neighbor_cost - current_path_cost
            if gain > 0 or np.exp(gain / temperature) > random.random():
                current_node = neighbor_node
                current_path_cost = neighbor_cost

                # Add current node to the tabu list (if tabu list is used)
                if tabu_list is not None:
                    tabu_list.remove(current_node)

                # Mark current node as visited
                visited_nodes.add(current_node)

        # Update heuristic matrix with the cost of the current path
        heuristic_matrix[current_node, current_node] = current_path_cost

        # Reduce temperature
        temperature *= alpha

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Density Measure (Number of Edges / Max Possible Edges)
    num_edges = np.sum(distance_matrix) / 2
    max_edges = len(distance_matrix) * (len(distance_matrix) - 1)
    density = num_edges / max_edges

    # Step 2: Directionality Heuristic (Probability of Edge Direction)
    # We assume all edges are unidirectional for this simplified model.
    # In a more complex scenario, you can replace this with a learned model.
    directionality_heuristic = 1 / len(distance_matrix)

    # Step 3: Structural Properties Heuristic (Weighted Sum of Neighbors)
    # We calculate a heuristic for each node by summing the weight of its neighbors.
    # Heavier neighbors should contribute less to this heuristic.
    # The weights could be based on various structural features like degree, clustering coefficient, etc.
    # For simplicity, we use a simple degree-based weight.
    node_heuristics = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)  # For each node
    weighted_neighbors = np.take(distance_matrix, np.arange(len(distance_matrix))[::-1])  # Reverse order for weighting
    combined_heuristic = node_heuristics * weighted_neighbors

    # Step 4: Combine the Heuristics
    # Linearly combine the above heuristics. Weights should be tuned based on specific problem requirements.
    combined_score = 0.4 * directionality_heuristic + 0.4 * density + 0.2 * combined_heuristic

    # Return the combined heuristic matrix
    return combined_score



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a diagonal matrix of the same size with the diagonal elements as the sum of each row in the distance matrix
    row_sums = np.diag(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1))
    
    # Calculate the shortest path between each pair of nodes (using Floyd-Warshall algorithm for efficiency)
    def floyd_warshall(dist):
        n = len(dist)
        for k in range(n):
            for i in range(n):
                for j in range(n):
                    dist[i][j] = min(dist[i][j], dist[i][k] + dist[k][j])
        return dist

    # Compute the tentative shortest paths
    tentative_shortest_paths = floyd_warshall(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate edge heuristics: negative of the shortest path
    # The idea is that an edge between nodes i and j with a shorter path will be less undesirable
    heuristics_matrix = -tentative_shortest_paths
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def bottleneck_distance(x, y):
    # Calculate the Euclidean distance between each pair of points (x, y)
    distances = np.linalg.norm(np.stack((x, y), axis=0) - np.stack((x, y), axis=0), axis=1)
    return np.max(distances)

import numpy as np
def edge_connectivity_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    connectivity = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate the minimum cut-set for each vertex
    for i in range(n):
        # For each vertex, find the minimum-weight edge connecting it to a non-i vertex
        min_weight_edge_to_other_vertex = np.min(distance_matrix[i, np.where(distance_matrix[i] > 0)])
        
        # Subtract this weight from the edges connected to i
        connectivity[i, np.where(distance_matrix[i] > 0)] -= min_weight_edge_to_other_vertex
    
    return connectivity

import itertools
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Calculate the total distance if the current edge doesn't exist
    unlinked_distances = [sum(row) for row in distance_matrix]
    
    # Calculate the total distance if the current edge exists
    linked_distances = [sum(row) - distance_matrix[i][j] for i, j in itertools.combinations(range(num_nodes), 2) if i!= j]
    
    # Add the benefits of linking (decrease in total distance) to the heuristics matrix
    for i, linked_distance in enumerate(linked_distances):
        heuristics_matrix[i][i] -= linked_distance
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize heuristic matrix with the same size as distance matrix
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Calculate distances in both directions
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
            heuristic_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j]  # For undirected graphs
    
    # Calculate connectivity factor
    connectivity = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:  # Avoid self-loops
                connectivity[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] / min(distance_matrix[i], distance_matrix[j])
    
    # Combine distance and connectivity to calculate final heuristic
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:  # Avoid self-loops
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] += connectivity[i][j]
    
    return heuristic_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    nad_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

    # Iterate through each node
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Check only nodes that are not the same as i or j
            if i!= j:
                # Calculate the average distance to neighboring nodes
                num_neighbors = 0
                sum_distance = 0
                for k in range(n):
                    if k!= i and k!= j:
                        sum_distance += distance_matrix[i][k]
                        num_neighbors += 1
                nad_matrix[i][j] = nad_matrix[j][i] = sum_distance / num_neighbors if num_neighbors > 0 else 0  # Avoid division by zero

    return nad_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def weighted_nearest_neighbor(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    visited = [False] * n
    path = []

    def nearest_neighbor(current):
        nonlocal path, visited
        min_dist = float('inf')
        nearest = -1

        for i in range(n):
            if not visited[i] and distance_matrix[current, i] < min_dist:
                min_dist = distance_matrix[current, i]
                nearest = i

        path.append(nearest)
        visited[nearest] = True
        return nearest

    def extend_path(current):
        nonlocal path, visited

        nearest = nearest_neighbor(current)

        if len(path) == n - 1:  # Path is complete
            return

        # Consider edge weights in next step
        next_node = min(range(n), key=lambda x: distance_matrix[current, x])
        extend_path(next_node)

    extend_path(0)
    return path
```

The `weighted_nearest_neighbor` function should provide a more insightful heuristic than the initial distance matrix return. It considers the edge weights, potentially capturing more of the problem's structure and leading to a better score. However, note that the actual score improvement will depend on the specific characteristics of the input distance matrices.

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    undesirability_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Step 1: Calculate the average weight of edges connected to each node
    avg_edge_weight_to_node = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Step 2: Identify high-weight, isolated edges (bottlenecks)
    isolated_bottlenecks = np.max(distance_matrix, axis=1) - avg_edge_weight_to_node
    
    # Step 3: Estimate the potential cost of adding or removing these bottlenecks
    potential_cost = isolated_bottlenecks * (num_nodes - 1)
    
    # Step 4: Calculate the total undesirability of an edge, considering bottlenecks and its position
    undesirability_matrix = avg_edge_weight_to_node + potential_cost
    
    return undesirability_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    """
    Calculate a heuristic matrix for each edge, indicating how undesirable it is to include it in a solution.
    
    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (numpy.ndarray): A 2D numpy array representing the distance matrix of the TSP.
    
    Returns:
    numpy.ndarray: A 2D numpy array of the same shape as distance_matrix, containing edge heuristics.
    """
    
    # Calculate the total length of the shortest route that includes the current edge
    total_shortest_route = np.min(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0), axis=0) + np.min(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1), axis=1)
    
    # Calculate the length of the current edge
    edge_length = distance_matrix[np.unravel_index(np.argmin(total_shortest_route), total_shortest_route.shape)]
    
    # Apply 2-opt heuristic for edge undesirability
    heuristics = np.where(distance_matrix == edge_length, total_shortest_route - edge_length, np.inf)
    
    return heuristics



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # First, let's normalize the distance matrix to be zero-based
    distance_matrix = distance_matrix - 1

    # Initialize the result matrix with the same shape as the input
    result_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()

    # Iterate over each element in the matrix
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(len(distance_matrix[i])):
            if i!= j:  # Ignore diagonal elements
                # For each edge (i, j), calculate its heuristic score
                edge_score = sum(min(d1, d2) for d1, d2 in zip(distance_matrix[i], distance_matrix[:, j]))

                # Assign this score to the corresponding element in result_matrix
                result_matrix[i][j] = edge_score

    return result_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def prim_mst(weight_matrix):
    # Initialize MST with a random vertex
    mst = set([0])
    heap = [(0, 0)]  # (distance, vertex)

    while mst!= set(range(len(weight_matrix))):
        # Get the smallest edge in the MST
        dist, u = heapq.heappop(heap)

        for v, w in enumerate(weight_matrix[u]):
            if v not in mst:
                heapq.heappush(heap, (w, v))
                mst.add(v)
                break

    return weight_matrix[u]



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def shortest_path(distance_matrix, start_vertex):
    num_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    visited = np.zeros(num_vertices, dtype=bool)
    predecessor = np.empty(num_vertices, dtype=int)
    distance = np.Inf * np.ones(num_vertices, dtype=float)
    distance[start_vertex] = 0

    queue = [(0, start_vertex)]

    while queue:
        current_distance, current_vertex = queue.pop(0)

        if current_distance > distance[current_vertex]:
            continue

        for neighbor, edge_cost in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_vertex]):
            if visited[neighbor] or edge_cost == float('Inf'):
                continue

            new_distance = current_distance + edge_cost
            if new_distance < distance[neighbor]:
                distance[neighbor] = new_distance
                predecessor[neighbor] = current_vertex
                queue.append((new_distance, neighbor))
                visited[neighbor] = True

    return distance, predecessor



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the number of nodes (N) from the shape of the distance_matrix
    N = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Initialize a matrix of zeros with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_values = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate Expected Shortest Path (ESP) for each node
    for i in range(N):
        # Current node
        curr_node = i
        
        # Initialize the set of outgoing nodes for this node
        outgoing_nodes = set(range(N))
        outgoing_nodes.remove(curr_node)

        # Initialize list to hold future distances
        future_distances = [0] * N

        # Calculate ESP
        for _ in range(10):  # Adjust this number for accuracy-performance trade-off
            # Generate future potential edge costs
            future_edge_costs = np.random.exponential(scale=1, size=len(outgoing_nodes))
            
            # Update future distances considering both current and potential future costs
            future_distances = [distance_matrix[curr_node, j] + min(future_edge_costs) for j in outgoing_nodes]

            # Sort future distances to form a priority queue
            future_distances.sort()

            # Update the heuristic value for each outgoing node
            for j in outgoing_nodes:
                heuristic_values[curr_node, j] = distance_matrix[curr_node, j] + future_distances[0]

                # Remove the chosen edge from the future distances
                future_distances[0] += distance_matrix[curr_node, j]
                outgoing_nodes.remove(j)

    return heuristic_values

def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    heuristic_matrix = [[0.0 for _ in range(num_nodes)] for _ in range(num_nodes)]

    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:
                # Calculate the disruption caused by including the edge (i, j)
                disruption = distance_matrix[i][j] + min(distance_matrix[i][k] for k in range(num_nodes) if k!= i and k!= j)
                # Add some base value to ensure non-negative heuristics
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = disruption + 1.0

    # Normalize heuristic values so they can be compared directly
    max_heuristic = max(map(max, heuristic_matrix))
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] /= max_heuristic

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize an effective distance matrix
    effective_distance = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Apply Floyd-Warshall algorithm to calculate effective distances
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                effective_distance[i, j] = min(effective_distance[i, j],
                                             distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j])
    
    # Add a penalty to longer distances
    penalty = np.where(effective_distance > distance_matrix,
                       distance_matrix - effective_distance, 0)
    
    return penalty

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    m, n = distance_matrix.shape
    heuristic_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)  # Start with the input distance matrix

    for i in range(m):
        for j in range(n):
            # Check the triangle inequality for every edge (i, j)
            if i!= j:
                # Check if j is closer to k (for some k > j) than it is to i
                for k in range(j+1, n):
                    if distance_matrix[i, k] < distance_matrix[j, k]:
                        # If yes, increment the heuristic value for edge (i, j)
                        heuristic_matrix[i, j] += 100  # Arbitrarily scale the heuristic value
                        heuristic_matrix[j, i] += 100  # Reflect the change in the transpose matrix

    return heuristic_matrix

# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the number of edges (i.e., pairs of nodes connected)
    n_edges = distance_matrix.shape[0] * distance_matrix.shape[1] - np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix == 0)
    
    # Initialize the heuristics matrix with zeros
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    # Compute the average distance for each node
    avg_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Assign a penalty for including edges in long paths
    long_path_penalty = np.max(avg_distances) / np.min(avg_distances)
    
    # Compute the heuristics for each edge
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i!= j:
                # Distance between nodes i and j
                dist = distance_matrix[i, j]
                
                # Penalty for long paths (between nodes i and j)
                path_penalty = dist / long_path_penalty
                
                # Bonus for short paths (between closely-located nodes)
                node_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix[i, :j+1] + distance_matrix[j+1:, :i])
                node_connection_bonus = np.mean(node_distances) / np.min(node_distances)
                
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = path_penalty - node_connection_bonus
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Create a weighted graph using the distance_matrix
    weights = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Normalize weights by node degrees
    weights /= degrees[:, np.newaxis]
    
    # Calculate shortest paths using MST
    mst_weights, _ = minimum_spanning_tree(csgraph=weights, directed=False)
    
    # Compute local optimality heuristic (2nd-nearest neighbor)
    neighbor_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    neighbor_matrix[range(n), np.argmin(distance_matrix, axis=0)] = np.inf
    neighbor_matrix[np.argmin(neighbor_matrix, axis=0), range(n)] = np.inf
    local_opt_heuristic = np.min(neighbor_matrix, axis=0) / np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate average number of times each edge has been chosen
    edge_counts = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    avg_edge_count = edge_counts / np.sum(edge_counts)
    
    # Combine all metrics into a single heuristic score
    heuristic_scores = -1 * (mst_weights + local_opt_heuristic + avg_edge_count)
    
    return heuristic_scores

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Assuming distance_matrix is a 2D numpy array for a grid-like structure
    # Calculate the Manhattan distance for each edge
    heuristic_matrix = np.abs(np.subtract.outer(distance_matrix, np.transpose(distance_matrix)))
    
    # Normalize heuristic values between 1 and 100 for a better comparison
    min_val = np.min(heuristic_matrix)
    max_val = np.max(heuristic_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = (heuristic_matrix - min_val) / (max_val - min_val) * 100
    
    return heuristic_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np
    
    # Step 1: Calculate inverse distances (higher inverse = shorter paths)
    inverse_distances = 1.0 / distance_matrix
    
    # Step 2: Normalize the inverse distances to sum up to 1
    normalized_inverse_distances = inverse_distances / np.sum(inverse_distances)
    
    # Step 3: Convert the normalized inverse distances to a heuristic score matrix
    heuristic_scores = normalized_inverse_distances.astype(float)
    
    return heuristic_scores

    def __init__(self):
        super(GraphEmbedding, self).__init__()
        # Initialize GCN layers
        self.conv1 = GraphConvolution(input_dim=distance_matrix.shape[0], hidden_dim=32, activation=torch.relu)
        self.conv2 = GraphConvolution(input_dim=32, hidden_dim=64, activation=torch.relu)
        self.fc = torch.nn.Linear(64, 1)

    def forward(self, x, adj):
        x = self.conv1(x, adj)
        x = F.relu(x)
        x = self.conv2(x, adj)
        x = F.relu(x)
        x = torch.sigmoid(self.fc(x))
        return x

def graph_embedding(distance_matrix, adj_matrix):
    device = torch.device('cuda' if torch.cuda.is_available() else 'cpu')
    embedding = GraphEmbedding().to(device)

    # Preprocessing: Standardize and reshape
    scaler = StandardScaler()
    distance_matrix = scaler.fit_transform(distance_matrix.reshape(1, -1))
    adj_matrix = scaler.fit_transform(adj_matrix.reshape(1, -1))

    # Create graphs
    graphs = [torch.tensor(distance_matrix, dtype=torch.float32).to(device)]
    graph_list = [graphs]
    adj_list = [adj_matrix.reshape(-1, 1).repeat(1, adj_matrix.shape[1]).view(-1, -1).to(device)]

    # Forward pass for embedding
    output = embedding(graphs[0], adj_list[0])
    return output.cpu().numpy()

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    """
    This function calculates the RDW heuristics for each edge in the distance matrix.
    It prioritizes smaller distances and down-weights larger distances, aiming to favor more efficient paths.
    
    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (list of lists): A 2D list representing the distance matrix.
    
    Returns:
    list of lists: A new matrix where each element indicates the relative undesirability of including that edge.
    """

    # Calculate the maximum distance in the matrix to normalize
    max_distance = max(max(row) for row in distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the RDW for each element in the matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [[(1 / (d + 1)) for d in row] for row in distance_matrix]
    
    # Normalize by the maximum distance
    for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
        for j in range(len(distance_matrix[0])):
            heuristics_matrix[i][j] *= max_distance / (max_distance + distance_matrix[i][j])
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_from_dense
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import depth_first_order
from networkx.algorithms.centrality import betweenness_centrality
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a graph from the distance_matrix
    graph = csgraph_from_dense(distance_matrix)
    
    # Get the number of nodes
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate node degrees
    node_degrees = np.sum(graph, axis=0)
    
    # Calculate betweenness centrality
    betweenness_centrality_scores = betweenness_centrality(csgraph_from_dense(graph), n)
    
    # Create an undesirability matrix of the same shape as the input
    undesirability = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Fill in undesirability based on distance, node degree, and betweenness centrality
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            # Distance-based undesirability
            undesirability[i, j] += distance_matrix[i, j]
            
            # Node degree-based undesirability
            undesirability[i, j] += node_degrees[j]
            
            # Betweenness centrality-based undesirability
            undesirability[i, j] -= betweenness_centrality_scores[i] * distance_matrix[i, j]
    
    return undesirability

    max_centrality = max(degree_centrality.values())
    normalized_centrality = {node: centrality / max_centrality for node, centrality in degree_centrality.items()}
    
    # Return the normalized degree centrality as a matrix
    return np.array(list(normalized_centrality.values()))



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get dimensions of the distance matrix
    rows, cols = distance_matrix.shape
    
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros, same shape as input
    heuristic = np.zeros((rows, cols))
    
    # Iterate over each node
    for i in range(rows):
        for j in range(cols):
            # Consider direct distance and two-hop distances for the heuristic
            effective_distance = distance_matrix[i][j]
            for k in range(rows):
                if k!= i and k!= j:
                    effective_distance += distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j]
            
            # Set the heuristic value
            heuristic[i][j] = effective_distance
    
    return heuristic

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_betweenness_centrality
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance matrix to a sparse graph
    graph = csgraph_betweenness centrality(csgraph=distance_matrix)
    
    # Convert the betweenness centrality matrix to a heuristic matrix
    # The value at position (i, j) indicates how undesirable it is to include edge (i, j)
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(i + 1, distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = heuristic_matrix[j, i] = graph[i, j]
            heuristic_matrix[j, i] = heuristic_matrix[i, j] = 1 / graph[i, j]  # to ensure non-negativity
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Check if the input is a 2D numpy array
    assert len(distance_matrix.shape) == 2, "Input should be a 2D array"
    
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Create adjacency matrix from distance matrix
    adjacency_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i][j]!= 0:
                adjacency_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
                adjacency_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j]  # Assuming undirected graph
    
    # Calculate weighted degree centrality for each node
    weighted_degree_centrality = np.sum(adjacency_matrix, axis=1)
    
    # Calculate heuristic score for each edge
    heuristic_scores = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # Score is the product of the edge weight and the sum of weights of its neighbors
            heuristic_scores[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] * weighted_degree_centrality[i] + 
                                 distance_matrix[j][i] * weighted_degree_centrality[j]
            heuristic_scores[j][i] = heuristic_scores[i][j]  # Assuming undirected graph
    
    return heuristic_scores



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    num_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    edge_weights = distance_matrix.flatten()
    vertex_degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    avg_edge_weight_per_vertex = edge_weights / (num_vertices - 1)  # Subtract 1 because we're considering each vertex as a vertex-target pair

    heuristics_matrix = -edge_weights  # Initialize as -1 for each edge (to be adjusted later)

    for i in range(num_vertices):
        for j in range(i+1, num_vertices):  # Only compare vertices that are not the same
            heuristics_matrix[i*num_vertices + j, 0] = -edge_weights[i*num_vertices + j]  # Set weight
            heuristics_matrix[i*num_vertices + j, 1] = (vertex_degrees[i] + 1) / avg_edge_weight_per_vertex[i]  # Degree and average weight
            heuristics_matrix[j*num_vertices + i, 0] = heuristics_matrix[i*num_vertices + j, 0]  # Symmetry

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # A constant value to ensure all edge weights are considered undesirable initially
    initial_undesirability = 1000

    # Create a copy of the distance matrix to avoid modifying the original
    undesirability_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()

    num_nodes = undesirability_matrix.shape[0]

    # Iterate 2-Opt for 'num_nodes' times
    for _ in range(num_nodes):
        # Find the shortest edge
        shortest_edge = min(zip(undesirability_matrix, np.diag(undesirability_matrix)), key=lambda x: x[0])
        
        # Edge indices
        u, v = shortest_edge[1][0], shortest_edge[1][1]

        # Reverse this edge
        reversed_edge = (v, u)
        reversed_undesirability = undesirability_matrix[u, v] + undesirability_matrix[v, u]

        # If the reversed edge is shorter, update the undesirability
        if reversed_undesirability < undesirability_matrix[u, v]:
            undesirability_matrix[u, v] = reversed_undesirability

    return undesirability_matrix

# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    m, _ = distance_matrix.shape

    # Initialize a matrix with the same dimensions as the input distance_matrix
    # to store the heuristic values
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Perform the Floyd-Warshall algorithm to compute the all-pairs shortest paths
    for k in range(m):
        for i in range(m):
            for j in range(m):
                # The potential negative impact is determined by the shortest path between i and j that goes through k
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = max(heuristic_matrix[i, j], distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j] - distance_matrix[i, j])

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of absolute differences from the shortest path for each edge
    diff_matrix = np.abs(distance_matrix - np.triu(np.ones(distance_matrix.shape), k=1))
    # Calculate the weights by taking the sum along the diagonal and multiplying by -1
    weights = np.diagonal(diff_matrix)
    return weights

import numpy as np
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
from scipy.cluster.hierarchy import dendrogram, linkage
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Calculate pairwise distance matrix
    dist_matrix = squareform(pdist(distance_matrix))

    # Cluster neighbors using hierarchical clustering
    link_matrix = linkage(distance_matrix, method='ward')
    # The linkage matrix contains distance values between clusters
    cluster_distances = np.min(link_matrix[:, -1], axis=0)

    # Calculate clustering coefficient
    # The clustering coefficient is the average local clustering coefficient
    # We use the pairwise connectivity matrix to compute this
    connectivity_matrix = (dist_matrix < 1).astype(int)
    clustering_coefficient = np.mean(np.sum(connectivity_matrix, axis=0) / (n - 1))

    # Path length heuristic
    # Here we use the average shortest path length in the graph
    # We'll assume a random starting node and calculate the shortest path
    path_length = np.mean(np.min(dijkstra(distance_matrix), axis=1))

    # Combine these heuristics into a single matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    heuristic_matrix += dist_matrix  # basic distance
    heuristic_matrix += cluster_distances  # consider neighbor's neighbor distances
    heuristic_matrix += clustering_coefficient  # consider local clustering
    heuristic_matrix += path_length  # consider overall connectivity

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]

    # Calculate the heuristic value for each edge
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i, n):
            # Find the minimum cost to reach nodes i and j from the rest of the graph
            min_cost_path_i = [float('inf')] * n
            min_cost_path_j = [float('inf')] * n
            for k in range(n):
                if k!= i and k!= j:
                    min_cost_path_i[k] = min(min_cost_path_i[k], distance_matrix[i][k] + min_cost_path_i[k])
                    min_cost_path_j[k] = min(min_cost_path_j[k], distance_matrix[j][k] + min_cost_path_j[k])
            
            # Calculate the potential saving by inserting the edge (i, j)
            saving = min(min_cost_path_i[j], min_cost_path_j[i]) - distance_matrix[i][j]
            
            # Set the heuristic value to be the absolute value of the saving
            heuristic_matrix[i][j] = abs(saving)
    
    return heuristic_matrix

import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert distance_matrix to adjacency matrix
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate shortest path lengths
    shortest_paths = nx.all_pairs_shortest_path_length(G)
    
    # Calculate edge betweenness
    edge_betweenness = nx.edge_betweenness_centrality(G, weight='weight')  # Assuming 'weight' is the original distance
    
    # Adaptive decay function
    # Simplified version: exponentially decreases with distance
    decay = 2 ** (G.number_of_nodes() - 1 - G.number_of_edges() / 2)
    
    # Combine all indicators
    heuristics_matrix = (
        (shortest_paths[u][v] + 1) * edge_betweenness[u, v] * decay
        for u, v in G.edges()
    )
    
    # Normalize heuristics values to a reasonable range
    return [min(x) for x in heuristics_matrix]

import numpy as np
def density_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the number of edges for each node
    num_edges_per_node = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)

    # Density of each node: edges per node / total edges
    density_per_node = num_edges_per_node / distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Density of the entire network: average node density
    avg_density = np.mean(density_per_node)

    # Heuristic score: penalize edges for nodes with high density
    heuristics = distance_matrix * (avg_density - density_per_node)
    
    return heuristics

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate cosine similarity between each pair of nodes
    cosine_similarities = np.dot(distance_matrix, distance_matrix.T) / (np.linalg.norm(distance_matrix, axis=0) * np.linalg.norm(distance_matrix, axis=1)).reshape(*distance_matrix.shape, distance_matrix.shape[0])
    
    # Combine cosine similarity with original distances
    heuristics_matrix = np.minimum(distance_matrix, cosine_similarities)
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_from_dense
from scipy.spatial.distance import pdist, squareform
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Create a graph from the distance matrix
    graph = squareform(pdist(distance_matrix, 'premac'))
    g = csgraph_from_dense(graph)

    # Calculate betweenness centrality for each node
    betw_centrality = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    for _ in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        betweenness, _ = scipy.spatial.distance.pdist_betweenness(g, distance_matrix)
        betw_centrality += betweenness

    # Normalize betweenness centrality values between 0 and 1
    betw_centrality = betw_centrality / betw_centrality.max()

    # Create a new matrix where each entry represents the heuristic score for including an edge
    heuristics_matrix = np.outer(betw_centrality, betw_centrality)

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the matrix is square and symmetric
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    assert n == distance_matrix.shape[0], "Matrix must be square"
    assert np.allclose(distance_matrix, distance_matrix.T), "Matrix must be symmetric"

    # Compute the Moore-Penrose inverse
    try:
        inverted_matrix = np.linalg.pinv(distance_matrix)
    except np.linalg.LinAlgError:
        # If the matrix is singular, return a large value (e.g., distance_matrix.max() + 1)
        return distance_matrix.max() + 1



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)  # number of nodes
    # Step 1: Simple Local Heuristic (same as the given one)
    local_heuristic = distance_matrix
    
    # Step 2: Global Neighborhood-aware Heuristic
    # We'll use a combination of the minimum and average distance to neighboring nodes
    # Compute the sum of all distances, and then divide by the number of neighbors
    total_distance = sum(sum(distance_matrix))
    num_neighbors = 2*n - 2  # for fully connected graph
    
    global_heuristic = total_distance / num_neighbors
    
    # Combine the two heuristics into a single score matrix
    combined_heuristic = (local_heuristic, global_heuristic)
    
    return combined_heuristic



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import laplacian
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance_matrix into a undirected graph (adjacency matrix)
    graph = np.abs(distance_matrix - distance_matrix.T)  # Use the Frobenius norm for symmetric matrix

    # Compute the degree centrality using Laplacian matrix
    # Laplacian matrix is related to the graph's conductance
    laplacian_matrix = laplacian(csgraph=csgraph.binarize(graph))
    degrees = np.array(np.sum(graph, axis=0)).reshape(-1)
    eigenvectors, _ = np.linalg.eig(laplacian_matrix.tocsc())
    centrality = np.array(eigenvectors).real[0] / np.sqrt(degrees)

    # Normalize centrality values to a range of 0 to 1
    centrality = (centrality - np.min(centrality)) / (np.max(centrality) - np.min(centrality))

    # Add a small constant to avoid division by zero
    centrality += 1e-9

    # Return the centrality matrix
    return centrality

    # Take absolute values to ignore direction (same as considering edge weights)
    abs_differences = np.abs(differences)
    # Sum these differences for each node (edge), giving higher values to those with larger discrepancies
    heuristic_values = abs_differences.sum(axis=1)

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import connected_components, shortest_path
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Calculate the shortest path between each pair of nodes
    distances = shortest_path(distance_matrix, directed=False)
    
    # Step 2: Calculate the node degrees (local connectivity)
    degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)  # sum of each row (degrees of the connected nodes)
    
    # Step 3: Calculate the product of shortest paths for each pair (global connectivity)
    product_shortest_paths = np.prod(distances, axis=1)
    
    # Step 4: Combine local and global connectivity
    heuristic_matrix = degrees * product_shortest_paths
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Estimate the "ease" of integration for each edge
    ease_of_integration = 1.0 / distance_matrix

    # Step 2: Introduce a heuristic based on the distances between source and destination
    # We'll use a simple Manhattan distance as our heuristic
    def manhattan_distance(row, col):
        return abs(row[0] - col[0]) + abs(row[1] - col[1])

    # Apply the heuristic to each edge
    heuristic_scores = np.vectorize(manhattan_distance)(distance_matrix, np.arange(distance_matrix.shape[0])).T

    # Combine the ease of integration and heuristic scores
    combined_score = ease_of_integration * heuristic_scores

    return combined_score

            third_node = j
            for k in range(i+1, n):
                if distance_matrix[i][j] > distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j]:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] += 1
                    heuristic_matrix[j][i] += 1
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def cheapest_insertion(distance_matrix):
    # Get the number of nodes (vertices) in the graph
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Initialize variables
    parent = np.zeros(n, dtype=int)
    rank = np.zeros(n, dtype=int)
    min_edge_weight = float('inf')
    
    def find(x):
        if parent[x]!= x:
            parent[x] = find(parent[x])
        return parent[x]

    def union(x, y):
        root_x = find(x)
        root_y = find(y)
        
        if root_x == root_y:
            return
        
        if rank[root_x] > rank[root_y]:
            parent[root_y] = root_x
        elif rank[root_x] < rank[root_y]:
            parent[root_x] = root_y
        else:
            parent[root_y] = root_x
            rank[root_x] += 1
        
        min_edge_weight = min(min_edge_weight, distance_matrix[find(x), find(y)])
    
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j] < min_edge_weight:
                union(i, j)
    
    # Create the result matrix
    heuristic_matrix = np.full_like(distance_matrix, min_edge_weight)
    return heuristic_matrix
```

The cheapest_insertion() function first builds a minimum spanning tree using Kruskal's algorithm. This tree's total edge weight is the cheapest possible sum of weights for a connected, acyclic subgraph. The function then returns a new distance matrix where each element represents the minimum total weight edge (not forming a cycle) to add to the MST for each edge.

This function should perform better than the initial two functions by providing a more realistic estimate of how desirable or undesirable each edge is to include in the optimal solution.
