# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    # Calculate the direct cost to include each edge
    heuristic_matrix += distance_matrix  # Direct cost of including an edge
    
    # Introduce a factor to consider the adjacency and mutual distance
    adjacency_cost = np.minimum(distance_matrix[:, np.newaxis], distance_matrix[np.newaxis, :])
    heuristic_matrix += (adjacency_cost * np.diag(np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)))
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Step 1: Identify the largest connected component in the graph
    def largest_component(matrix):
        n = len(matrix)
        visited = [False] * n
        component_size = 0
        for i in range(n):
            if not visited[i]:
                stack = [i]
                visited[i] = True
                component_size += 1
                while stack:
                    node = stack.pop()
                    for neighbor in range(n):
                        if matrix[node][neighbor]!= float('inf') and not visited[neighbor]:
                            visited[neighbor] = True
                            stack.append(neighbor)
        return component_size

    # Step 2: Assign a penalty proportional to the number of edges in the largest connected component
    component_size = largest_component(distance_matrix)
    penalized_matrix = (distance_matrix + (n - component_size)) / n

    # Step 3: Assign a higher penalty for edges within the largest connected component
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if distance_matrix[i][j]!= float('inf'):
                if i in penalized_matrix[i] or j in penalized_matrix[j]:
                    penalized_matrix[i][j] += 1.5
                else:
                    penalized_matrix[i][j] += 1

    return penalized_matrix

import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    k = int(distance_matrix.shape[0] * 0.5)  # number of edges to consider

    # Calculate shortest path lengths
    shortest_paths = nx.all_pairs_shortest_path_length(G, k=k)

    # Calculate closeness centrality and betweenness centrality
    closeness = nx.closeness_centrality(G)
    betweenness = nx.betweenness_centrality(G)

    # Combine heuristics: average shortest path length, weighted by closeness and betweenness
    heuristic_matrix = (shortest_paths[0] + shortest_paths[1]) / 2.0
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = (closeness[i] + betweenness[i]) * shortest_paths[0][i][j] / (closeness[j] + betweenness[j])

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
def get_k_nearest_neighbors(distance_matrix, k):
    # Neighbors indices for each point
    neighbors = np.argpartition(distance_matrix, k, axis=1)[:, 1:k+1]
    # Average distances to these neighbors
    avg_distances = np.mean(distance_matrix[np.arange(distance_matrix.shape[0]), neighbors], axis=1)
    return avg_distances

import numpy as np
def relaxation_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the inverse of each element in the distance matrix
    inv_distances = 1 / distance_matrix
    
    # Apply softmax to get the probabilities
    sum_inv_distances = np.sum(inv_distances, axis=0)
    exp_inv_distances = np.exp(inv_distances - sum_inv_distances[:, np.newaxis])
    probs = exp_inv_distances / np.sum(exp_inv_distances, axis=0)
    
    # The resulting matrix now represents the undesirability of including each edge
    return probs



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute the sum of diagonal elements
    diagonal_sum = sum(distance_matrix[i][i] for i in range(len(distance_matrix)))
    
    # Compute the sum of the absolute differences from the diagonal
    sum_diff = sum(abs(distance_matrix[i][i] - distance_matrix[i][j]) for i in range(len(distance_matrix)) for j in range(len(distance_matrix)) if i!= j)
    
    # Normalize by dividing the sum by the diagonal sum
    return [sum_diff / diagonal_sum if distance_matrix[i][j] < diagonal_matrix[i][i] for i in range(len(distance_matrix)) for j in range(len(distance_matrix))]



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
    from scipy.optimize import linear_sum_assignment
    from collections import defaultdict
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np
    from scipy.optimize import linear_sum_assignment
    from collections import defaultdict

    # Calculate the number of edges in the graph
    num_edges = np.sum(distance_matrix) // 2
    
    # Create a graph representation using adjacency matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    graph = np.zeros((n, n), dtype=bool)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i, n):
            if distance_matrix[i][j]!= 0:
                graph[i][j] = graph[j][i] = True
    
    # Function to calculate local degree for each node
    def local_degree(graph, i):
        return sum(graph[i, j] for j in range(n) if graph[i, j])
    
    # Calculate the local degree of each node and the average degree
    local_degrees = [local_degree(graph, i) for i in range(n)]
    avg_degree = sum(local_degrees) / n
    
    # Function to calculate network flow heuristic score
    def network_flow_heuristic(graph, avg_degree):
        n = len(graph)
        M = np.zeros((n, n), dtype=bool)
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(i, n):
                if graph[i][j]:
                    M[i, j] = 1
        
        row_sums = np.sum(M, axis=1)
        col_sums = np.sum(M, axis=0)
        
        # Min-cost flow problem
        row_costs = row_sums
        col_costs = col_sums - avg_degree
        
        # Solve the minimum-cost flow problem
        _, _, _, _ = linear_sum_assignment(M, maximize=False)
        
        # The heuristic score is the total cost of the minimum-cost flow
        return sum(row_costs[i] + col_costs[i] for i in range(n))
    
    return network_flow_heuristic(graph, avg_degree)



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the minimum edge priority queue
    min_heap = [(0, 0)]  # (weight, node)
    # Initialize the visited set and parent set
    visited = set()
    parent = {i: None for i in range(n)}

    while min_heap:
        weight, u = heapq.heappop(min_heap)

        # If the node is already visited, skip it
        if u in visited:
            continue

        # Add the node to the visited set
        visited.add(u)

        # Iterate over neighboring nodes
        for v in range(n):
            if distance_matrix[u][v]!= 0 and v not in visited:
                # Calculate the new edge weight
                new_weight = weight + distance_matrix[u][v]
                
                # If this is a lighter edge to node v or if v is already in the tree
                if new_weight < distance_matrix[parent[u]][v] or v not in parent:
                    parent[v] = u
                    heapq.heappush(min_heap, (new_weight, v))

    # The result is a matrix of the lowest edge weights in the MST, i.e., the heuristic
    return [min(distance_matrix[u][v], distance_matrix[parent[u]][v]) for u in range(n) for v in range(n) if parent[u] == v]



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Check if matrix is square (as it would be for a graph's adjacency matrix)
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    if not all(distance_matrix[i][j] == distance_matrix[j][i] for i in range(n) for j in range(i+1, n)):
        raise ValueError("Distance matrix must be square.")
    
    # Apply Reverse Distance Weighting heuristic
    weighted_matrix = [[n - distance_matrix[i][j] for j in range(n)] for i in range(n)]
    
    return weighted_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import minimum_spanning_tree
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Calculate initial edge costs (distance_matrix)
    edge_costs = np.triu(distance_matrix, k=1)
    
    # Compute Minimum Spanning Tree (MST)
    MST_costs = minimum_spanning_tree(csgraph=edge_costs)
    
    # Compute distance from each node to MST (these are potential edge costs)
    potential_edge_costs = edge_costs - MST_costs
    
    # Adjust potential costs based on similarity to MST edges
    # In TSP, edges closer to MST tend to be less undesirable
    adjusted_costs = potential_edge_costs / np.maximum(MST_costs, 1)
    
    return adjusted_costs



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize the improved matrix with the original matrix
    improved = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Iterate over all pairs of nodes
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # Find the minimum cost edge that includes both i and j
            min_cost = float('inf')
            improved_edge = (None, None)
            for k in range(n):
                if k not in (i, j):
                    cost = distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[k][j] + distance_matrix[i][k]
                    if cost < min_cost:
                        min_cost = cost
                        improved_edge = (i, j, k)
            
            # If the minimum cost edge can be improved, update it
            if improved_edge[2] is not None:
                improved[i][j] = min(improved[i][j], distance_matrix[i][j] + distance_matrix[i][improved_edge[2]] + distance_matrix[improved_edge[2]][j])
                improved[j][i] = improved[i][j]
    
    return improved

from scipy.sparse.csgraph import betweenness_centrality
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Compute betweenness centrality
    betweenness = betweenness_centrality(csgraph=distance_matrix, directed=False)
    
    # Normalize betweenness values between 0 and 1
    betweenness_normalized = (betweenness - min(betweenness)) / (max(betweenness) - min(betweenness))
    
    # Create a matrix with the same shape as the distance matrix, filled with normalized betweenness values
    heuristics_matrix = np.array(betweenness_normalized).reshape(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Number of cities
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the inverse distance as the initial heuristic
    heuristic_matrix = -1 * np.diag(1 / distance_matrix)

    # Additional nearest neighbor heuristic
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = min(distance_matrix[i, j], heuristic_matrix[i, :].min(), heuristic_matrix[:, j].min())

    return heuristic_matrix

import numpy as np
from scipy.optimize import linear_sum_assignment
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Convert the distance matrix to a cost matrix where larger values imply undesirability
    cost_matrix = 1 / (1 + distance_matrix)  # 1/distance for minimization
    
    # Add a small constant to the diagonal for stability
    cost_matrix[np.diag_indices(n)] += 1e-9
    
    # Solve the assignment problem to get the optimal assignment
    _, assignment = linear_sum_assignment(cost_matrix)
    
    # Create a new matrix where each value represents the cost of including the corresponding edge
    heuristics_matrix = np.take(cost_matrix, assignment)
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    centrality = np.zeros((n, n))
    
    # Calculate average distances from each node to all other nodes
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                centrality[i, j] = np.mean(distance_matrix[i, :j] + distance_matrix[j, :i])

    # Calculate weighted centrality
    weighted_centrality = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if distance_matrix[i, j] > 0:  # Assuming zero distance means no connection
                weighted_centrality[i, j] = centrality[i, j] / distance_matrix[i, j]

    # The heuristics matrix is the negative of weighted centrality
    heuristics_matrix = -weighted_centrality

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, iterations=100):
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same dimensions as the distance matrix
    heuristic_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()
    
    # Define initial weight for edges (higher weight indicates less congestion)
    initial_weight = 1
    
    # Run the AIMD algorithm for a specified number of iterations
    for _ in range(iterations):
        # For each edge
        for i in range(len(distance_matrix)):
            for j in range(len(distance_matrix[i])):
                # Compute the current congestion score
                current_score = heuristic_matrix[i][j] / distance_matrix[i][j]
                
                # Apply AIMD update rule
                if current_score > 1:
                    # Reduce the congestion for less congested edges
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] *= 0.99
                elif current_score < 1:
                    # Increase the congestion for more congested edges
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] *= 1.01
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def branch_and_bound(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    # Initialize the resulting matrix with zeros
    branch_bound_scores = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    def branch_bound(curr_node, low, high, min_cost):
        nonlocal branch_bound_scores
        
        # If we've reached the lowest node (all edges have been considered), update the min_cost
        if low == high:
            branch_bound_scores[curr_node] = min_cost
            return

        # Explore branches
        for i in range(low, high):
            if distance_matrix[curr_node][i] < min_cost:
                # Include this edge in the MST
                branch_bound(i, low, i+1, min_cost + distance_matrix[curr_node][i])
        
        # Exclude the current node (edge) from the MST
        branch_bound(curr_node, i+1, high, min_cost)

    # Start the branch-and-bound algorithm from the first node
    branch_bound(0, 0, n, 0)
    return branch_bound_scores
```

This function implements a depth-first search strategy, where each node represents a potential solution (a subset of edges) and the edges between nodes represent the addition or exclusion of edges in the MST. At each step, it considers two alternatives: including the current edge in the MST and excluding it. The algorithm uses a "min_cost" to keep track of the lowest total cost found so far.

The main advantage of this method over the simple distance matrix multiplication is that it considers all possible subsets of edges and their combinations, providing a more comprehensive analysis of the undesirability of including each edge.

Note that this function can be computationally expensive for large matrices due to its nature of exploring all possible combinations, and it might not provide a polynomial-time solution. However, it should generally outperform the simple distance matrix multiplication for moderate-sized problems.

To evaluate the performance of this function, you would need to use a suitably-sized distance matrix and compare the achieved score with those from the simpler versions. Adjustments might be necessary based on your specific use case and the characteristics of your data.



# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_weights, adjacency_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((n, n))

    # Edge Frequency
    edge_freq = (adjacency_matrix > 0).sum(axis=1) / n

    # Position-based Influence
    pos_influence = (np.arange(n) - np.arange(n).reshape(n, 1)).abs()

    # Weight-based Importance
    weight_importance = edge_weights / np.sum(edge_weights, axis=1).reshape(n, 1)

    # Combine the three factors
    heuristic_matrix = distance_matrix * edge_freq * pos_influence * weight_importance

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the input is a numpy array for consistent indexing
    distance_matrix = np.array(distance_matrix)
    
    # Compute a weighted average of the original distance matrix
    avg_distance = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=0)
    
    # Incorporate edge weights into the heuristic
    edge_weights = distance_matrix.sum(axis=1)
    weighted_avg = (edge_weights * avg_distance) / distance_matrix.sum()
    
    # Add network density factor: normalize by total number of edges
    num_edges = distance_matrix.shape[0] * distance_matrix.shape[1]
    density = num_edges / distance_matrix.size
    
    # Incorporate random walk probability based on edge weights
    walk_probs = edge_weights / edge_weights.sum()
    
    # Combine factors to form the heuristic score matrix
    heuristic_scores = 1 / (1 + np.exp(-weighted_avg) * np.exp(-density) * np.prod(walk_probs))
    
    return heuristic_scores

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = len(distance_matrix)
    flow_matrix = [[(distance_matrix[i][j] ** 2) / (i * j) for j in range(num_nodes)] for i in range(num_nodes)]
    
    # Adjust the flow matrix based on a simple heuristic:
    # 1. Smaller distances are assigned lower flow values to prioritize shorter paths.
    # 2. Higher degree nodes (nodes with more connections) are given a penalty to discourage a single bottleneck.
    for node in range(num_nodes):
        degree_penalty = 1 / (node + 1)  # This penalty increases linearly with the node's degree.
        for neighbor in range(num_nodes):
            if node!= neighbor:
                flow_matrix[node][neighbor] *= degree_penalty
    
    return flow_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    adj_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

    # We'll use Kruskal's algorithm to calculate edge priorities.
    # First, sort the edges (considering only distinct distances).
    unique_distances = sorted(set(distance_matrix.flatten()))
    edge_indices = [i for i, d in enumerate(distance_matrix) if d in unique_distances]

    # Initialize the priority queue (min-heap) and the set to keep track of edges used.
    priority_queue = [(distance_matrix[i][j], i, j) for i, j in zip(*[iter(edge_indices)]*2) if i < j]
    used_edges = set()

    while priority_queue:
        _, i, j = heapq.heappop(priority_queue)

        # If either vertex is already connected, skip it.
        if i in used_edges or j in used_edges:
            continue
        used_edges.add(i)
        used_edges.add(j)
        adj_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
        adj_matrix[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j]  # Symmetric matrix

    return adj_matrix

import numpy as np
def bellman_ford(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    for _ in range(n):
        for u in range(n):
            for v in range(n):
                if distance_matrix[u][v] > distance_matrix[u][v] + distance_matrix[v][u]:
                    distance_matrix[u][v] = distance_matrix[u][v] + distance_matrix[v][u]
    return distance_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the 2D distance matrix to a sparse CSR (Compressed Sparse Row) format for efficient computations
    distance_matrix = csr_matrix(distance_matrix)
    
    # Step 1: Local community detection
    # Use Louvain method for modularity optimization
    from community import community_louvain
    modularity, communities = community_louvain.best_partition(distance_matrix)
    
    # Create a new distance matrix for communities, where edges within a community have smaller weight
    community_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i, comm in enumerate(communities):
        community_matrix[np.ix_(comm, comm)] = 1 - distance_matrix[np.ix_(comm, comm)]
    
    # Step 2: Global community detection and removal
    # Find the largest connected component in the community graph
    largest_component = csgraph_largest_component(distance_matrix)
    
    # Create a new distance matrix for the largest component
    largest_component_matrix = largest_component.toarray()
    
    # Step 3: Greedy approximation
    # Assume that removing an edge has cost 'weight'
    weight = 1.0  # You can adjust this to better fit your problem

    # Initialize the heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(i + 1, distance_matrix.shape[0]):
            # If the edge is in the largest component
            if distance_matrix[i, j] in largest_component_matrix[largest_component_matrix == 1, largest_component_matrix == 1]:
                # If the nodes belong to the same community
                if comm_i == comm_j:
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] = weight
                # If they belong to different communities, consider the cost of the community split
                else:
                    heuristics_matrix[i, j] = weight * (1 - community_matrix[i, comm_i] * community_matrix[j, comm_j])
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate average distance for importance weight
    avg_distance = np.mean(distance_matrix)
    distance_importance = avg_distance * 2  # heuristically doubling the importance of larger distances

    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Calculate neighbor density
    neighbor_density = np.zeros_shape(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            neighbors = distance_matrix[i][max(0, i-1):i] + distance_matrix[i][max(0, i+1):i+2]
            neighbor_density[i][j] = sum(neighbors < distance_matrix[i, j]) / (2*distance_matrix.shape[0] - 1)

    # Apply importance and neighbor density to generate heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix + distance_importance * neighbor_density

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the number of vertices (or nodes)
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # The edge weights in our new heuristic will be the pairwise distances, but with a twist:
    # we'll subtract the smallest distance for each vertex to penalize edges connecting
    # to those vertices. This is a basic form of cost-based edge selection.
    # We use a min-heap to efficiently select the smallest unconnected vertex.
    
    # Initialize an empty min-heap and the result matrix
    min_heap, result = [], [[float('inf')]*n for _ in range(n)]
    
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            # For each edge (i,j), add it to the heap and update the result matrix
            heapq.heappush(min_heap, (distance_matrix[i][j], i, j))
            
            # Update the result matrix for (i,j)
            result[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
    
    # Process the heap to fill in the result matrix
    while min_heap:
        # Pop the smallest edge from the heap
        w, u, v = heapq.heappop(min_heap)
        
        # Skip if the vertices (u,v) are already connected
        if result[u][v] < float('inf'):
            continue
        
        # Include the edge in the MST, updating the result matrix
        result[u][v] = w
        result[v][u] = w
        
        # Update the min-heap with the remaining unconnected neighbors of u
        for neighbor in range(n):
            if result[u][neighbor] == float('inf'):
                heapq.heappush(min_heap, (result[u][neighbor], u, neighbor))
    
    return result



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    heuristic_matrix = [[0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Calculating the heuristic score for each node (except source node)
    for i in range(1, n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i == j:  # No-self-loop
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
            else:
                heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j] + min(heuristic_matrix[i][k] for k in range(n) if k!= j)  # Min-path sum heuristic
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    rows, cols = distance_matrix.shape
    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Step 1: Assign negative weights to edges based on proximity
    for i in range(rows):
        for j in range(cols):
            if i!= j:
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] - max(distance_matrix[i, k] for k in range(cols) if k!= j)

    # Step 2: Assign higher negative values to edges connecting disconnected components
    distances = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1)  # Minimum distance from node i
    heuristic_matrix[distances > np.max(distances)] = -np.inf

    # Step 3: Distance-based heuristics (assuming'shortest_distance' function returns the minimum distance from node i to all other nodes)
    shortest_distance = np.minimum.reduce([np.min(distance_matrix[i, :], axis=0) for i in range(rows)])
    heuristic_matrix += distance_matrix - shortest_distance[:, np.newaxis] - shortest_distance[np.newaxis, :]

    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000
import heapq
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Initialize the priority queue and visited set
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    pq = [(0, 0)]  # (current_distance, current_node)
    visited = set()

    # Floyd-Warshall to compute all pair shortest paths
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                # Update distance if a shorter path is found
                distance_matrix[i][j] = min(distance_matrix[i][j], distance_matrix[i][k] + distance_matrix[k][j])
    
    # Compute heuristic values for each edge
    heuristics_matrix = [[0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                # Dijkstra's algorithm to estimate distance from node i to all nodes
                dist_to_i = [float('inf')] * n
                dist_to_i[i] = 0
                heapq.heappush(pq, (0, i))

                while pq:
                    current_distance, current_node = heapq.heappop(pq)
                    if current_node in visited:
                        continue
                    visited.add(current_node)

                    for neighbor, edge_weight in enumerate(distance_matrix[current_node]):
                        if neighbor not in visited:
                            new_distance = dist_to_i[current_node] + edge_weight
                            if new_distance < dist_to_neighbor:
                                dist_to_neighbor = new_distance
                                heapq.heappush(pq, (dist_to_neighbor, neighbor))

                heuristics_matrix[i][j] = dist_to_i[j]  # Estimated distance from i to j

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristics_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Update heuristics for each node
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(num_nodes):
            # Avoid diagonal elements
            if i == j:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = 0
            else:
                heuristics_matrix[i, j] = sum(distance_matrix[i, k] + distance_matrix[k, j] for k in range(num_nodes))

    # Normalize to have values between 0 and 1
    max_distance = np.max(heuristics_matrix)
    heuristics_matrix = heuristics_matrix / max_distance

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def weighted_heuristics(distance_matrix, weights=None):
    """
    This function calculates a new heuristic matrix based on the input distance_matrix,
    applying a weighted distance approach and a penalty for high-weight edges.
    The weights can be provided as a separate array of the same shape as the distance_matrix.
    """
    if weights is None:
        # If weights are not provided, assign equal weights to all edges
        weights = np.ones_like(distance_matrix)
    
    # Apply a penalty for high-weight edges
    penalty = 10  # Adjust this value according to the desired penalty strength
    high_weight_penalty = np.where(weights > 0.5, penalty, 0)
    weighted_distance = distance_matrix * weights
    heuristic_matrix = weighted_distance + high_weight_penalty
    
    return heuristic_matrix

    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np
    
    # Edge impact score calculation
    N = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    for i in range(N):
        for j in range(i+1, N):
            # We'll consider the sum of distances from the current vertex to all others
            edge_sum = np.sum(distance_matrix[i]) + np.sum(distance_matrix[j])
            # We'll also consider the position of the edge in the matrix, more central edges being potentially more desirable
            position_score = i + j - N // 2
            # We'll use the Manhattan distance as a rough measure of the edge's'spread'
            edge_spread = np.abs(distance_matrix[i] - distance_matrix[j])
            
            # Combine these factors
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = heuristic_matrix[j, i] = edge_sum + position_score + edge_spread
            
    return heuristic_matrix

# Score: -20000
    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Calculate the shortest path from each node to all others using Dijkstra's algorithm
    def dijkstra(matrix):
        n = matrix.shape[0]
        distances = np.copy(matrix)
        visited = np.zeros(n, dtype=bool)
        for _ in range(n):
            min_distance = np.inf
            u = -1
            for v in range(n):
                if not visited[v] and distances[v] < min_distance:
                    min_distance = distances[v]
                    u = v
            visited[u] = True
            for v in range(n):
                if visited[v] and distances[v] > distances[u] + matrix[u, v]:
                    distances[v] = distances[u] + matrix[u, v]
        return distances

    # Calculate the distance impact factor (DIF) for each edge
    DIF = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            DIF[i, j] = distance_matrix[i, j] / np.sum(dijkstra(distance_matrix))

    return DIF

def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    row_sums = sum(distance_matrix, [])
    
    # Create a new matrix of the same shape with the same negative values as row sums
    heuristics_matrix = [[-row_sum for _ in range(len(distance_matrix[0]))] for row_sum in row_sums]
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]

    # Shortest Path Heuristic
    shortest_paths = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    shortest_paths_matrix = np.repeat(shortest_paths[:, np.newaxis], n, axis=1)
    
    # Betweenness Centrality
    betweenness = np.zeros((n, n))
    for node in range(n):
        shortest_paths_to_node = np.min(distance_matrix, axis=0)
        path_counts = np.repeat(distance_matrix[node, np.arange(n)], distance_matrix[np.arange(n), node], axis=1)
        path_counts[path_counts == 0] = 1  # Avoid division by zero
        betweens_sum = np.sum(path_counts, axis=0) / np.sum(distance_matrix!= 0, axis=0)
        betweenness += distance_matrix[node, np.arange(n)] * (betweens_sum - distance_matrix[node, np.arange(n)] / np.sum(distance_matrix!= 0))

    # Closeness Centrality
    closeness = np.zeros((n, n))
    for node in range(n):
        distances = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
        closeness[node] = np.sum(1 / distances, axis=0)

    # Combine heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = shortest_paths_matrix + betweenness + closeness

    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the number of connections (degrees) for each node
    degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)

    # Normalize by the total number of nodes
    normalized_degrees = degrees / np.sum(degrees)

    # Calculate a new heuristic value based on normalized degrees
    heuristics_matrix = 1 / normalized_degrees

    # To avoid numerical instability, clamp values between 0 and 1
    heuristics_matrix = np.clip(heuristics_matrix, 0, 1)

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Ensure the distance matrix is symmetric
    distance_matrix = np.maximum(distance_matrix, distance_matrix.T)
    
    # Calculate the all-pairs shortest paths using Floyd-Warshall
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    all_pairs_shortest_paths = distance_matrix
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                all_pairs_shortest_paths[i, j] = min(all_pairs_shortest_paths[i, j], 
                                                   all_pairs_shortest_paths[i, k] + 
                                                   all_pairs_shortest_paths[k, j])
    
    # Create a new matrix of the same shape where each entry represents the "undesirability" of the corresponding edge
    undesirability_matrix = np.triu(all_pairs_shortest_paths, k=1)
    
    return undesirability_matrix

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    
    # Calculate the cost-to-come for each edge
    cost_to_come = np.inf * np.ones((num_nodes, num_nodes))
    for u in range(num_nodes):
        for v in range(num_nodes):
            if u == v:
                cost_to_come[u, v] = 0  # No cost to come back to the same node
            else:
                for w in range(num_nodes):
                    cost_to_come[u, v] = min(cost_to_come[u, v], distance_matrix[u, w] + distance_matrix[w, v])
    
    # Normalize cost-to-come to get the heuristic values
    for u in range(num_nodes):
        for v in range(num_nodes):
            if u!= v:
                cost_to_come[u, v] /= (num_nodes - 1)  # Normalize by number of nodes - 1
    
    return cost_to_come



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def weighted_centrality(distance_matrix):
    # Get dimensions of the distance matrix
    num_nodes, _ = distance_matrix.shape
    
    # Initialize a new matrix with the same shape
    heuristics_matrix = np.copy(distance_matrix)
    
    # Iterate over each node
    for node in range(num_nodes):
        # Get neighbors of the current node
        neighbors_indices = np.where(distance_matrix[node]!= np.inf)[0]
        
        # Calculate the sum of distances to all neighbors
        distances_to_neighbors = np.sum(distance_matrix[node, neighbors_indices], axis=0)
        
        # Assign a heuristic score
        heuristics_matrix[node, neighbors_indices] = 1 / distances_to_neighbors  # Use reciprocal of distance as a heuristic
    
    return heuristics_matrix



# Score: -20000

def effective_distance_heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_vertices = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    effective_distances = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    
    for i in range(num_vertices):
        # Sum up the minimum distance to all neighboring vertices
        neighbor_distances = np.min(distance_matrix[i, np.nonzero(distance_matrix[i, :]!= np.inf)], axis=1)
        effective_distances[i, :] = np.sum(neighbor_distances)
    
    return effective_distances



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix, edge_attributes):
    # Define a multiplier for each attribute that indicates its 'undesirability'
    attribute_multipliers = {
        'attribute1': 1.5,
        'attribute2': 2,
        'attribute3': 1  # Assume some attributes are less undesirable
    }

    num_edges = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros((num_edges, num_edges))

    for i in range(num_edges):
        for j in range(i, num_edges):
            # Compute the distance between the two nodes
            dist = distance_matrix[i, j]

            # Compute a negative score based on edge attributes
            negative_score = sum(edge_attributes[i][attr] * attr_multiplier for attr, attr_multiplier in attribute_multipliers.items() if attr in edge_attributes[i])

            # Use the minimum of the distance and negative score as the heuristic value
            heuristic_matrix[i, j] = min(dist, negative_score)
            heuristic_matrix[j, i] = heuristic_matrix[i, j]  # Symmetry assumption

    return heuristic_matrix

def heuristics(distance_matrix):

    # A heuristic risk score is computed based on the inverse of the square of distance
    # This encourages higher-distance edges as they are less critical.

    return risk_scores



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Define a connection weight function
    def connection_weight(node, connections):
        return 1 / (np.sum(np.abs(node - connections)) + 1)
    
    # Create a mask for connections of each node
    node_connections = np.argsort(distance_matrix, axis=1)[:,1:]
    
    # Calculate the connection weight for each edge
    weight_matrix = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in node_connections[i]:
            weight_matrix[i,j] = connection_weight(i, j)
    
    # Calculate the "distance-based cost" for each edge
    # This is a simple form that increases with distance and decreases with weight
    distance_based_cost = distance_matrix + weight_matrix
    
    # Normalize to ensure it's a valid score matrix
    max_cost = np.max(distance_based_cost)
    if max_cost == 0:
        return distance_based_cost



# Score: -20000

def floyd_warshall(distance_matrix):
    # Initialize the graph as the input distance matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    graph = [[float('inf') for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

    # Each node is its own shortest path
    for i in range(n):
        graph[i][i] = 0

    # Fill in the graph with the shortest path values
    for k in range(n):
        for i in range(n):
            for j in range(n):
                graph[i][j] = min(graph[i][j], graph[i][k] + graph[k][j])

    return graph



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Convert the distance matrix into a graph
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    graph = np.zeros((n, n))

    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i, n):
            graph[i][j] = graph[j][i] = distance_matrix[i][j]

    # Weighted Shortest Path Heuristic
    def wsp(start, end):
        visited = np.zeros(n, dtype=bool)
        path_length = np.full(n, np.inf)
        path_length[start] = 0

        while np.any(visited!= np.union1d(visited, np.where(path_length!= np.inf)[0])):
            min_length_vertex = np.argmin(path_length)
            visited[min_length_vertex] = True

            for neighbor in range(n):
                if graph[min_length_vertex][neighbor]!= np.inf and not visited[neighbor]:
                    new_length = path_length[min_length_vertex] + graph[min_length_vertex][neighbor]
                    if new_length < path_length[neighbor]:
                        path_length[neighbor] = new_length

    # Compute and store the number of edges in the shortest path
    heuristic_scores = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)
    for i in range(n):
        wsp(i, i)  # path length is 0 for a vertex
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            wsp(i, j)
            heuristic_scores[i][j] = path_length[j] - 1  # subtract 1 to get number of edges in shortest path

    return heuristic_scores
```

This function first constructs a weighted graph from the distance matrix. Then, for each pair of vertices, it computes the shortest path (using a simple iterative approach) and counts the number of edges in this path. This should provide a better indicator of how undesirable it is to include each edge in a solution. The idea here is to incorporate a local perspective by considering shortest paths, and a global perspective by treating all edges equally (except for the self-loop).

Remember, "better" is context-dependent and relies heavily on the specific problem you're trying to solve. This is a generalized approach and might need further refinement for certain edge cases or problem constraints.



# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]  # number of nodes
    avg_dist = np.mean(distance_matrix, axis=0)  # average distance from each node
    path_counts = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)  # total number of paths from each node
    dand = np.mean(distance_matrix[np.arange(n), :] * np.arange(n).reshape(-1, 1), axis=1)  # DAND
    weighted_degree = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)  # weighted degree for each node

    # Combine these metrics into a single score matrix
    heuristics_matrix = (1 - avg_dist) * path_counts + (avg_dist - dand) * weighted_degree

    # Normalize the scores so they sum to 1
    heuristics_matrix /= np.sum(heuristics_matrix, axis=0)

    return heuristics_matrix

    import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    import numpy as np

    # Compute the degree of each node (number of connections)
    degrees = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)

    # Initialize the heuristic matrix with the same shape as the input
    heuristic_matrix = np.zeros_like(distance_matrix)

    # Assign lower heuristic values to edges between nodes with high degrees
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            if i < j:
                heuristic_matrix[i, j] = degrees[i] + degrees[j]  # High degree nodes' connections
                heuristic_matrix[j, i] = degrees[i] + degrees[j]  # Symmetry
    
    return heuristic_matrix

    # Calculate the total shortest path lengths
    total_path_length = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)

# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Get the shape of the input matrix
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    
    # Initialize heuristic matrix with zeros
    heuristic_matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    
    # Add a diagonal of ones to the heuristic matrix as a'shortcut'
    for i in range(n):
        heuristic_matrix[i][i] = distance_matrix[i][i]
    
    # Fill in'similarity' based heuristics
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                # Calculate the similarity to the diagonal element
                similarity = max(distance_matrix[i][k] for k in range(n) if k!= i)
                # If the diagonal element is the smallest, it's a potential shortcut
                if distance_matrix[i][j] > similarity:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] = similarity
                else:
                    heuristic_matrix[i][j] = distance_matrix[i][j]
    
    return heuristic_matrix



# Score: -20000

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    num_nodes = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    heuristics_matrix = distance_matrix.copy()

    # For each edge, calculate its proximity to its neighboring edges
    for i in range(num_nodes):
        for j in range(i+1, num_nodes):
            edge_weight = distance_matrix[i][j]
            for neighbor_i in range(num_nodes):
                for neighbor_j in range(neighbor_i+1, num_nodes):
                    if (i!= neighbor_i and j!= neighbor_j):
                        neighbor_weight = distance_matrix[neighbor_i][neighbor_j]
                        heuristics_matrix[i][j] += (edge_weight + neighbor_weight) / (2 * num_nodes - 1)
                        heuristics_matrix[j][i] = heuristics_matrix[i][j]  # symmetry across edges

    return heuristics_matrix

# Score: -20000
import numpy as np
from scipy.sparse.csgraph import csgraph_shortest_path
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    """
    Calculate edge-based heuristics based on shortest path lengths.
    A higher value indicates that the corresponding edge should be less likely to be included in the solution.
    
    Parameters:
    distance_matrix (numpy.ndarray): A square matrix representing the distance between each pair of nodes.
    
    Returns:
    numpy.ndarray: A matrix of the same shape as input, where each element is the heuristic value for the corresponding edge.
    """
    # Compute the shortest path lengths
    n = distance_matrix.shape[0]
    adj_matrix = csgraph_shortest_path(csgraph=distance_matrix, directed=True)
    
    # Create the heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = np.minimum(distance_matrix, adj_matrix)

    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Nodes and edges counts
    num_nodes, num_edges = distance_matrix.shape
    node_counts = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=1)
    edge_counts = np.sum(distance_matrix, axis=0)

    # Heuristic factors based on node and edge importance
    # Hypothetical factors, replace with actual or appropriate values
    node_importance = np.array([0.3, 0.2, 0.5])  # Example node importance scores
    edge_importance = np.array([0.5, 0.7, 0.8])  # Example edge importance scores

    # Heuristic values: absolute distance + node importance + edge importance
    heuristic_values = distance_matrix + (node_importance * node_counts) + (edge_importance * edge_counts)

    return heuristic_values

def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Total sum of all edge weights
    total_weight = sum(sum(row) for row in distance_matrix)

    # Calculate heuristics
    heuristics_matrix = [
        [dist * total_weight / (weight * len(row)) for weight, row in zip(distance_matrix[0], row)]
        for dist in distance_matrix
    ]
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    # Calculate the sum of the distance matrix
    total_distance = np.sum(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the number of connections
    num_connections = np.count_nonzero(distance_matrix)
    
    # Calculate the Weighted Connection Score (WCS)
    # WCS is the total distance divided by the number of connections
    # This will penalize frequently connected edges more
    wcs_matrix = total_distance / num_connections
    
    return wcs_matrix

import heapq
from collections import defaultdict
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    n = len(distance_matrix)
    # Initialize adjacency list
    graph = defaultdict(list)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i+1, n):
            graph[i].append((j, distance_matrix[i][j]))
            graph[j].append((i, distance_matrix[j][i]))

    # Calculate total outgoing degree
    total_outgoing_degrees = [sum(dist[1] for dist in graph[i]) for i in range(n)]

    # Initialize heuristics matrix
    heuristics_matrix = [[0.0 for _ in range(n)] for _ in range(n)]

    # Calculate heuristics
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(n):
            if i!= j:
                # Calculate weight based on normalized outgoing degrees and distance
                weight = (total_outgoing_degrees[i] + total_outgoing_degrees[j]) / 2.0 - (distance_matrix[i][j] / max(total_outgoing_degrees))
                heuristics_matrix[i][j] = weight
    
    return heuristics_matrix

import numpy as np
import networkx as nx
def heuristics(distance_matrix):
    G = nx.from_numpy_array(distance_matrix)
    # Calculate betweenness centrality
    betweenness_centrality = nx.betweenness_centrality(G)

    # Convert centrality values to heuristic scores
    heuristic_scores = np.zeros(distance_matrix.shape)
    for i in range(distance_matrix.shape[0]):
        for j in range(distance_matrix.shape[1]):
            heuristic_scores[i,j] = distance_matrix[i,j] + betweenness_centrality[i,j]

    return heuristic_scores
